Praying with Impurity When Unable to Remove It
Ruling on praying with najāsah when unable to remove it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying with najasah when removal is impossible and explain why no qada is required.

Core Idea
When removing impurity is impossible, prayer is valid without repetition – the Shari'ah does not burden beyond capacity.

This short ruling addresses a situation of genuine hardship: a person has najasah on their body or clothes but no water or other purifying liquid to remove it. The Hanafi school provides a clear concession based on the Quranic principle that Allah does not oblige a soul beyond its capacity. Understanding this ruling removes unnecessary anxiety and clarifies that necessity indeed overrides the normal condition of purity in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The person has najasah (impurity) on their body or clothing, and they cannot remove it because they lack water or any other purifying substance.
The inability must be genuine; if water is available nearby, the ruling differs.
2
Identify the ruling
The person should pray in that state; the prayer is valid and does not need to be repeated (qada) later.
This is a rukhsah (concession) specific to the situation of duress.
3
Identify the underlying principle
The Shari'ah does not burden a person beyond their capacity (Quran 2:286). Since removing the najasah is impossible, the obligation to purify is lifted.
This principle overrides the general requirement of taharah for prayer.
4
Confirm no qada
There is no need to repeat the prayer even if water becomes available later, because the prayer was valid under the given constraints.
This differs from the case where one deliberately neglects purification.
5
Note the concession status
The ruling is a rukhsah (concession), not an original ruling. It applies only when the barrier is genuine and beyond the person's control.
If the person could have removed the najasah but chose not to, the prayer is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[١٦٤ (٦) ومن لم يجد ما يزيل النجاسة صلى معها ولم يعد
کپڑے پر یا جسم پر نجاست لگی ہوئی ہے لیکن نجاست کو زائل کرنے کے لئے اور اس کو دھونے کے لئے اس کے پاس پانی یا بہنے والی چیز نہیں ہے تو وہ اس کپڑے میں اور اسی جسم کے ساتھ نماز پڑھ لے گا۔
اس کی طاقت میں اس سے زائد نہیں ہے اور شریعت طاقت سے زیادہ مکلف نہیں بناتی۔ اس لئے اس کی نماز جائز ہو جائے گی۔ لوٹانے کی ضرورت نہین ہوگی۔
[164] (6) Whoever does not find anything to remove the impurity, he should pray with it and not repeat. He has impurity on his clothes or body, but he has no water or liquid to remove the impurity, so he will pray in that cloth and with that body. He is not able to do more than that, and the Shari'ah does not burden beyond capacity. Therefore his prayer will be valid. There is no need to repeat.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This is a short ruling: if a person has impurity (najis) on their clothing or body and has no water or other purifying liquid, they should pray in that state and do not need to repeat the prayer later. The principle here is that the Shari'ah does not obligate what is beyond one's capacity. This is based on the Quranic principle 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.' The ruling is straightforward: the prayer is valid and does not require qada.

Key Terms
نجاسة (najasah): Ritual impurity on the body or clothes that prevents the validity of prayer unless removed.
إزالة (izalah): Removal of impurity, typically by washing with water or a purifying substance.
رفع الحرج (raf' al-haraj): Lifting of hardship, a key Shari'ah principle that concessions are granted when obligations become excessively difficult.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a person do if they have impurity on their clothes and no water to wash it?
A) Pray without the clothes
B) Pray with the impurity and not repeat
C) Wait until they find water
D) Repeat the prayer later when water is found

Key Takeaway
When removing najasah is not possible, the prayer is valid and need not be repeated because Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.

Praying Naked: Sitting with Gestures
Ruling on how to pray when no clothing is available

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who has no clothes to cover their 'awrah and explain why sitting with gestures is required.

Core Idea
When covering 'awrah is impossible, the obligation reduces to what is possible: sitting with gestures.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling for a person who has no clothing to cover their 'awrah during salah. The text specifies that such a person must pray sitting and make gestures for ruku and sujud. We will explore the evidence from the practice of the Companions and the rationale behind this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The ruling applies to a person who has no clothes at all, or whose clothes are more than three-fourths impure. Recognize that this is a case of necessity ('udhr).
The threshold of impurity is three-fourths or more of the garment.
2
State the ruling
Such a person must pray naked, but sitting, and perform ruku and sujud by gestures (nodding the head). Standing is not allowed because it would expose the 'awrah more.
Sitting is the required posture; standing would lead to greater exposure.
3
Locate the dalil
The text cites the statement of Ibn Abbas: 'The one who prays in a ship and the one who prays naked should pray sitting.' This is a qawl sahabi and serves as evidence.
This report is from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
4
Understand the rationale
The reasoning is that standing would cause the 'awrah to be seen clearly, so sitting reduces exposure. The principle is to perform the prayer as much as possible while minimizing sin.
The default ruling of covering 'awrah is wajib, but when impossible, it is excused.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that sitting with gestures is required; if he stands, the prayer is still valid but sitting is better and more cautious.
This is from zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ ۱۶۵] (٧) ومن لم يجد ثوبا صلى عريانا قاعدا يومئ بالركوع والسجود
ان کے پاس بالکل کپڑے نہیں ہے یا کپڑے ہیں لیکن تین چوتھائی سے زیادہ ناپاک ہیں تو گویا کہ اس کے پاس کپڑے ہیں ہی نہیں ۔ اس لئے وہ ننگا ہو کر نماز پڑھے گا۔ البتہ کھڑا ہونے میں ستر دور تک نظر آئے گا اور برا معلوم ہوگا اس لئے قیام چھوڑے گا اور بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھے گا۔ اور رکوع اور سجدے کے لئے اشارہ کرے گا۔ کیونکہ یہی اس کے بس میں ہے (۲) عن ابن عباس قال الذي يصلي في السفينة والذى يصلى عريانا يصلى جالسا (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب صلوۃ العریان ج ثانی ص ۵۸۴ نمبر ۴۵۶۵ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ننگا آدمی مجبوری کہ وجہ سے بیٹھ کر نماز فرض ادا کرے گا اور اس سے قیام ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ لغت یومی : اشارہ کرے گا۔
[165] (7) Whoever does not find a garment, he prays naked, sitting, gesturing for ruku and sujud. He has no clothes at all, or he has clothes but more than three-fourths is impure, so it is as if he has no clothes. Therefore he will pray naked. However, if he stands, his 'awrah will be seen from afar and will look bad, so he abandons standing and prays sitting. And he makes gestures for ruku and sujud, because that is within his capacity. (2) From Ibn Abbas, he said: The one who prays in a ship and the one who prays naked should pray sitting. This effect shows that a naked person, due to necessity, will pray the obligatory prayer sitting and standing is dropped. Lexically: 'yūmi' means he gestures.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This ruling covers the situation when a person has no clothing to cover their 'awrah, either because they have none or because the clothes they have are mostly najis (more than three-fourths). In such a case, they must pray naked. However, to minimize exposure, they should pray sitting rather than standing, because standing would expose the 'awrah more. They also perform ruku and sujud by gestures (nodding) rather than full prostration, because that might expose more. The evidence is the hadith of Ibn Abbas that both the one praying in a ship and the one praying naked should pray sitting. The principle is that the prayer is valid with the maximum capability, and standing is not required when it leads to excessive exposure of 'awrah.

Key Terms
يومئ (yūmī'): To gesture, i.e., to make movements with the head for ruku and sujud instead of actual bending and prostrating.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum posture required for a person who has no clothes to cover themselves?
A) Standing with full ruku and sujud
B) Sitting with gestures for ruku and sujud
C) Lying down
D) Standing with gestures only

Key Takeaway
A person with no clothes must pray sitting with gestures to minimize exposure of the 'awrah.

Standing While Naked: Valid but Not Preferred
Ruling if a naked person prays standing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a naked person's choice to pray standing and explain why sitting is preferable.

Core Idea
A naked person's prayer is valid whether sitting or standing, but sitting is better to avoid exposure.

This passage from the matn clarifies the ruling for a person who has no clothes and must pray. While the preferred method is to pray sitting to minimize exposure of the 'awrah, if he chooses to stand, his prayer is still valid and does not need to be repeated. The commentator explains the reasoning behind this preference, linking it to the substitute role of sitting for standing in cases of illness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The source discusses a person who has no clothing and must pray. Two postures are possible: standing or sitting.
The person is excused (ma'dhur) due to lack of clothing.
2
State the ruling for each posture
If he prays standing, it suffices (اجزاه) — the prayer is valid. If he prays sitting, the matn says 'the first is better' (والاول افضل), meaning sitting is the preferred method.
The ruling is not that standing is invalid, only that sitting is superior.
3
Explain the preference for sitting
When standing, the 'awrah is more exposed to creation and to Allah in a sense of respect. Sitting reduces exposure. Since there is no substitute for covering, sitting is chosen to show humility.
The commentary analogizes to illness where sitting is a substitute for standing; here it is not a substitute but a better choice.
4
Memorize the key Arabic phrase
The core phrase is: فان صلى قائما اجزاه والاول افضل. Memorize this for the ruling.
This is a memorization anchor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[١٦٦] (۸) فان صلى قائما اجزاه والاول افضل.
مرض کی مجبوری کے وقت کھڑے ہونے کا نائب بیٹھنا ہے اور رکوع اور سجدے کا نائب ان کو اشارہ سے ادا کرنا ہے۔ اس لئے ان سب ارکان کا نائب ہو گیا۔ لیکن کھڑے ہونے میں ستر کھلنے کی بدنمائی واضح ہے اس کا کوئی نائب بھی نہیں ہوا اس لئے بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھنا افضل ہے تا کہ عند اللہ اور عند الناس بدنمائی سے بچ جائے۔ تاہم کھڑے ہو کر نماز پڑھے گا تو نماز ادا ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ یہ مجبور ہے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس (پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے) ...
[166] (8) If he prays standing, it suffices him, and the first (sitting) is better. In times of illness, sitting is a substitute for standing, and gestures are a substitute for ruku and sujud. So all these pillars are substituted. But in standing, the exposure of 'awrah is clear and has no substitute, so sitting is better to avoid nudity before Allah and people. However, if he prays standing, his prayer will be valid because he is excused.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This final ruling addresses the case where a naked person chooses to pray standing despite the earlier recommendation to sit. The matn says that if he prays standing, it is valid and suffices, but the earlier method (sitting) is better. The commentary explains that in illness, sitting is a substitute for standing; similarly, for the naked person, sitting serves as a substitute to avoid excessive exposure. Since exposure of 'awrah is worse when standing, sitting is preferred. However, if he stands, the prayer is still valid because he has no other option and is excused due to the constraint.

Key Terms
اجزاه (ajzāhu): It suffices him; the prayer is valid and no repetition is required.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person with no clothes prays standing instead of sitting, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid
B) The prayer is valid and it is mandatory to sit
C) The prayer is valid but sitting is still better
D) He must repeat the prayer standing

Key Takeaway
A naked person's prayer is valid whether sitting or standing, but sitting is better to avoid exposing the 'awrah.

Prayer with Unremovable Impurity: Validity and No Repetition
Ruling on praying with impurity when unable to remove it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying with najasah when unable to remove it, and identify the condition that makes the prayer valid.

Core Idea
Inability to remove impurity makes the prayer valid and no repetition is required.

The Hanafi school recognises that circumstances can limit a person's ability to fulfil the requirement of purity before prayer. This passage addresses a specific case: when a person has najasah on his body or garment but lacks any means to remove it. Instead of abandoning the prayer, he prays in that state, and his prayer is valid. The ruling is built on the principle that Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'prayer while unable to remove najasah'. The ruling is that the prayer is valid (sahih) and does not require repetition.
2
State the condition for this ruling
The condition is the inability to find anything (water or other cleansing agent) to remove the impurity. The text explicitly says 'whoever does not find something to remove impurity'.
Inability here means no means at all, not merely difficulty.
3
Understand the consequence of the condition
Because of the inability, the Shari'ah does not burden the person beyond his capacity, so the prayer is accepted and no qada (repetition) is required.
4
Distinguish from the general rule
Normally, prayer with najasah is invalid. This ruling is a concession (rukhsah) for necessity. If the person later acquires water, he does not need to repeat past prayers made under this concession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن لم يجد ما يزيل النجاسة صلى معها ولم يعد

أگر كوئي ايسي چيز نه پائے جس سے نجاست زائل كر سكے تو ايسي نجاست كے ساتھ هي نماز پڑھے گا اور بعد ميں نهيں لوٹائے گا۔ كپڑے پر يا جسم پر نجاست لگي هوئي ہے ليكرن نجاست كو زائل كرنے كے لئے اور اس كو دھونے كے لئے اس كے پاس پاني يا بهنے والي چيز نهيں ہے تو وه اس كپڑے ميں اور اسي جسم كے ساتھ نماز پڑھ لے گا۔ اس كي طاقت ميں اس سے زائد نهيں ہے اور شريعت طاقت سے زياده مكلف نهيں بناتي۔ اس لئے اس كي نماز جائز هو جائے گي۔ لوٹانے كي ضرورت نهين هوگي۔
And whoever does not find something to remove impurity, he prays with it and does not repeat. (Urdu: If someone does not find any thing to remove impurity, he will pray with that impurity and will not repeat later. There is impurity on the cloth or body, but he has no water or flowing thing to remove it, so he will pray in that cloth and with that body. He has no ability beyond this, and the Shari'ah does not burden beyond capacity. Therefore his prayer will be valid, and there is no need to repeat.)
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the Hanafi school: if a person is unable to remove najasah (ritual impurity) from his body or garment because water or another cleansing agent is unavailable, he is permitted to pray in that state. The prayer is valid and does not require repetition (qada). The reasoning is based on the principle of 'لا يكلف الله نفسا إلا وسعها' (Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity). The author emphasizes that since the person has no means to remove impurity, the Shari'ah does not oblige him to do so. This is a concession for necessity.

Key Terms
نجاست (najāsah): Ritual impurity, such as blood, urine, etc., that prevents validity of prayer unless removed or excused.
لا يُكَلِّفُ اللَّهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا (lā yukallifu Allahu nafsan illā wus‘ahā): Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity. This principle justifies the concession of praying with impurity when unable to remove it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person has impurity on his garment but has no water to wash it, what should he do?
A) He must delay the prayer until he finds water.
B) He prays with the impurity and does not repeat.
C) He prays naked.
D) He prays with the impurity but must repeat later.

Key Takeaway
Prayer with unremovable impurity is valid and does not require repetition.

Prayer of the Naked Person: Sitting or Standing?
Ruling on prayer of one without clothing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who has no garment for prayer and explain the preferred posture and its evidence.

Core Idea
A naked person must pray sitting with gestures to minimize shame, though standing is also valid.

Imagine you are in a situation where you have absolutely nothing to cover your awrah for prayer—or your only garment is heavily impure. Can you still pray? The Hanafi school addresses this necessity with a clear ruling. This lesson unpacks that ruling, its proof, and the wisdom behind preferring one posture over another.

Guided Path
1
Identify the situation and the ruling
The text deals with a person who has no garment to cover the awrah. The ruling: he must pray naked, but in a specific posture. Determine the default posture and the alternative.
Note the condition: no cloth or cloth more than 3/4 impure means considered clothless.
2
Locate the primary and secondary postures
The primary posture is sitting with gestures for ruku and sujud. The secondary posture is standing, which is valid but less preferred. Understand why sitting is better: it reduces exposure of the awrah.
The preference is based on modesty (haya), not invalidity.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The text cites the hadith of Ibn Abbas (in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) that the one who prays in a boat and the one who prays naked should pray sitting. This shows that qiyam is dropped due to necessity.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but accepted in the Hanafi school for this ruling.
4
Understand the 'afdaliyyah' (preference)
Even though standing suffices, sitting is better to avoid shame before Allah and people. The text explains that standing exposes the awrah, and there is no substitute for that, so sitting is superior.
This is a case where a valid alternative becomes the recommended practice due to a higher legal objective (hifz al-'awrah).
5
Apply to a practical scenario
Imagine a prisoner stripped of clothes. He must pray naked. He has the choice: sit and gesture, which is better, or stand, which is valid. The mufta bihi (operative position) is to sit.
If cloth becomes available mid-prayer, he must cover and continue standing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن لم يجد ثوبا صلى عريانا قاعدا يومئ بالركوع والسجود [١٦٦] (۸) فان صلى قائما اجزاه والاول افضل.

جو کپڑا نہ پائے تو نگا ہی نماز پڑھے گا۔ بیٹھ کر رکوع اور سجدہ کا اشارہ کرے گا۔ ان کے پاس بالکل کپڑے نہیں ہے یا کپڑے ہیں لیکن تین چوتھائی سے زیادہ ناپاک ہیں تو گویا کہ اس کے پاس کپڑے ہیں ہی نہیں ۔ اس لئے وہ ننگا ہو کر نماز پڑھے گا۔ البتہ کھڑا ہونے میں ستر دور تک نظر آئے گا اور برا معلوم ہوگا اس لئے قیام چھوڑے گا اور بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھے گا۔ اور رکوع اور سجدے کے لئے اشارہ کرے گا۔ کیونکہ یہی اس کے بس میں ہے (۲) عن ابن عباس قال الذي يصلي في السفينة والذى يصلى عريانا يصلى جالسا (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب صلوۃ العریان ج ثانی ص ۵۸۴ نمبر ۴۵۶۵ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ننگا آدمی مجبوری کہ وجہ سے بیٹھ کر نماز فرض ادا کرے گا اور اس سے قیام ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ لغت یومی : اشارہ کرے گا۔ [۱۲] (۸) پس اگر ننگے نے کھڑے ہو کر نماز پڑھی تو کافی ہو جائے گی لیکن پہلا افضل ہے (یعنی بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھنا) مرض کی مجبوری کے وقت کھڑے ہونے کا نائب بیٹھنا ہے اور رکوع اور سجدے کا نائب ان کو اشارہ سے ادا کرنا ہے۔ اس لئے ان سب ارکان کا نائب ہو گیا۔ لیکن کھڑے ہونے میں ستر کھلنے کی بدنمائی واضح ہے اس کا کوئی نائب بھی نہیں ہوا اس لئے بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھنا افضل ہے تا کہ عند اللہ اور عند الناس بدنمائی سے بچ جائے۔ تاہم کھڑے ہو کر نماز پڑھے گا تو نماز ادا ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ یہ مجبور ہے
Whoever does not find a garment, prays naked sitting, indicating ruku and sujud. If he prays standing, it suffices, but the first is better. (Urdu: He who does not find cloth will pray naked. He will sit and indicate ruku and sujud. If he has no cloth at all, or if more than three-quarters of his cloth is impure, he is considered as having no cloth. So he will pray naked. However, while standing the awrah would be seen far and appear evil, so he abandons standing and prays sitting, indicating ruku and sujud because that is within his capacity. From Ibn Abbas: 'The one who prays in a boat and the one who prays naked should pray sitting.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab Salah al-Uryan, no. 4565) This shows that a naked person, due to necessity, will perform the obligatory prayer sitting and qiyam is dropped. Then: If the naked person prays standing, it is sufficient, but the first is better, i.e., praying sitting. In case of illness, sitting is the substitute for standing, and indicating is the substitute for ruku and sujud. Thus these pillars have substitutes. But standing exposes the awrah, and there is no substitute for that, so sitting is better to avoid shame before Allah and people. Nevertheless, if he prays standing, the prayer is fulfilled because he is excused.)
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling of one who has no clothing to cover his 'awrah during prayer. The Hanafi position: he must pray naked, but sitting with gestures for ruku and sujud, because standing would expose his 'awrah more. However, if he prays standing, his prayer is valid but sitting is better. The evidence is the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the one who prays in a boat and the one who prays naked should pray sitting. The commentary explains that if one has no cloth at all, or if more than three-quarters of his cloth is impure, he is considered clothless. He must sit to minimize exposure. The preference for sitting is to avoid shame before Allah and people. The standing prayer is still valid due to necessity, but the optimal practice is sitting.

Key Terms
عريان (uryān): One who has no covering for his 'awrah (parts that must be covered in prayer).
قيام (qiyām): Standing during prayer, which is a pillar (rukn) for those capable.
يومئ (yūmi'u): He indicates, i.e., makes a gesture for ruku and sujud instead of fully bowing and prostrating.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the preferred posture for a person who has no garment to cover his awrah for prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) Standing
B) Sitting with gestures
C) Lying down
D) Prostrating only

Key Takeaway
A naked person must pray sitting with gestures to uphold modesty, but standing also fulfills the obligation.

Intention for Prayer and Its Timing with the Opening Takbir
Ruling on intention for prayer and its timing with takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of intention for prayer and apply it to scenarios involving intervals or lack of intention.

Core Idea
Intention must coincide with the opening takbir; any intervening action breaks the connection.

This lesson examines the requirement of intention (niyyah) for prayer in the Hanafi school. You will learn that intention is an essential condition that must be present at the very moment of the opening takbir (tahrimah) and that no worldly action should separate the two. The lesson also covers the additional requirement for a follower (muqtadi) to intend to follow the imam, supported by hadith proofs. By the end, you will be able to correctly assess common scenarios that might invalidate the intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the intention (niyyah) for prayer. According to the Hanafi school, it is fard (obligatory) and must be present at the time of the opening takbir (tahrimah). Without it, the prayer is invalid.
The text uses 'niyyah' and 'tahrimah' as key terms.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith 'Actions are but by intentions' (al-a'malu bi al-niyyat), reported from Umar ibn al-Khattab. This is a well-known hadith with strong transmission (sahih).
The hadith is cited in the source to establish the general principle that deeds require intention.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith indicates that the validity of deeds depends on intentions. Since prayer is a deed, it requires a proper intention. The Hanafi school deduces that the intention must be present at the beginning of the prayer—the opening takbir—because the takbir is the entry into prayer.
The logical link: the hadith establishes intention as a condition; takbir is the start; therefore intention must accompany takbir.
4
Apply the ruling to scenarios
Use the rule to evaluate cases: a) praying without any intention → invalid; b) intending but performing an action before takbir → intention is broken, must re-intend at takbir; c) for a muqtadi, additionally intending to follow the imam is required.
The text provides these scenarios explicitly.
5
Note the additional requirement for muqtadi
The follower must intend to follow the imam. This is based on hadiths that command complete following and the imam being a guarantor. Without this intention, the follower's prayer is not connected to the imam's.
This is a separate condition specific to congregational prayer.

Source Text

وينوى للصلوة التي يدخل فيها بنية لا يفصل بينها و بين التحريمة بعمل

[۱۶۷] (۹) اس نماز کی نیت کرے جس میں داخل ہو رہا ہے ایسی نیت کہ اس کے درمیان اور تحریمہ کے درمیان کسی عمل سے فصل نہ ہو۔ نیت ارادے کا نام ہے۔ تحریمہ کے ساتھ ساتھ ارادہ ہو کہ میں فلاں نماز پڑھ رہا ہوں۔ اگر دل کے ارادہ کے بغیر نماز پڑھ لی یا تحریمہ باندھ لیا تو نماز نہیں ہوگی۔ اگر نیت کی پھر کوئی عمل کیا اور عمل کے بعد دوبارہ نیت کئے بغیر احرام باندھ لیا تو چونکہ احرام کے وقت نیت نہیں تھی اس لئے احترام نہیں ہوا۔ وجہ یہ حدیث ہے سمعت عمر بن خطاب على المنبر يقول سمعت رسول الله عليه يقول انما الاعمال بالنيات (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب کیف کان بدء الوحی الی رسول اللہ ص نمبر 1 ) اگر امام کی اقتدا کر رہا ہو تو یہ بھی نیت کرنی پڑے گی کہ میں اس امام : کی اقتدا میں نماز پڑھ رہا ہوں۔ کیونکہ مقتدی کی نماز امام کی نماز کے ساتھ متضمن ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة أن رسول الله الا الله قال انما جعل الامام ليؤتم به فلا تختلفوا عليه فاذا كبر فكبرو (ب) مسلم شریف، باب انتمام الماموم بالا مام ، ص ۷ ۱۷، کتاب الصلوۃ، نمبر ۴۱۴ / بخاری شریف، باب انما جعل الامام لیوتم به ص ۹۵ نمبر (۶۸۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مقتدی کو امام کی مکمل اقتدا کرنی چاہئے ۔ اور اس سے انحراف نہیں کرنا چاہئے ۔ اس لئے امام کی اقتدا کی نیت ضروری ہے۔ عن ابی ھریرۃ قال قال رسول الله الله الامام ضامن والمؤذن مؤتمن ( ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء ان الامام ضامن والمؤذن مؤتمن ص ۵۱ نمبر ۲۰۷) جب امام ضامن ہوا تو اس کی اقتدا بھی کرنی چاہئے ۔ ون نیت میں دل سے ارادہ کرنا کافی ہے۔ زبان سے بولنا ضروری نہیں ، مگر زبان سے بول لے تو بہتر ہے۔
And he intends the prayer he enters with an intention such that no action separates between it and the takbir. (Urdu: He should intend the prayer he is entering with an intention where no action intervenes between it and the tahrimah. Intention is the name of resolve. At the time of tahrimah, the resolve should be: I am praying such-and-such prayer. If he prays or ties the tahrimah without the resolve of the heart, the prayer is invalid. If he intends then performs an action, and after the action ties the ihram without re-intending, then since at the time of ihram there was no intention, the ihram is not valid. The proof is the hadith: I heard Umar ibn al-Khattab on the minbar saying: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'Actions are but by intentions.' (Bukhari, Bad' al-Wahy, no. 1) If he is following an imam, he must also intend that he is praying in the imam's following, because the follower's prayer is connected to the imam's prayer. From Abu Huraira: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The imam is appointed to be followed; so do not differ from him. When he says takbir, say takbir.' (Muslim and Bukhari) This hadith shows that the follower must completely follow the imam and not deviate. Therefore, intending to follow the imam is necessary. From Abu Huraira: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The imam is a guarantor, and the mu'adhdhin is a trustee.' (Tirmidhi) Since the imam is a guarantor, he must be followed. And in intention, resolving in the heart is sufficient; speaking is not necessary, but if one speaks it is better.)
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage deals with the requirement of niyyah (intention) for prayer. The Hanafi position: the intention must be present at the time of the opening takbir (tahrimah) and must not be separated by any action. The intention is an act of the heart; verbal utterance is not required but recommended. Additionally, for a follower (muqtadi), it is necessary to intend to follow the imam, based on hadiths. The commentary emphasizes that if one prays without intention, the prayer is invalid. Also, if one intends then does an action before the takbir, the connection is broken and the takbir becomes invalid. The main evidence is the well-known hadith 'Actions are but by intentions.' Other hadiths stress following the imam correctly.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention, the resolve of the heart to perform a specific prayer.
تحريمة (taḥrīmah): The opening takbir that initiates the prayer and makes it forbidden to engage in worldly actions.
مقتدي (muqtadī): The follower in congregational prayer; one who prays behind an imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Prayer is valid but makruh
D) Prayer is valid if he recites aloud

Key Takeaway
The intention for prayer must be made simultaneously with the opening takbir, and any action separating them invalidates the intention.

Facing the Qibla: Obligation and Exception in Fear
Ruling on facing qibla and exception for fear

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on facing the qibla in normal and fearful conditions and identify the Quranic proofs used.

Core Idea
Facing the qibla is fard, but fear lifts the obligation — Allah's mercy encompasses all directions.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on facing the qibla during prayer. While the general obligation is derived from the clear command in Surah al-Baqarah (2:144), the school recognizes an exception for those in genuine fear, based on the same surah's later verse (2:115). We will explore how both verses are reconciled and what constitutes a valid excuse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is facing the qibla during prayer. Under normal conditions, the Hanafi ruling is that it is fard (obligatory).
2
Locate the primary dalil
The obligation is proven by Quran 2:144: 'Turn your faces towards the Sacred Mosque.'
The command is general and unambiguous.
3
Identify the exception
The passage states an exception for those in fear (khā'if). The exception is proven by Quran 2:115: 'Wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah.'
This verse is used to justify deviation when necessary.
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The first verse is a general command; the second provides a concession, indicating that the command is not absolute and can be overridden by necessity. The Hanafi school reconciles by viewing 2:115 as a mukhassis (specifier).
The ruling is conditional upon ability.
5
Apply the ruling
A person in fear (e.g., enemy attack, dangerous animal) may pray without facing the qibla, and the prayer is valid.
The fear must be genuine and immediate.

Source Text

[۱۲۸ (۱۰) نماز میں قبلہ کا استقبال کرے مگر یہ کہ خوف ہو تو نماز پڑھے جدھر چاہے۔ آیت میں ہے وحیث ما كنتم فولوا وجوهكم شطره (ج ) ( آیت ۱۴۴ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز میں قبلہ کی طرف چہرہ کرنا چاہئے۔ اور خوف کے وقت جدھر ممکن ہو اس طرف چہرہ کرنے سے نماز ادا ہو جائے گی۔ اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے واللہ المشرق والمغرب باينما تولو فثم وجه الله ( د ) ( آیت ۱۵ اسورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ مجبوری کے موقع پر کسی اور

حاشیہ : (الف) عمر ابن خطاب سے منبر پر کہتے ہوئے سنا کہ حضور نے فرمایا کرتے تھے کہ اعمال کا دارومدار نیتوں پر ہے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا امام بنایا گیا ہے تا کہ اس کی اقتدا کی جائے اس لئے اس کے خلاف نہ کرو۔ پس جب وہ تکبیر کہے تو تم تکبیر کہو ( ج ) جہاں کہیں ہو اپنا چہرہ بیت اللہ کی طرف نماز میں کرو ( د ) اللہ ہی کے لئے مشرق و مغرب ہے تو جدھر بھی چہرہ کر ووہاں اللہ ہے۔
And he faces the qibla unless he is in fear, then he prays towards whichever direction he can. (Urdu: In prayer, one should face the qibla, except if there is fear, then he prays in whatever direction he wishes. The verse says: 'And wherever you are, turn your faces towards it' (2:144). This shows that one should face the qibla in prayer. And in time of fear, facing any possible direction suffices for the prayer. Its proof is the verse: 'To Allah belong the east and the west; wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah' (2:115). This shows that in a situation of constraint, one may face another direction. Footnotes: (a) I heard Umar ibn al-Khattab on the minbar saying: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'Actions are but by intentions.' (d) To Allah belong the east and the west; wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah.)

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on facing qibla. It is obligatory to face the Kaaba during prayer, as derived from the Quranic verse 'turn your faces towards it' (2:144). However, in a state of fear (e.g., enemy attack or danger), the obligation is lifted, and one may pray in any direction, based on the verse 'wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah' (2:115). The Hanafi school allows this concession for necessity. The footnotes at the bottom of the page provide the full citations for the hadith and verses mentioned in this lesson and the previous one.

Key Terms
قبلة (qiblah): The direction of the Kaaba in Mecca towards which Muslims pray.
خائف (khā'if): One who fears for his life or safety, such as during battle or threat.

The Ruling on Intention (Niyyah) for Prayer
Ruling on intention for prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intention for prayer and identify the conditions for its validity, including the requirement for followers.

Core Idea
Intention must be simultaneous with the opening takbir and requires no verbal utterance.

Intention (niyyah) is a fundamental condition for the validity of prayer. In this lesson, we examine the precise ruling: that the intention must coincide with the opening takbir (tahrimah) without any intervening action. We also explore the additional requirement for a follower (muqtadi) and the evidence from the hadith 'Actions are but by intentions.' Understanding this ruling helps ensure your prayer is legally sound.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on intention
The passage states that one must intend the specific prayer simultaneously with the takbir tahrimah. Intention is a condition (shart) for prayer's validity, not a pillar.
In Hanafi fiqh, intention is obligatory (wajib) and failure to intend invalidates the prayer.
2
Understand the simultaneity condition
No action may separate the intention from the takbir. If you intend, then perform an action (e.g., step forward), then say takbir, the intention is considered disconnected and the prayer is invalid.
The intention and tahrimah must be spiritually and temporally linked.
3
Recognise the evidence from hadith
The hadith 'Innama al-a'malu bi-nniyyat' (Actions are but by intentions) is the primary proof. The particle 'innama' indicates restriction (hasr), meaning actions depend entirely on intention.
This hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari and is accepted by all schools.
4
Apply the follower's additional rule
A muqtadi must intend not only the prayer itself but also to follow that specific imam. The hadith 'The imam is appointed to be followed' provides the basis.
Without this intention, the follower's prayer is invalid because it is contingent on the imam's.
5
Distinguish heart intention from verbal utterance
Intention is a resolve of the heart; speaking it aloud is not required, though it is recommended. The prayer is valid even if one does not utter the intention verbally.
Many mistakenly believe verbal intention is obligatory; this clarifies it is merely praiseworthy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

197 (9) And he intends the prayer which he enters with an intention such that no action separates it from the tahrimah. [Urdu: He should intend the prayer he is entering, an intention such that no action comes between it and the tahrimah. Intention is called resolve. Along with the tahrimah, he resolves, 'I am praying such-and-such prayer.' If he prays without resolve of the heart or ties the tahrimah without intention, the prayer is not valid. The reason is this hadith: I heard 'Umar bin al-Khattab on the minbar saying, I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) saying, 'Actions are but by intentions.' ... If he is following an imam, he must also intend that he is praying following that imam. Because the follower's prayer is included with the imam's prayer. ... Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage states the legal ruling on intention (niyyah) for entering the prayer. The author begins by stating the rule: one must intend the specific prayer he is entering with no action separating the intention from the takbir tahrimah. The commentary then explains that niyyah is a resolve of the heart, not merely verbal pronunciation. Simultaneity of intention and tahrimah is required; if one prays without heart intention or ties tahrimah without intention, the prayer is invalid. The hadith 'Actions are but by intentions' is cited as primary evidence (from Bukhari). Additionally, the commentary addresses the follower (muqtadi): he must also intend to follow the imam, as proven by the hadith 'The imam is appointed to be followed.' This is because the follower's prayer is contingent upon the imam's. The passage concludes that intention in the heart is sufficient; verbal articulation is recommended but not mandatory.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The resolve of the heart to perform a specific act of worship; must be simultaneous with the opening takbir.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir (saying Allahu Akbar) which prohibits worldly actions and initiates the prayer.
مقتدي (muqtadi): A follower who prays behind an imam in congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a follower (muqtadi) intend when praying behind an imam?
A) Only the prayer itself, e.g., 'I intend to pray Maghrib'
B) To follow the imam, in addition to the prayer
C) To say the intention aloud
D) To intend only if they are late for the prayer

Key Takeaway
Intention must be simultaneous with the opening takbir and, for followers, include the intent to follow the imam; heart intention suffices.

Facing the Qibla: Obligation and Exception for Fear
Ruling on facing qibla and concession when fearful

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on facing qibla in prayer and identify the Quranic proof for the exception in fear.

Core Idea
Facing qibla is wajib; genuine fear allows prayer in any direction, as Quran 2:115 permits turning anywhere out of necessity.

In normal circumstances, facing the qibla is a condition for the validity of prayer. However, the Shariah recognizes that situations of fear (khawf) may make it impossible or dangerous to face the Ka'bah. This lesson examines the general ruling and its exception, along with the Quranic proofs that establish both the obligation and the concession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling and its condition
The text states that one must face the qibla (استقبال القبلة). Recognize this as a condition (shart) for prayer validity in normal circumstances.
The ruling is wajib; not a pillar (rukn).
2
Identify the exception and its condition
The exception is for a fearful person (خائف). Note that the fear must be genuine and immediate, such as from an enemy or predator.
The concession allows prayer in any direction the person is able.
3
Locate the primary proof and its implication
The author cites Quran 2:144: 'Wherever you are, turn your faces toward it.' Recognize this as a direct command (amr) establishing the obligation.
In Hanafi usul, a command indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is a qarina to the contrary.
4
Locate the secondary proof and its role
Quran 2:115: 'To Allah belong the east and the west; wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah.' This verse provides the basis for the concession in fear, indicating that direction is not absolute in hardship.
This verse does not abrogate the first but provides an exception.
5
Synthesize the two verses and apply to the case
Combine both proofs: the general rule (2:144) is operative unless a valid excuse (fear) exists, in which case 2:115 allows turning in any direction.
The Hanafi position is that the prayer of a fearful person facing any direction is valid and complete.

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on facing the qibla during prayer. The author states the general obligation: one must face the qibla. However, an exception is made for a person who is in fear (e.g., of enemy or predator); such a person may pray in any direction he can. The commentary then cites two Quranic proofs: (1) Surah al-Baqarah 2:144 commands turning towards the Masjid al-Haram, establishing the general rule. (2) Surah al-Baqarah 2:115, which states that Allah's face is everywhere, provides the basis for the concession in fear—where necessity overrides the specific direction. Additionally, a hadith about a naked person praying is included to show that in circumstances of being unseen, one may pray standing, indicating that the direction is not the sole focus when there is a genuine need.

Key Terms
قبلة (qibla): The direction of the Ka'bah in Mecca, which must be faced during prayer.
خوف (khawf): Fear of an external threat (e.g., enemy, animal, natural disaster) that makes it difficult or dangerous to face qibla.

Ijtihad for Qibla When Ambiguous: No Repeat After Error
Ruling on prayer after ijtihad for qibla and hadith evidence for validity despite error.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer when qibla is ambiguous after ijtihad and apply the hadith evidence to determine the obligation of repeat.

Core Idea
Sincere ijtihad for qibla makes your prayer valid even if you faced the wrong direction — no repeat required.

Imagine you are traveling, the sky is overcast, and no one can tell you the qibla. You do your best to determine the direction and pray. Later, you realize you were completely wrong. Is your prayer valid? The Hanafi school says yes, based on a clear prophetic tradition. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the evidence, and the underlying principle of doing what is within one's capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and the Ruling
Read the passage to identify when ijtihad is required (qibla ambiguous and no one to ask) and the resulting hukm: the prayer is valid even if error is discovered later, with no repeat (fala i'adah 'alayh).
The ruling applies only when ijtihad was performed. If one prayed without ijtihad, the rule differs.
2
Understand the Key Terms: Ijtihad and Taharri
In this context, ijtihad and taharri mean exerting effort to determine the qibla using available signs (e.g., stars, sun, landmarks). They are synonymous here.
The result of taharri becomes the effective qibla for that prayer.
3
Examine the Hadith Evidence
Read the hadith of Jabir. The companions differed in their taharri due to cloud cover. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Your prayers are valid' (اجزأت صلواتكم). This directly establishes the ruling.
The hadith is narrated by al-Bayhaqi and al-Tirmidhi; its transmission is zanni but its meaning is qat'i for this case.
4
Connect the Evidence to the Ruling
The Prophet's explicit declaration proves that ijtihad suffices and error does not invalidate. The commentary adds that this is because the person did what was within his capacity (wus'at).
The underlying principle: 'Do what you can, and the rest is excused.'
5
Note the Cross-Madhhab Difference
The Shafi'i and Maliki schools require repetition if the error is discovered within the prayer time. The Hanafi school holds that no repeat is needed at all, relying on the same hadith and the principle that taharri itself becomes the qibla.
This difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf (thamarah al-khilaf).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

19 (1) If the qibla becomes ambiguous for him and there is no one present whom he can ask, he makes ijtihad and prays. If he knows after praying that he erred, there is no repeat upon him. [Urdu: If the qibla is confusing for the one praying and there is no one present from whom he can ask about it, he will do ijtihad and pray. We mentioned that to the Prophet (peace be upon him), and he said: 'Your prayers are valid.' Commentary
This passage addresses the situation when the qibla direction is unknown and no one knowledgeable is available to ask. The ruling is that the person must exert ijtihad (effort) to determine the qibla, then pray according to his best judgment. If after completing the prayer he discovers that he prayed in the wrong direction, the prayer is valid and need not be repeated. The commentary explains that one performs taharri (scrutiny) and prays where his heart inclines. The primary evidence is the hadith of Jabir where companions prayed in different directions due to cloud cover; the Prophet (peace be upon him) declared their prayers valid despite being wrong. The rationale is that the person did what was within his capability (wus'at). Therefore, taharri effectively becomes his qibla for that prayer.

Key Terms
اجتهاد (ijtihad): Exerting effort to determine the qibla direction using available signs or reasoning.
تحري (taharri): Scrutiny or seeking the correct direction by using one's judgment when the qibla is unclear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When ijtihad for qibla is performed sincerely, the prayer is valid even if the direction is wrong; no repeat is required, because taharri becomes the effective qibla for that prayer.

Correcting Qibla During Prayer: Turn and Continue
Ruling on turning to correct qibla if error is realized while still in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that turning towards the correct qibla during prayer is wajib and that the prayer continues validly, and explain the evidence from the hadith of the Companions in Quba.

Core Idea
Realizing wrong qibla while praying? Turn immediately and continue; earlier part is valid due to ijtihad.

What if you start praying in a direction you believe is correct, but then learn the true qibla while still in prayer? Should you stop and start over, or keep going? The Hanafi school has a clear ruling: you must turn toward the right direction immediately and continue from where you left off. This ruling is rooted in the incident of the Companions when the qibla was changed from Jerusalem to Makkah, and it is supported by authentic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is: a person is in prayer and realizes they are facing the wrong qibla. The ruling is: it becomes wajib to turn towards the correct qibla and continue the prayer (bana). The previous portion is valid.
This applies whether the original direction was based on ijtihad or a reliable source that later proved wrong.
2
Examine the historical precedent
The text recounts the story of the Companions in Quba who were praying Fajr facing Jerusalem. Upon hearing the revelation to face the Ka'bah, they turned around during the prayer and completed it without restarting.
This shows that turning during prayer does not invalidate it when done for a valid reason.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence
The hadith of Ibn 'Umar is cited from Sahih al-Bukhari. The Companions turned immediately, and the Prophet's approval is implied by the preservation of this incident in the Sunnah.
The hadith is considered qati' al-thubut and qati' al-dalalah, providing strong evidence.
4
Derive the legal principle
From this, the Hanafi school derives that bana (building on the previous prayer) is permissible. The earlier part is valid because it was based on ijtihad (taharri), which has legal weight.
This principle is limited to cases where the person was making an effort to determine the qibla, not if they were negligent.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage deals with what happens when a person discovers the correct qibla direction while he is still engaged in prayer. Rulings on Ijtihad for Qibla: Validity and Action upon Error
Rulings on ijtihad for qibla and its validity after error.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of prayer performed after ijtihad for qibla when the direction is later found mistaken, and explain the proof from the hadith of Jabir.

Core Idea
Ijtihad for qibla fulfills the obligation; prayer is valid even if the direction is later found wrong.

When the qibla is unclear and no one is available to ask, a Muslim must perform ijtihad (taharri) to determine the correct direction. But what if he later discovers he was mistaken? This lesson explores the Hanafi position that such prayer is valid and need not be repeated, supported by a clear hadith. It also covers what to do if the error is realized during prayer, and addresses a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding a complete reversal of direction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
Read the passage to extract the two main rulings: (1) after prayer error – no repetition; (2) error during prayer – turn and continue. Note the condition: ijtihad performed when qibla is unclear and no one to ask.
The ruling applies only when ijtihad is genuine and based on available signs.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
Find the hadith of Jabir (RA) quoted in the passage. Identify it as an ahad hadith with zanni thubut and dalala.
The hadith explicitly states prayers were valid despite the wrong qibla.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze the phrase 'قد اجزأت صلواتكم' (your prayers are sufficient/valid). This indicates the Prophet (ﷺ) did not order repetition, which is the basis for Hanafi ruling.
The generality of the hadith covers all degrees of error, including complete opposite direction.
4
Note the ikhtilaf with Shafi'i
Contrast the Hanafi view with Imam al-Shafi'i's position that if the qibla was exactly opposite, repetition is required. Understand the opposing proof (qiyas: total inversion invalidates).
Shafi'i restricts the hadith to cases of partial error, not complete reversal.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand why the Hanafi school gives precedence to the literal wording of the hadith and the principle of istihsan (juristic preference) over strict qiyas.
The mufta bihi position is the Hanafi view, based on the generality of the hadith and the principle that ijtihad exhausts one's duty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلوة
(۱۹) فان اشتبهت عليه القبلة وليس بحضرته من يسئله عنها اجتهد و صلى فان علم انه اخطأ بعد ما صلى فلا اعادة عليه (۱۰) (۱۲) و ان علم ذلك و هو في الصلوة طرف توجہ کر کے نماز پڑھ لی تو نماز ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ وہاں اللہ کا چہرہ ہے۔ (۱۶۹) (۱۱) اگر نماز پڑھنے والوں پر قبلہ مشتبہ ہو جائے اور وہاں کوئی موجود نہیں ہے جس سے اس کے بارے میں پوچھ سکے تو اجتہاد کر یگا اور نماز پڑھیگا پس اگر جانا کہ غلطی ہوگئی نماز پڑھنے کے بعد تو اس پر لوٹانا نہیں ہے۔
قبلہ کا پتہ نہ چلے اور کوئی آدمی بھی نہ ہو کہ اس سے پوچھ سکے تو تحری کرے گا اور جدھر دل کا رجحان ہو اسی طرف نماز پڑھ لیگا۔ اور نماز کے بعد معلوم ہوا کہ کہ غلط جہت میں نماز پڑھی ہے تب بھی نماز لوٹانے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے نماز ہو گئی۔ اس لئے کہ اس کی وسعت میں جتنا تھا وہ کر گزرا ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن جابر قال كنا مع النبي الله في مسير او سرية فاصابنا غيم فتحرينا واختلفنا في القبلة فصلى كل رجل منا على حدة فجعل احدنا يخط بين يديه لنعلم امكنتنا فلما اصبحنا نظرناه فاذا نحن قد صلينا على غير القبلة فذكرنا ذلك للنبي الا الله فقال قد اجزأت صلواتكم (الف ) ( سنن بیھقی ، باب الاختلاف في القبلة عند التحری، ج ثانی، ص ۱۶، نمبر ۲۲۳۵ / ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء في الرجل يصلى لغير المقبلة في الغيم ص ۸۰ نمبر ۳۴۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تحری کر کے نماز پڑھی تو قبلہ غلط بھی ہو جائے تو نماز لوٹانے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ تحری ہی اس کا قبلہ ہو گیا۔
(۱۷۰) (۱۲) اور اگر قبلہ کی غلطی کو جانا اس حال میں کہ وہ نماز میں ہے تو قبلہ کی طرف گھومے گا اور اسی پر بنا کرے گا۔ صحابہ بیت المقدس کی طرف نماز پڑھتے تھے۔ سولہ یا سترہ ماہ کے بعد قبلہ بدل گیا۔ کچھ صحابہ نماز میں تھے اور اطلاع دی گئی کہ قبلہ بدل گیا ہے تو وہ لوگ نماز کے درمیان ہی گھوم گئے ۔ ارنماز پر بنا کی اور نماز پڑھتے رہیں۔ حدیث میں ہے عن عبد الله بن عمر قال بين الناس بقباء في صلوة الصبح اذ جاء هم آت فقال ان رسول الله الله قد انزل عليه الليلة قرآن وقد امر ان يستقبل الكعبة فاستقبلوها وكانت وجوههم الى الشام فاستداروا الى الكعبة (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب ما جاء ومن لم سر الا عادة علی من سہی فصلی الی غیر القبلة ص ۵۸ کتاب الصلوۃ نمبر ۴۰۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تحری کر کے غیر قبلہ کی طرف نماز پڑھ رہا ہو اور درمیان میں بیح قبلہ کا علم ہو گیا تو اس طرف پھر جائے اور پہلی نماز پر بنا کرے۔ پہلی نماز بھی تحری کی بنا پر مسیح ہے۔
استدار : گھوم جائے مشتق دور سے ہے، بنی : بنا کرے۔
حاشیه : (الف) حضرت جائیم سے روایت ہے کہ ہم حضور کے ساتھ کسی سفر میں تھے۔ پس ہم لوگوں پر بادل چھا گیا۔ پس ہم نے تحری کی اور ہم قبلہ کے بارے میں اختلاف کرنے لگے۔ پس ہم میں سے ہر ایک نے الگ الگ جہت میں نماز پڑھی۔ پس ہم میں سے ہر ایک نے اپنے سامنے خط کھینچا تا کہ ہم اپنی اپنی جگہ جائیں۔ پس جب صبح ہوئی تو ہم نے دیکھا کہ ہم نے قبلہ کے علاوہ کی طرف نماز پڑھی تھی۔ پس اس کا حضور کے سامنے تذکرہ کیا تو آپ نے فرمایا تمہاری نماز جائز ہو گئی (ب) حضرت عبداللہ بن عمرؓ نے فرمایا اس درمیان کہ لوگ قباء میں صبح کی نماز پڑھر ہے تھے کوئی آنے والا آیا اور کہا کہ حضور پر رات میں قرآن اترا ہے اور حکم دیا ہے کہ کعبہ کا استقبال کریں تو لوگوں نے کعبہ کا استقبال کیا۔ حالانکہ ان کا چہرہ شام کی طرف تھا تو وہ لوگ کعبہ کی طرف گھوم گئے۔
قال استدار الى القبلة و بنى عليها .
كتاب الصلوة
فائن امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر قبلہ بالکل پشت کے پیچھے ہو گیا تو چونکہ کمل الٹا ہو گیا اس لئے نماز لوٹائے گا۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ اس کی طاقت میں اتنا ہی تھا اس لئے نہیں لوٹائے گا۔ پھر حدیث میں بھی لوٹانے کا حکم نہیں ہے۔
Book of Prayer. (19) If the qibla is unclear to him and he does not have someone present to ask, he will perform ijtihad and pray. If he knows that he was mistaken after praying, there is no repetition upon him. (10) (12) And if he knows that while he is in prayer, he turns (in that direction) and completes his prayer, then the prayer is valid. Because that is the face of Allah. (169) (11) If the qibla becomes unclear to the one praying and there is no one present to ask about it, he will do ijtihad and pray. Then if he knows that he made a mistake after praying, he does not have to repeat it. If the qibla cannot be determined and there is no person to ask, he will perform taharri (seeking the correct direction) and pray in the direction his heart inclines. And if after prayer it becomes known that he prayed in the wrong direction, still there is no need to repeat the prayer; the prayer is valid. Because he did what was within his capacity. (2) In hadith: From Jabir, he said: We were with the Prophet (ﷺ) on a journey or expedition, and clouds covered us. So we performed taharri and differed about the qibla. Each man among us prayed separately. One of us would draw a line in front of him so we would know our places. When morning came, we looked and found that we had prayed in a direction other than the qibla. We mentioned that to the Prophet (ﷺ), and he said: 'Your prayers are valid.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Ikhtilaf fi al-Qibla 'inda al-Taharri, vol. 2, p. 16, no. 2235; Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi al-rajul yusalli li-ghayr al-qibla fi al-ghaym, p. 80, no. 345). From this hadith it is known that if one prays after taharri and the qibla turns out to be wrong, there is no need to repeat the prayer. Because the direction he determined became his qibla. (170) (12) And if he realizes the mistake in qibla while he is in prayer, he will turn towards the qibla and continue building on that prayer. The Companions used to pray facing Bayt al-Maqdis. After sixteen or seventeen months, the qibla was changed. Some Companions were in prayer and were informed that the qibla had changed. They turned during the prayer, built on it, and continued praying. In hadith: From Abdullah ibn Umar, he said: While the people were at Quba' praying the morning prayer, someone came and said: 'Indeed, the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) received revelation last night and was commanded to face the Ka'bah, so face it.' Their faces were towards Syria, so they turned towards the Ka'bah. (Bukhari, Bab ma ja'a wa man lam yara al-i'ada 'ala man saha fasalla ila ghayr al-qibla, p. 58, Kitab al-Salah, no. 403). From this hadith it is known that if one is praying after taharri in a direction other than the qibla and becomes aware of the qibla in the middle, he turns to that direction and builds on the previous prayer. The previous prayer is also valid based on taharri. 'Istadara' means he turned around, from the root 'dawr'. 'Bana' means he built on it. Footnote (a): From Jabir: We were with the Prophet on a journey... (as above). (b): From Abdullah ibn Umar: While the people were at Quba'... (as above). It is said: He turned to the qibla and built upon it. Book of Prayer. So Imam Shafi'i says: If the qibla is completely behind him, since the entire direction is reversed, he will repeat the prayer. We say: He did what was within his capacity, so he will not repeat. Moreover, there is no command to repeat in the hadith.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings concerning the qibla when it is unclear. First, if one is unable to determine the qibla and has no one to ask, he must perform ijtihad (also called taharri) — a reasoned effort to ascertain the correct direction. He prays according to his best guess. If after prayer he discovers he was mistaken, his prayer is valid and need not be repeated. This is supported by the hadith of Jabir (RA), where the Companions prayed in different directions due to clouds, yet the Prophet (ﷺ) declared their prayers valid. The Hanafi position is that taharri itself becomes the effective qibla for that person; his obligation was to seek, and he fulfilled it. The second ruling concerns discovering the error during prayer: he must turn towards the true qibla and continue from where he was, without restarting. This is proven by the incident of the change of qibla from Jerusalem to the Ka'bah, where the Companions turned in prayer and the Prophet (ﷺ) approved. At the end, a brief inter-madhhab dispute is mentioned: Imam al-Shafi'i held that if one prays with taharri but the actual qibla is exactly opposite (behind him), the prayer is invalid and must be repeated, because the direction is entirely wrong. The Hanafi response is that the person did his utmost (ijtihad), and the hadith does not distinguish degrees of error; therefore, repetition is not required. This illustrates the Hanafi principle of istihsan (juristic preference) over strict qiyas.

Key Terms
قبلة (qibla): The direction (towards the Ka'bah) that one must face during prayer.
اجتهاد (ijtihad): Exerting one's effort to determine the correct qibla through reasoning and available signs.
تحري (taharri): Seeking the correct direction by using signs and personal judgment; synonymous with ijtihad in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person performs ijtihad to determine the qibla, prays, and later realizes he prayed in the wrong direction, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) He must repeat the prayer.
B) His prayer is valid and no repetition is required.
C) He must repeat only if the error was more than 90 degrees.
D) He must repeat but without recitation.

Key Takeaway
Prayer after ijtihad for qibla is valid even if mistaken, because the obligation is to do one's utmost (ijtihad), not to attain certainty.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Follower of a Shafi'i Imam Who Turns from Qibla
Discusses Hanafi position on follower repeating prayer when Shafi'i imam faces away from qibla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether a follower must repeat prayer when his imam errs in qibla direction, and explain the rationale based on the follower's capability and absence of a hadith command.

Core Idea
A follower is not liable for the imam's error if he prayed to his utmost ability.

When a person prays behind an imam from another madhhab, differences in rulings on validity can arise. This passage discusses a scenario where a Shafi'i imam completely turns his back to the qibla, which in the Shafi'i school invalidates the prayer and requires repetition. The Hanafi school, however, holds that the follower who simply followed the imam in good faith does not need to repeat. Understanding this dispute highlights the Hanafi emphasis on individual capacity and the absence of explicit textual command.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: the follower does not repeat the prayer. Note the reason given: the follower only had that much capability (i.e., he followed the imam to the best of his ability).
The Hanafi position prioritises the follower's limited control over the imam's actions.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
The Shafi'i position holds that because the imam completely reversed direction (qibla behind his back), the prayer is invalid and must be repeated. The proof is based on the necessity of facing the qibla for validity.
The Shafi'i school considers facing the qibla a condition (shart) of the prayer.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response has two parts: (1) the follower did what he could, and (2) no hadith commands repetition in such a case. The implication is that the follower's prayer is valid because he acted according to his ability, and the burden of facing the qibla correctly falls on the imam, not the follower who is unaware.
This reflects the Hanafi legal maxim: 'al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir' (hardship brings ease).
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In a congregation where the imam is Shafi'i and errs in qibla direction, Shafi'i followers would need to repeat the prayer, but Hanafi followers would not. This difference matters in mixed-madhhab settings.
The tarjih (preferred view) in the Hanafi school is the stated position, as the text says 'we say' and rejects repetition.

Source Text

استدار الى القبلة و بنى عليها . ۱۲۸ كتاب الصلوة فائن امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر قبلہ بالکل پشت کے پیچھے ہو گیا تو چونکہ کمل الٹا ہو گیا اس لئے نماز لوٹائے گا۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ اس کی طاقت میں اتنا ہی تھا اس لئے نہیں لوٹائے گا۔ پھر حدیث میں بھی لوٹانے کا حکم نہیں ہے۔
He turned towards the qibla and built upon it. 128 Kitab al-Salah. If the imam is Shafi'i and says if the qibla is completely behind his back, then since he has completely reversed, he will repeat the prayer. We say that he only had that much capability, so he will not repeat. Moreover, the hadith does not command repetition.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding a follower who prays behind a Shafi'i imam who inadvertently turns his back completely to the qibla. The Shafi'i position is that the prayer is invalid due to complete reversal, thus must be repeated. The Hanafi position, stated by the author, is that the follower is not required to repeat because he performed the prayer to the best of his ability given the circumstances. Additionally, the Hanafis argue that there is no command in the hadith to repeat in such a case. This reflects the Hanafi principle of considering intention and effort.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a follower prays behind a Shafi'i imam who completely turns his back to the qibla, what should the follower do?
A) Repeat the prayer because the imam's prayer is invalid.
B) Not repeat because the follower did what he could.
C) Repeat only if the imam was aware of the error.
D) Repeat both the follower and the imam's prayers.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not require a follower to repeat prayer if his imam errs in qibla direction, as long as the follower prayed to the best of his ability.

The Six Fara'id of Salah and Their Proofs
Lists the six obligatory elements of prayer with Quranic and Hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six obligatory elements of salah according to the Hanafi school and identify the scriptural proof for each.

Core Idea
The six fara'id of salah are the structural necessities established by Quran and Hadith.

The foundation of salah rests on six obligatory acts (fara'id). Without any one of them, the prayer is invalid. This lesson presents each fard with its direct evidence from the Quran or Sunnah, allowing you to understand the scriptural basis for the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six fara'id
List the six obligatory acts as stated in the passage: tahrimah, qiyam, qira'ah, ruku', sujud, and qa'dah akhirah (final sitting to the extent of tashahhud).
2
Locate the proof for each
For each fard, find the Quranic verse or hadith cited. For example, tahrimah is proven by 'And your Lord magnify' (74:3) and the hadith from Abu Sa'id.
3
Understand the distinction between fard and wajib in the final sitting
Note that sitting for the duration of tashahhud is fard, but reciting tashahhud itself is wajib. This is a key Hanafi nuance.
4
Recognize cross-madhhab differences
While Hanafis classify these as fard, other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider some as arkan (pillars) with slightly different definitions, but the list is largely agreed upon.

سورۃ الحج ۲۲) اور واقیموا : الصلوة وآتو الزكوة واركعوا مع الراكعين (ه) (آیت ۴۳ سورة البقرة ٢) [۱۷۶] (۶) اور قعدہ اخیرہ تشہد کی مقدار ( فرض ہے) تخری تشہد پڑھنا تو واجب ہے لیکن تشہد کی مقدار قعدہ اخیرہ میں بیٹھنا فرض ہے۔ حاشیہ : آپ نے فرمایا نماز شروع کرنے کی چیز پاکی ہے۔ اور اس کا تحریمہ باندھنا تکبیر کہنا ہے اور نماز کو کھولنا سلام کرتا ہے اور اس کی نماز ہی مکمل نہیں ہوئی جس نے الحمد اور سورۃ نہیں پڑھی فرض نماز میں ہو یا اس کے علاوہ میں (ب ) اللہ کے لئے خاموشی کے ساتھ کھڑے رہو ( ج ) قرآن سے جتنا آسان ہو پڑھو اور نماز قائم کرو اور زکوۃ دو ( د ) اے ایمان والور کوع کرو سجدہ کرو اور اپنے رب کی عبادت کرو (و) نماز قائم کرو، زکوۃ دو اور رکوع کرنے والوں کے ساتھ رکوع کرو۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri Vol. 1, p.129, Kitab al-Salah. Bab Sifat al-Salah. [1] The obligatory acts of prayer are six: the tahrimah [12], and standing [173], and recitation 13, and bowing 175, and prostration [16], and the final sitting to the extent of tashahhud. Necessary note: Sifat al-Salah means the form of prayer: how to perform prayer and what is in it. [17] (1) The fara'id of prayer are six: (1) Tahrimah. The proof of tahrimah is this verse: 'And your Lord magnify' (Surah al-Muddaththir, verse 3) (2) In hadith: from Abu Sa'id, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The key to prayer is purification, its tahrim is takbir, and its tahlil is taslim, and no prayer is valid for one who does not recite al-Hamd and a surah in an obligatory prayer or otherwise' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi tahrim al-salah wa tahliliha, p.55 no.238; Abu Dawud, Bab al-imam yuhdithu ba'da ma yarfa'u ra'sahu min akhri rak'ah, p.98 no.618). From this hadith it is known that for beginning prayer, it is fard to say the tahrimah. In the verse: 'And mention the name of his Lord and pray' (Surah al-A'la, verse 15). From this verse also the tahrimah is established, because by 'dhikr' here is meant the takbir of tahrimah. (172) (2) Standing. The proof of standing is this verse: 'And stand before Allah with devotion' (Surah al-Baqarah, verse 238). From this verse, standing in prayer is fard. (173) (3) Recitation is fard: 'So recite what is easy of it, and establish prayer and give zakah' (Surah al-Muzzammil, verse 20). From this verse it is known that recitation in prayer is fard. (2) Also from the above hadith it is known that recitation is fard. (174) (4) Bowing is fard. [175] (5) Prostration is fard. The proof of both is this verse: 'O you who believe, bow and prostrate and worship your Lord' (Surah al-Hajj, verse 77) and 'Establish prayer, give zakah, and bow with those who bow' (Surah al-Baqarah, verse 43). [176] (6) And the final sitting to the extent of tashahhud is fard. (Note: Reciting tashahhud is wajib, but sitting to the extent of tashahhud in the final sitting is fard.) Footnote: He said: The thing that begins prayer is purification, and its tahrim is saying takbir, and its tahlil is saying salam, and his prayer is not complete who does not recite al-Hamd and a surah, whether in obligatory prayer or otherwise. (b) Stand before Allah with devotion. (j) Recite what is easy of it, establish prayer, and give zakah. (d) O believers, bow and prostrate and worship your Lord. (w) Establish prayer, give zakah, and bow with those who bow.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, a Hanafi commentary, presents the six obligatory elements (fara'id) of salah with their scriptural proofs. The author begins by defining 'sifat al-salah' as the manner of performing prayer. Then lists each fard: 1) Tahrimah (the opening takbir) supported by Quran (Surah al-Muddaththir) and Hadith (from Abu Sa'id that the key to prayer is purification, its tahrim is takbir). 2) Qiyam (standing) from Surah al-Baqarah 238. 3) Qira'ah (recitation) from Surah al-Muzzammil 20 and the Hadith. 4) Ruku' (bowing) and 5) Sujud (prostration) from Surah al-Hajj 77 and Surah al-Baqarah 43. 6) The final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) to the extent of tashahhud is fard, but recitation of tashahhud itself is wajib. The footnote reiterates the hadith. Each ruling is backed by primary textual evidence, consistent with Hanafi methodology.

Key Terms
تحریمہ (tahrimah): The opening takbir (saying Allahu Akbar) that begins the prayer.
قیام (qiyam): Standing upright during prayer.
قراءة (qira'ah): Recitation of Quran in prayer.
رکوع (ruku'): Bowing from the waist in prayer.
سجود (sujud): Prostration with forehead on the ground.
قعدة اخیرہ (qa'dah akhirah): The final sitting at the end of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the six fara'id of salah according to the Hanafi school as listed in this passage?
A) Tahrimah
B) Qiyam
C) Taslim (salutation)
D) Qira'ah

Key Takeaway
The six fara'id of salah — tahrimah, qiyam, qira'ah, ruku', sujud, and qa'dah akhirah — are obligatory upon every Muslim in every prayer, established by Quran and Hadith.

Salah — Prayer

The Six Obligatory Acts of Prayer: Fara'id with Proofs
Lists and proves the six obligatory acts of prayer with textual evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six fara'id of prayer and prove each with textual evidence from the Quran and Hadith.

Core Idea
Six acts are fard in prayer; omitting any invalidates it. Each is proven by a direct command.

This lesson dives into the six obligatory acts (fara'id) of prayer according to the Hanafi school. These acts are not merely recommended but essential—if any one is left out, the prayer does not count. The author provides clear proofs from the Quran and Sunnah for each one, showing how Hanafi jurists derive rulings from texts. Understanding these fara'id is foundational for every Muslim's prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six acts
List the six fara'id as mentioned in the matn: tahrimah, qiyam, qira'ah, ruku', sujud, and qa'dah akhirah.
2
Locate the proof for each act
For each fard, find the specific evidence cited from the Quran or Hadith. Note the references provided (e.g., Quran 74:3 for tahrimah, 2:238 for qiyam, etc.).
3
Understand the Hanafi istidlal
See how imperative verbs in the verses (e.g., 'magnify', 'stand', 'recite') are used by Hanafis to indicate obligation (wujub) per the principle 'al-amr yufidu al-wujub'.
This is a key usul point: a command without a permissive context implies obligation.
4
Distinguish fard from wajib
Note that the tashahhud recitation itself is classified as wajib (not fard), while sitting to its extent is fard. Understand the Hanafi distinction: fard omission nullifies prayer; wajib omission requires compensation (sajdah sahw) but does not invalidate.
This nuance is essential for correct fatwa.
5
Appreciate cross-madhhab differences
Observe that the last sitting (qa'dah akhirah) is fard for Hanafis but a rukn for Shafi'is. The practical difference is minimal (both require it), but the underlying proof structure differs.
These differences stem from variant usul methodologies.

سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ قعدہ اخیرہ فرض ہے۔
The obligatory acts of prayer are six: the opening takbir (tahrimah), standing (qiyam), recitation (qira'ah), bowing (ruku'), prostration (sujud), and the last sitting to the extent of tashahhud. (1) The prayer's obligatory acts are six: (1) Tahrimah. Its proof is the verse 'And magnify your Lord' (Surah al-Muddaththir 74:3). (2) In hadith: from Abu Sa'id that the Prophet said: 'The key to prayer is purification, its tahrimah is the takbir, its tahlil is the taslim, and there is no prayer for one who does not recite al-Hamd and a surah in an obligatory prayer or otherwise.' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud). From this hadith it is known that binding the tahrimah to start prayer is obligatory. Also in the verse 'And mention the name of his Lord and pray' (Surah al-A'la 87:15), this also proves tahrimah because the mention refers to the takbir of tahrimah. (2) Standing. Its proof is the verse 'And stand before Allah devoutly' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:238). From this verse, standing in prayer is obligatory. (3) Recitation is obligatory: 'So recite what is easy from it, and establish prayer and give zakah' (Surah al-Muzzammil 73:20). From this verse it is known that recitation in prayer is obligatory (2) Also from the previous hadith it is known that recitation is obligatory. (4) Bowing is obligatory. (5) Prostration is obligatory. Their proof is the verse 'O you who have believed, bow and prostrate and worship your Lord' (Surah al-Hajj 22:77) and 'Establish prayer and give zakah and bow with those who bow' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:43). (6) And the last sitting to the extent of tashahhud is obligatory. Tashahhud recitation is wajib, but sitting in the last sitting to the extent of tashahhud is fard. Footnote: ... (1) This is the hadith of the companion who performed prayer hastily and came to the Prophet three times; the Prophet taught him the method of prayer. At the end of the hadith, the Prophet emphasized four actions. Three of these are fard because of verses, so the fourth must also be fard. In the hadith: from Rifa'ah ibn Rafi', that the Prophet, while sitting in the mosque one day, said: 'If you have some Quran, recite it; otherwise praise Allah, magnify Him, and declare His oneness. Then bow with tranquility, then stand up straight, then prostrate with tranquility, then sit with tranquility, then stand. When you have done that, your prayer is complete, and if you omit anything from it, you have deducted from your prayer.' (Tirmidhi). In this hadith, (1) recitation, (2) bowing, (3) prostration, and (4) sitting for tashahhud are commanded. Then it says that if any of these is deficient, the prayer is deficient. This means that if the last sitting is deficient, the prayer is deficient. So the last sitting to the extent of tashahhud is fard. (2) In the same chapter of Tirmidhi, from Abu Hurairah, the phrase 'then raise until you sit with tranquility and do that in all your prayers' (Tirmidhi). This also shows that sitting in the last sitting is fard. (3) In Abu Dawud, from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, the Prophet took his hand and taught him the tashahhud in prayer, then said: 'When you say this or complete this, you have completed your prayer. If you wish to stand, stand; if you wish to sit, sit.' (Abu Dawud). This also shows that sitting to the extent of tashahhud completes the prayer otherwise not. (4) The Prophet never performed any prayer without sitting to the extent of tashahhud. This indicates that sitting to the extent of tashahhud is fard. (5) From Ibn Umar, the Prophet said: 'When the Imam completes the prayer and sits, then has an event before speaking, his prayer is complete, and those behind him who have completed the prayer are also complete.' (Abu Dawud). This also shows that the last sitting is fard.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (hukm wa dalil) from the commentary on the matn of the six obligatory acts of prayer. The author lists the six fara'id: the opening takbir (tahrimah), standing (qiyam), recitation (qira'ah), bowing (ruku'), prostration (sujud), and the last sitting to the extent of the tashahhud (qa'dah akhirah). For each, he provides textual evidence from the Quran and Hadith. The tahrimah is proven by the command to magnify Allah and by the hadith that the key to prayer is purification, its tahrimah is the takbir, and its tahlil is the taslim. Standing is proven by the command 'Stand before Allah devoutly.' Recitation is proven by the command to recite what is easy of the Quran. Bowing and prostration are proven by the verses commanding bowing and prostration. The last sitting is proven by multiple ahadith, including the hadith of the one who prayed hastily, which emphasizes four actions: recitation, bowing, prostration, and sitting; and the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that tashahhud completes the prayer. The author also notes that while reciting the tashahhud itself is wajib, sitting for its duration is fard. The textual evidence establishes these six as fard, meaning their omission invalidates the prayer. The commentary follows the order of the matn, explaining each proof.

Key Terms
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir (saying Allahu Akbar) that begins the prayer, making what was halal (e.g., eating, speaking) haram until the prayer ends.
قعدة أخيرة (qa'dah akhirah): The last sitting in prayer after the second sujud of the final rakah, to the extent of reciting the tashahhud.
تشهد (tashahhud): The testimony recited while sitting: 'at-tahiyyatu lillahi...'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is NOT one of the six obligatory acts (fara'id) of prayer?
A) The opening takbir (tahrimah)
B) Standing (qiyam)
C) Recitation of the tasbih in ruku'
D) The last sitting to the extent of tashahhud

Key Takeaway
The six fara'id of prayer are essential acts proven by Quran and Sunnah; omission of any one invalidates the prayer, and the last sitting is fard, not the tashahhud recitation.
