Why the Author Calls Non-Fard Acts 'Sunnah' – A Terminological Clarification
Definitional ruling: clarifies the scope of the term 'Sunnah' for acts beyond the six fara'id.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school categorizes acts beyond the six fara'id of prayer as 'Sunnah' and distinguish between the broad and technical meanings of the term.

Core Idea
Acts proven by the Sunnah are called 'Sunnah' even if they carry the legal weight of wajib—terminology follows the proof source.

You have learned the six fara'id of prayer; now the author states that every other action is 'Sunnah'. But is tashahhud really just a sunnah? The commentator clarifies that the author uses 'Sunnah' broadly to indicate the source (Prophetic practice) rather than the legal obligation level. This lesson unpacks this important terminological distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six fara'id
Recall the six fara'id of prayer (intention, takbir, qiyam, recitation, ruku, sujud). The passage refers to 'what is beyond that'.
2
Note the author's blanket term
The author states 'وما زاد على ذلك فهو سنة' – 'And what is beyond that is Sunnah.' Recognize that he groups all non-fard acts under one term.
This is a definitional choice.
3
Read the commentator's clarification
The commentator says that some of these acts are actually wajib (e.g., tashahhud). The author calls them Sunnah because they are proven by the Sunnah (Prophetic practice), not because they are optional.
The commentator corrects a potential misunderstanding.
4
Understand the rationale
In Hanafi usul, the term 'Sunnah' can be used broadly for any act established by the Prophet's practice, regardless of its legal weight (wajib or sunnah proper).
This contrasts with the technical usage where sunnah is less than wajib.
5
Apply the Hanafi hierarchy
Classify the six fara'id as fard (Quran/mutawatir). Acts beyond them: some are wajib (ahad hadith), some are sunnah muakkadah, some are ghayr muakkadah. The passage simplifies by calling all 'Sunnah'.
Mufta bihi (operative) position: the six fara'id are fard; tashahhud is wajib; reciting a surah after Fatiha is sunnah muakkadah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما زاد على ذلك فهو سنة.
مصنف نے ان کے علاوہ کو سنت کہا ہے حالانکہ نماز میں کچھ چیزیں واجب بھی ہیں۔ لیکن سب کو سنت اس لئے کہا کہ وہ سنت اور
And what is beyond that is Sunnah. The author called everything other than these (the six fara'id) Sunnah, even though in prayer there are some wajib things. But he called them all Sunnah because they are from the Sunnah and...
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This is a definitional ruling from the commentary. After listing the six fara'id of prayer, the author states that every other action in prayer is 'Sunnah'. The commentator clarifies that the author uses 'Sunnah' in a broad sense, meaning that these acts are proven by the Sunnah (the Prophet's practice). However, some of these acts are technically wajib (obligatory but not fard), such as reciting tashahhud or performing sajdah sahw. The author's terminology groups them as 'Sunnah' to contrast them with the six fara'id, which are established by Quran or mutawatir reports. This does not mean they are optional; rather, their authority comes primarily from the Sunnah, not from the Quran or ijma. In Hanafi fiqh, acts in prayer are categorized as fard, wajib, sunnah, and mustahabb. The text here simplifies by calling all non-fard acts 'Sunnah', but the sharh clarifies that some are wajib.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): In this context, 'sunnah' refers to acts proven by the Prophet's practice (Sunnah) that are not fard. These include both wajib and sunnah proper.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author call acts beyond the six fara'id 'Sunnah' even though some are wajib?
A) He is only mentioning the six fara'id and ignoring the others
B) He uses 'Sunnah' broadly because these acts are established by the Sunnah, not by explicit Quranic verses
C) He made a mistake and later corrected it
D) Wajib and sunnah are the same in his view

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the term 'Sunnah' in classical texts can encompass acts that are technically wajib, so students must verify the specific ruling of each non-fard act.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Final Sitting (Qad'ah Akhirah) is Fard: Proofs from Hadith
Establishes that the final sitting for tashahhud is obligatory (fard) with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the final sitting (qad'ah akhirah) for tashahhud is fard, list the five hadith proofs, and distinguish between fard, wajib, and sunnah in the context of salah.

Core Idea
The final sitting is a pillar (fard) of salah; omitting it invalidates the entire prayer.

In this passage, the Hanafi school defends the position that the final sitting (qad'ah akhirah) is not merely recommended but an obligatory pillar (fard) of salah. The author marshals five hadith proofs, including the famous instruction of the Prophet to a companion who prayed hastily. Understanding this ruling is essential for every Muslim, as it directly affects the validity of one's daily prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in dispute
The passage argues that the final sitting (qad'ah akhirah) for tashahhud is fard. Some other schools consider it sunnah or wajib. The Hanafi position is that it is a rukn (pillar).
Hanafi: fard = rukn; omission invalidates.
2
Examine the first hadith proof (Rifa'ah ibn Rafi')
The hadith lists four actions: recitation, bowing, prostration, and sitting. The Prophet says if any is omitted, the prayer is diminished. Since three are fard by Quranic evidence, the fourth (sitting) must also be fard.
Key phrase: 'If you do that, your prayer is complete; if you omit something, it is diminished.'
3
Analyze additional hadiths
Three more hadiths are cited: Abu Hurayrah's hadith commanding sitting with tranquility, Ibn Mas'ud's hadith linking tashahhud to completing the prayer, and Ibn Umar's hadith about the imam's prayer being valid after sitting. The Prophet's constant practice also proves it.
Each hadith reinforces the obligatory nature of sitting.
4
Understand the distinction: fard, wajib, sunnah
The matn states 'what is more than that is sunnah.' The commentary clarifies that this refers to extra recitations, not the sitting itself. The author then lists eight wajibat in prayer (e.g., reciting Fatihah, first sitting, qunut) that are obligatory but not fard.
Hanafi: fard = qat'i dalil; wajib = zanni dalil; omission of wajib requires sujud al-sahw.
5
Apply the ruling to one's own salah
Ensure you sit for at least the duration of tashahhud in the final sitting. If you forget and stand up, you must perform sujud al-sahw. If you deliberately omit it, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
Practical takeaway.

Source Text

التشهد [۱۷۷ (۷) وما زاد على ذلك فهو سنة.
(۱) یہ حدیث ہے وہ صحابی جس نے نماز جلدی جلدی پوری کی اور تین مرتبہ حضور کی خدمت میں آئے ان کو آپ نے نماز پڑھنے کا طریقہ بتایا۔ اس حدیث کے آخر میں آپ نے چار کام کرنے پر زور دیا ہے۔ ان میں سے تین کام تو آیت کی وجہ سے فرض ہیں۔ اس لئے چوتھا کام بھی فرض ہی ہونا چاہئے ۔ حدیث میں ہے عن رفاعة بن رافع ان رسول الله الا الله بينما هو جالس في المسجد يوما ... فان كان كان معك قرآن فاقرء والا فاحمد الله وكبره وهلله ثم اركع فاطمئن راكعا ثم اعتدل قائما ثم اسجد فاعتدل ساجدا ثم اجلس فاطمئن جالسا ثم قم فاذا فعلت ذلك فقد تمت صلوتک وان انتقضت منه شيئا انتقضت من صلوتک (الف) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی وصف الصلوۃ ص ۶۶ نمبر ۳۰۲) اس حدیث میں (۱) قرات (۲) رکوع (۳) سجدہ (۴) اور تشہد میں بیٹھنے کے لئے کہا گیا ہے۔ پھر یہ بھی کہا کہ ان میں سے کسی چیز کی کمی رہ گئی تو تمہاری نماز میں کمی رہ گئی۔ اس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ قعدہ اخیرہ میں کمی رہ گئی تو نماز میں کمی رہ گئی تو نماز میں کمی رہ جائے گی۔ اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ قعدہ اخیرہ تشہد کی مقدار فرض ہے (۲) ترمذی کے اسی باب میں حضرت ابو ہریرہ کی حدیث ہے جس کے اخیر میں یہ جملہ ہے ثم ارفع حتى تـطـمـئـن جـالـسـا وافعل ذلك في صلوتک کلما (ب) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء وصف الصلوۃ ص ۶۷ نمبر ۳۰۳) اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ قعدہ اخیرہ میں بیٹھنا فرض ہے(۳) ابوداؤد میں عبداللہ بن مسعود کی حدیث ہے وان رسول الله الله اخذ بيد عبد الله بن مسعود فعلمه التشهد في الصلوة فذكر مثل دعاء حديث الاعمش اذا قلت هذا او قضيت هذا فقد قضيت صلوتک إن شئت ان تقوم فقم وان شنت ان تقعد فاقعد (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب التشهد ص ۱۴۶ نمبر ۹۷) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھے گا تو نماز پوری ہوگی ورنہ نہیں (۴) آپ نے کوئی بھی نماز بغیر تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھے ہوئے پوری نہیں کی ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنا فرض ہے (۵) عن ابن عمر ان رسول الله الله الله قال اذا قضى الامام الصلوة وقعد فاحدث قبل ان يتكلم فقد تمت صلوته ومن كان خلفه ممن اتم الصلوة (و) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الامام محدث بعد ما یرفع راسہ ص ۹۸ نمبر ۶۱۷) اس سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ قعدہ اخیرہ فرض ہے۔
[۱۷۷] (۷) اور جوان سے زیادہ ہو وہ سنت ہے۔
مصنف نے ان کے علاوہ کو سنت کہا ہے حالانکہ نماز میں کچھ چیزیں واجب بھی ہیں۔ لیکن سب کو سنت اس لئے کہا کہ وہ سنت اور
حاشیہ : (الف) حضور مسجد میں ایک دن بیٹھے ہوئے تھے . آپ نے فرمایا کہ اگر تمہارے پاس کچھ قرآن ہو تو اس کو پڑھو ورنہ اللہ کی تحمید کروہ تکبیر کرو اور تہلیل کرو۔ پھر اطمینان سے رکوع کرو پھر پورے کھڑے ہو جاؤ پھر سجدہ کرو اور پورے اطمینان سے سجدہ کرو۔ پھر بیٹھ جاؤ اور پورے اطمینان سے بیٹھو پھر کھڑے ہو جاؤ۔ پس جب تم نے اتنا کیا تو نماز پوری کر لی اور ان میں سے کچھ کمی رہ گئی تو نماز میں کمی رہ گئی (ب) پھر سر سجدے سے اٹھا ئیں یہاں تک کہ اطمینان سے بیٹھ جائیں اور یہ چیزیں اپنی تمام نمازوں میں کریں (ج) آپ نے عبداللہ بن مسعود کا ہاتھ پکڑا پھر ان کو نماز کی تشہد سکھلائی (پس حضرت اعمش کی حدیث کی طرح دعا کا ذکر کیا) پھر آپ نے فرمایا جب تم نے تشہد کہ لیایا ادا کرلیا تو اپنی نماز پوری کر لی۔ اس لئے اگر اٹھنا چاہیں تو اٹھ جائیں اور اگر بیٹھنا چاہیں تو بیٹھ جائیں (د) آپ نے
فرمایا اگر امام نے نماز پوری کر لی اور بیٹھ گیا پھر بات کرنے سے پہلے حدث ہو گیا تو اس کی نماز پوری ہوگئی۔ اور جو اس کے پیچھے ہیں ان کی نماز بھی پوری ہوگئی۔

حدیث سے ثابت ہیں۔ اس لئے ان کو سنت کہا ہے۔ ورنہ اس میں کچھ واجبات بھی ہیں۔ مثلا (۱) قرأت فاتحه (۲) سورۃ ملانا (۳) مکررا فعال میں ترتیب کی رعایت رکھنا (۴) قعدہ اولی (۵) قعدہ اخیرہ میں تشہد پڑھنا (4) جن رکعتوں میں قرآت جہری ہے اس کو جہری پڑھنا اور جن
رکعتوں میں سری ہے اس کو سری پڑھنا ( ۷ ) وتر میں دعائے قنوت پڑھنا (۸) تکبیرات عیدین ، یہ سب واجبات ہیں۔
The tashahhud [177 (7)] and whatever is more than that is sunnah. (1) This is a hadith: a companion who performed prayer hastily and came to the Prophet three times; the Prophet taught him the method of prayer. At the end of the hadith, the Prophet emphasized four actions. Three of these are fard because of a verse, so the fourth must also be fard. In the hadith: from Rifa'ah ibn Rafi' that the Messenger of Allah... 'If you have some Qur'an, recite; otherwise, praise Allah, glorify Him, and say La ilaha illa Allah. Then bow with tranquility, then stand up straight, then prostrate with tranquility, then sit with tranquility, then stand. If you do that, your prayer is complete, and if you omit something, your prayer is diminished.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi wasf al-salat, p. 66 no. 302). In this hadith, (1) recitation, (2) bowing, (3) prostration, and (4) sitting for tashahhud are commanded. Then it is said that if any of these is lacking, the prayer is diminished. This means that if the final sitting is lacking, the prayer is diminished, so the final sitting to the extent of tashahhud is fard. (2) In the same chapter of Tirmidhi, the hadith of Abu Hurayrah ends with: 'Then raise your head until you sit with tranquility, and do that in all your prayers.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi wasf al-salat, p. 67 no. 303). This also shows that sitting in the final sitting is fard. (3) In Abu Dawud, the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: 'The Messenger of Allah took Abdullah ibn Mas'ud's hand and taught him the tashahhud in prayer... when you say this or complete this, you have completed your prayer. If you wish to stand, stand; if you wish to sit, sit.' (Abu Dawud, Bab al-tashahhud, p. 146 no. 97). This also shows that if one sits to the extent of tashahhud, the prayer is complete, otherwise not. (4) The Prophet never completed any prayer without sitting for the extent of tashahhud. This shows that sitting to the extent of tashahhud is fard. (5) From Ibn Umar: The Messenger of Allah said, 'When the imam completes the prayer and sits, then he becomes impure before speaking, his prayer is complete, and those behind him who completed the prayer also.' (Abu Dawud, Bab al-imam muhdith ba'd ma yarfa' rasahu, p. 98 no. 617). This also shows that the final sitting is fard. [177] (7) And whatever is more than that is sunnah. The author called other things sunnah, although there are some wajibat in prayer. But he called them all sunnah because they are proven by sunnah and hadith. So he called them sunnah. Otherwise, among them there are some wajibat, for example: (1) reciting Fatihah, (2) adding a surah, (3) maintaining order in repeated actions, (4) the first sitting, (5) reciting tashahhud in the final sitting, (6) reciting aloud in loud prayers and silently in silent prayers, (7) reciting qunut in witr, (8) the takbirs of Eid. All these are wajib.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from multiple hadiths establishing that the final sitting (qad'ah akhirah) for the recitation of tashahhud is obligatory (fard) in the Hanafi school. The author begins by referencing the matn that the tashahhud and what exceeds it is sunnah, but then the commentary argues that the final sitting itself is fard. Five proofs are presented: (1) The hadith of Rifa'ah ibn Rafi' where the Prophet commands four actions including sitting, saying that if any is omitted the prayer is diminished. (2) The hadith of Abu Hurayrah commanding sitting with tranquility. (3) The hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud teaching tashahhud and stating that completing it completes the prayer. (4) The constant practice of the Prophet never praying without sitting for tashahhud. (5) The hadith of Ibn Umar about the imam's prayer being valid if he sits and then becomes impure, implying the final sitting is essential. Then the author explains that the matn's statement 'what is more is sunnah' refers to extra recitations, but the author lists several wajibat that are not fard but still obligatory, such as reciting Fatihah, adding a surah, maintaining order, the first sitting, reciting tashahhud in the final sitting, loud/silent recitation in appropriate places, qunut in witr, and the takbirs of Eid. These are all wajib, not sunnah, in the Hanafi school. The commentary clarifies that the author of the matn called them sunnah because they are proven by sunnah texts, but the Hanafi school distinguishes between fard, wajib, and sunnah.

Key Terms
قعدہ اخیرہ (qad'ah akhirah): The final sitting in salah after completing the last sajdah, where tashahhud is recited.
تشہد (tashahhud): The specific supplication recited in the final sitting (and first sitting) of salah, bearing witness to the oneness of Allah and the prophethood of Muhammad.
فرض (fard): An obligation established by definitive evidence (Quran, mutawatir sunnah, ijma). Its omission invalidates the act.
واجب (wajib): An obligation established by speculative evidence (ahad hadith, qiyas). Its omission requires compensation but does not invalidate the act.
سنت (sunnah): Recommended actions proven by the Prophet's practice. Omission is not sinful but disliked if habitual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the final sitting (qad'ah akhirah) for tashahhud?
A) It is sunnah and not obligatory.
B) It is fard (obligatory) and its omission invalidates the prayer.
C) It is wajib and requires sujud al-sahw if omitted.
D) It is recommended but not stressed.

Key Takeaway
The final sitting for tashahhud is a fard (rukn) in the Hanafi school; its omission invalidates the prayer, and the distinction between fard, wajib, and sunnah is critical for understanding the consequences of omission.

Salah — Prayer

Takbir al-Tahrimah: Condition of Salah or Part of It?
Inter-madhhab dispute on takbir al-tahrimah as condition vs. part of salah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi position on takbir al-tahrimah as a condition from the Shafi'i view as a pillar, and explain the proof and practical consequence of this difference.

Core Idea
Takbir al-tahrimah is a condition for salah, not part of it.

This passage presents a key inter-madhhab dispute about the opening takbir. Understanding whether it is a condition (shart) or a part (juz') of salah clarifies how each school defines the beginning of the prayer and the implications for validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
Locate the act being discussed: saying takbir when entering salah. Identify that the core dispute is whether this takbir is a condition for salah or part of the prayer itself.
2
State the Hanafi position and its dalil
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that takbir is a condition (shart), not part of salah. His proof is the verse 'wadhkura isma rabbihi fasalla' which places remembrance before prayer.
This verse is cited in the source.
3
State the Shafi'i position and its dalil
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that takbir is a pillar (rukn) inside salah. His proof is the hadith 'tahrimuha al-takbir', which indicates the takbir marks the start of prayer.
The hadith is cited in the source.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the hadith 'tahrimuha al-takbir' means the prohibitory effect is achieved by the takbir, but the takbir itself is performed before entering the prayer proper.
The Hanafi school prioritizes the Quranic verse over the hadith in this case.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In the Hanafi school, forgetting the takbir entirely invalidates the prayer because a condition is missing. In the Shafi'i school, it also invalidates but because a pillar is omitted.
Both agree on invalidity but differ on the categorization.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸) واذا دخل الرجل في صلوته كبر [۱۷۹](۹) ورفع يديه مع التكبير حتى يحاذي بابهامیه شحمتی اذنيه
تحریمہ باندھتے وقت تکبیر کہے۔ کیونکہ آیت میں ہے وربک فکبر (آیت ۳ سورۃ المدثر ہے ) اس لئے تحریمہ کے ساتھ ہی تکبیر کہے۔ مسئلہ نمبرا میں حدیث گزری جس میں تھا و تحریمها التكبير اس حدیث سے بھی پتہ چلتا ہے کہ تحریمہ کے وقت تکبیر کہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک تکبیر داخل نماز نہیں ہے بلکہ وہ شرائط نماز میں سے ہے۔ کیونکہ آیت میں ہے وذكر اسم ربه فصلی (الف) (آیت ۱۵ سورۃ الاعلی ۱۸۷) اس آیت میں کہا گیا ہے کہ اللہ کا ذکر کرو پھر نماز پڑھو۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ ذکر پہلے ہو گا تکبیر پہلے ہوگی پھر نماز ہوگی۔ فا امام شافعی کے نزدیک وہ داخل نماز اور فرائض نماز میں سے ہے۔ اس لئے ان کے تمام شرائط وہی ہیں جو نماز کے لئے ہیں۔

تکبیر کہنے کے ساتھ دونوں ہاتھوں کو اتنا اٹھائے یہاں تک کہ دونوں انگوٹھوں کو کان کی لو کے مد مقابل کر دے۔ تکبیر کہنے کے ساتھ دونوں ہاتھوں کو اتنا اٹھائے کہ دونوں انگوٹھے کان کی لو کے برابر ہو جائے۔
حدیث میں دونوں طریقہ ہیں یعنی پہلے ہاتھ اٹھائے پھر تکبیر کہے اور یہ بھی ہے کہ پہلے تکبیر کہے پھر ہاتھ اٹھائے ۔ حنفیہ کے نزدیک بہتر یہ ہے کہ پہلے ہاتھ اٹھائے تا کہ عمل سے بھی اللہ کے علاوہ کا انکار ہو جائے پھر تکبیر کہے تا کہ اللہ کی وحدانیت کا اقرار ہو جائے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ان ابن عمر قال كان رسول الله الله الله اذا قام للصلوة رفع يديه حتى تكونا حذو منكبيه ثم كبر (ب) مسلم شریف، باب رفع اليدين حذوا المنكبين مع تکبیرة الاحرام ص ۱۶۸ نمبر ۳۹۰ ابو داؤد شریف ، باب رفع الیدین ص ۱۱ نمبر ۷۲۲ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ پہلے ہاتھ اٹھائے پھر تکبیر کہے تو بہتر ہے۔ اور اگر پہلے تکبیر کہے پھر ہاتھ اٹھائے تب بھی کچھ حرج نہیں ہے۔ حدیث میں اس کا بھی ذکر ہے۔ انه رأی مالک بن الحویرث اذا صلى كبر ثم رفع يديه .... وحدث ان رسول الله له كان يفعل هكذا (مسلم شریف، باب رفع الیدین حذو منكبين مع تكبيرة الاحرامص ۶۸ نمبر ۳۹ ابوداؤد شریف ، باب رفع الیدین فی الصلوة ص ۱۱ نمبر ۷۲۶ ) اس حدیث میں پہلے تکبیر کہی پھر ہاتھ اٹھائے۔ ہاتھ کان کی لو تک اٹھائے اس طرح کہ انگلیاں کان کی لو کے مد مقابل ہوں اور باقی ہاتھ گلے اور مونڈھے کے قریب ہوتا کہ تمام احادیث پر عمل ہو جائے ۔ کان کی لو تک انگلیاں رکھنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن مالک بن الحوريث ان رسول الله الا الله كان اذا كبر رفع حاشیہ : (الف) اپنے رب کا نام ذکر کرو پھر نماز پڑھو ( ب ) آپ جب نماز کے لئے کھڑے ہوتے تو دونوں ہاتھوں کو مونڈھے کے برابر اٹھاتے پھر تکبیر کہتے ۔
(8) When a man enters his prayer, he says takbir. (9) He raises his hands with the takbir until his thumbs align with the lobes of his ears. He says takbir when binding the tahrimah. Because the verse says: 'And your Lord magnify' (Surah al-Muddaththir, verse 3). So he says takbir with the tahrimah. In the earlier issue, a hadith passed which said 'and its tahrimah is the takbir'. From this hadith it is also known that he says takbir at the time of tahrimah. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the takbir is not part of the prayer, but rather from the conditions of prayer. Because the verse says: 'And mention the name of his Lord and pray' (Surah al-A'la, verse 15). In this verse, it is said: remember Allah, then pray. Its meaning is that the remembrance comes first; the takbir comes first, then the prayer comes. According to Imam Shafi'i, it is part of the prayer and from the obligations of prayer. Therefore, all conditions for it are the same as for the prayer. He raises his hands with the takbir so that his thumbs become opposite the lobes of his ears. He raises both hands so that both thumbs become level with the earlobes. In the hadith, both methods are found: he raised his hands first, then said takbir, and also he said takbir first, then raised hands. According to the Hanafis, it is better to raise hands first, so that by action one renounces anything other than Allah, then says takbir to affirm Allah's oneness. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'When the Messenger of Allah stood for prayer, he raised his hands until they were level with his shoulders, then he said takbir.' (Muslim, Bab raf' al-yadayn hidha' al-minkibayn ma'a takbirat al-ihram, p. 168 no. 390; Abu Dawud, Bab raf' al-yadayn, p. 11 no. 722). From this hadith, it is known that raising hands first then takbir is better. And if one says takbir first then raises hands, there is no harm. There is also mention of this in the hadith: 'He saw Malik ibn al-Huwayrith when he prayed, he said takbir then raised his hands... and he narrated that the Messenger of Allah used to do that.' (Muslim, Bab raf' al-yadayn hidha' al-minkibayn ma'a takbirat al-ihram, p. 68 no. 39; Abu Dawud, Bab raf' al-yadayn fi al-salah, p. 11 no. 726). In this hadith, he said takbir first then raised hands. He raises hands up to the earlobes so that the fingers are opposite the earlobes, and the rest of the hands are near the neck and shoulders, so that all hadiths are acted upon. The proof for placing fingers at the earlobes is this hadith from Malik ibn al-Huwayrith: 'The Messenger of Allah, when he said takbir, he raised...' (Footnote: (a) 'Mention the name of your Lord and pray.' (b) 'When the Messenger of Allah stood for prayer, he raised both hands to the level of his shoulders, then said takbir.')
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage covers two interrelated rulings about the start of salah: the takbir al-tahrimah and the raising of hands. First, it states that when beginning salah, one says takbir. This is proven by the Quranic command 'wa rabbaka fakabbir' and the hadith 'tahrimuha al-takbir'. Then it presents an inter-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam al-Shafi'i. Abu Hanifa considers the takbir a condition (shart) of salah, not part of the prayer itself, based on the verse 'wadhkura isma rabbihi fasalla' which orders remembrance of Allah before prayer. Imam Shafi'i holds that the takbir is part of the prayer and an obligatory component (fard). The Hanafi view is that the takbir is performed before the actual prayer begins, thus it is a condition for validity. The second part discusses the sunnah of raising hands (raf' al-yadayn) with the takbir. It details the preferred method: raising hands so that the thumbs are level with the earlobes, and the fingers are opposite the earlobes while the rest of the hands are near the neck and shoulders. It mentions that both orders are found in hadith: raising hands first then takbir, and takbir first then raising hands. The Hanafi preference is to raise hands first, to symbolically renounce everything other than Allah, then say takbir to affirm His oneness. The hadith of Ibn Umar is cited as evidence for this order. However, if one does the opposite, it is also permissible. The goal is to combine all authentic hadiths by allowing either order, but the preferred one is raising hands first.

Key Terms
تحریمہ (tahrimah): The opening takbir that prohibits worldly actions and enters one into the state of prayer.
تکبیر (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar'; specifically the opening takbir that initiates salah.
رفع الیدین (raf' al-yadayn): Raising both hands during the opening takbir as a sunnah practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the status of the opening takbir (takbir al-tahrimah) in relation to salah?
A) It is a pillar (rukn) of salah.
B) It is a condition (shart) of salah, not part of it.
C) It is an obligatory act (wajib) that requires sujud al-sahw if omitted.
D) It is a sunnah act that is recommended but not required.

Key Takeaway
The takbir al-tahrimah is a condition (shart) for salah in the Hanafi school, not a pillar (rukn).

Raising Hands (Raf' al-Yadayn) in Salah: Method and Preferable Order
Sunnah practice of raising hands during takbir al-tahrimah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi method of raising hands during the opening takbir and state the preferred order (hands first vs. takbir first) with evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Raising hands is sunnah; either order is valid, but hands first is preferred.

This passage details the sunnah practice of raising hands when beginning salah. It reconciles two authentic hadiths by allowing both sequences—hands first or takbir first—while clearly stating the Hanafi preference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah act
Recognize that raising hands (raf' al-yadayn) during the opening takbir is a sunnah, not fard or wajib. It is a recommended practice that enhances the prayer.
2
Note the method described
The text describes raising hands so that the thumbs are level with the earlobes, and the fingers are opposite the earlobes; the rest of the hands are near the neck and shoulders. This method combines multiple hadiths.
The source mentions raising until thumbs are opposite earlobes.
3
State the two orders found in hadith
Two authentic hadiths are presented: one showing the Prophet raised hands first then said takbir (Ibn Umar), and another showing he said takbir first then raised hands (Malik ibn al-Huwayrith).
Both orders are valid and found in Sahih Muslim and Abu Dawud.
4
Apply the Hanafi preference
The Hanafi school prefers raising hands first to symbolically renounce everything other than Allah, then saying takbir to affirm Allah's oneness. This is supported by the hadith of Ibn Umar where 'thumma' indicates sequence.
The preferred order is not obligatory; the opposite is permissible.
5
Determine the ruling on the opposite order
If one says takbir first and then raises hands, the salah is valid and there is no harm. The Hanafi school allows this based on the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith.
Flexibility ensures that all authentic hadiths are acted upon.

Source Text

The Eight Wajibat of Salah
Enumeration of the eight wajibat of salah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the eight wajibat of salah in the Hanafi school and explain the consequence of omitting a wajib.

Core Idea
Eight wajibat of salah: omission requires sajdah al-sahw or repetition; neither fard nor sunnah.

This passage enumerates the eight obligatory elements (wajibat) of salah according to the Hanafi school. Understanding these is crucial because their omission requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw) if done inadvertently, or repetition if deliberate. This lesson will help you internalize this core list and distinguish it from fard and sunnah actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Context
The passage distinguishes wajibat from sunnah. Note that the list is specifically for the Hanafi school; other schools may have different categorizations.
The phrasing 'they are established by hadith' indicates these are proven by ahad hadith, hence wajib not fard.
2
Memorize the List
The eight wajibat are: (1) Reciting Surah al-Fatihah, (2) Adding a surah after Fatihah, (3) Maintaining order in repeated actions, (4) The first sitting, (5) Reciting tashahhud in the last sitting, (6) Reciting aloud/silently as required, (7) Du'a al-qunut in Witr, (8) Takbirs of 'Eid prayer.
Note the OCR duplicate numbering; the list is eight items.
3
Understand the Consequence
If a wajib is omitted inadvertently, perform sajdah al-sahw. If omitted deliberately, the salah is valid but must be repeated (i.e., it is a sin).
This is different from omitting a fard, which invalidates the salah entirely.
4
Apply to Practice
When reviewing salah, check if any wajib was missed. For example, if you forget to recite a surah after Fatihah in the first two rak'ahs, you owe sajdah al-sahw.
Use this list as a checklist for praying correctly.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حدیث سے ثابت ہیں۔ اس لئے ان کو سنت کہا ہے۔ ورنہ اس میں کچھ واجبات بھی ہیں۔ مثلا (۱) قرأت فاتحه (۲) سورۃ ملانا (۳) مکررا فعال میں ترتیب کی رعایت رکھنا (۴) قعدہ اولی (۵) قعدہ اخیرہ میں تشہد پڑھنا (4) جن رکعتوں میں قرآت جہری ہے اس کو جہری پڑھنا اور جن رکعتوں میں سری ہے اس کو سری پڑھنا ( ۷ ) وتر میں دعائے قنوت پڑھنا (۸) تکبیرات عیدین ، یہ سب واجبات ہیں۔

All these are wajibat.

Commentary
This passage lists the eight wajibat of salah according to the Hanafi school. These are actions that are obligatory but not at the level of fard. If a wajib is omitted inadvertently, one must perform sajdah al-sahw. If omitted deliberately, the salah must be repeated. The passage states that these actions are established by hadith, but they are called sunnah generally; however, within them some are wajib. The list includes: recitation of Fatihah, adding a surah, order of actions, first sitting, tashahhud in last sitting, reciting aloud or silently as required, qunut in witr, and the takbirs of Eid prayer. Note: Eid takbirs are additional takbirs in the Eid prayer, not the regular takbirs. This is a core list to memorize for understanding the internal structure of salah.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): An obligatory element whose omission requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw) but does not invalidate the prayer.

The Opening Takbir: Condition or Integral?
Dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i on the legal status of the opening takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that takbirat al-ihram is a condition (shart) of prayer, cite the Quranic and hadith proofs, and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) with the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
The opening takbir is a condition of prayer, not an integral; the prayer begins after it.

When a Muslim begins salah, the first act is to say 'Allahu Akbar'. But is this takbir part of the prayer itself or a prerequisite? The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differ on this foundational question. This lesson unpacks the evidence each school uses and shows how the difference shapes their conceptual framework, even if the practical outcome is often the same.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the opening takbir is a condition (shart) of prayer, not a part (rukn) of it.
Condition: something that must exist before the act for it to be valid.
2
Identify the Shafi'i opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i considers the takbir an integral (rukn) of prayer, i.e., part of the prayer itself.
Integral: omission invalidates, just like rukuh or sujud.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof from the Quran
The verse 'wa dhakara isma rabbihi fasalla' (Surah al-A'la 15) places remembrance (dhikr) before prayer, indicating takbir is before the prayer, hence a condition.
The word 'fa' (then) shows sequence.
4
Examine the hadith 'tahrimatuha al-takbir'
This hadith defines the start of the prohibitive state; Hanafis interpret it as the takebir being the trigger, not a component.
Shafi'is use the same hadith to argue takbir is the first integral.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If takbir is omitted, both schools rule the prayer invalid, but the reasoning differs: missing condition vs. missing integral.
This conceptual difference can affect rulings on related issues, such as repetition of takbir or the status of actions before it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا دخل الرجل في صلوته كبر تحریمہ باندھتے وقت تکبیر کہے۔ کیونکہ آیت میں ہے وربک فکبر (آیت ۳ سورۃ المدثر ہے ) اس لئے تحریمہ کے ساتھ ہی تکبیر کہے۔ مسئلہ نمبرا میں حدیث گزری جس میں تھا و تحریمها التكبير اس حدیث سے بھی پتہ چلتا ہے کہ تحریمہ کے وقت تکبیر کہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک تکبیر داخل نماز نہیں ہے بلکہ وہ شرائط نماز میں سے ہے۔ کیونکہ آیت میں ہے وذكر اسم ربه فصلی (الف) (آیت ۱۵ سورۃ الاعلی ۱۸۷) اس آیت میں کہا گیا ہے کہ اللہ کا ذکر کرو پھر نماز پڑھو۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ ذکر پہلے ہو گا تکبیر پہلے ہوگی پھر نماز ہوگی۔ فا امام شافعی کے نزدیک وہ داخل نماز اور فرائض نماز میں سے ہے۔ اس لئے ان کے تمام شرائط وہی ہیں جو نماز کے لئے ہیں۔
And when a man enters into his prayer, he says takbir. He says takbir when binding the tahrimah. Because in the verse: 'And your Lord magnify' (Surah al-Muddaththir, verse 3). Therefore, he says takbir with the tahrimah. In issue number one, a hadith passed in which it was: 'and its tahrimah is the takbir.' From this hadith, it is also clear that he says takbir at the time of tahrimah. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the takbir is not inside the prayer, but rather it is among the conditions of prayer. Because in the verse: 'And he mentioned the name of his Lord and prayed' (Surah al-A'la, verse 15). In this verse, it is said: 'Make remembrance of Allah, then pray.' The meaning of this is that the remembrance comes first; the takbir will be first, then the prayer. As for Imam al-Shafi'i, according to him, it is inside the prayer and among the obligations of prayer. Therefore, all its conditions are the same as those for the prayer.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of the opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram). The base matn states: 'When a man enters his prayer, he says takbir.' The commentator explains that the takbir is said when binding the tahrimah (the prohibitive state). The proof is from the Quranic command 'wa rabbaka fakabbir' and the hadith 'tahrimatuha al-takbir.' The key dispute here is the legal nature of the takbir: Is it part of the prayer (dakhil) or a condition (shart) outside of it? Abu Hanifa holds it is a condition, based on the verse in Surah al-A'la where remembrance of Allah (dhikr) precedes prayer, indicating that the takbir is before the prayer. Al-Shafi'i holds it is an integral part of prayer (fard). This difference has practical implications: for example, if someone forgets the takbir, according to Hanafi, the prayer is invalid because the condition is missing; according to Shafi'i, the prayer is invalid because an integral is missing. The consequence is the same, but the conceptual framework differs. The Hanafi view aligns with the idea that the prayer begins after the takbir, not with it.

Key Terms
تحریمہ (tahrimah): The state of prohibition that begins with the takbir, making worldly actions (like talking, eating) prohibited during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the opening takbir is considered a:
A) Integral (rukn) of prayer
B) Condition (shart) of prayer
C) Sunnah of prayer
D) Recommended action

Key Takeaway
The opening takbir is a condition (shart) in Hanafi fiqh, not an integral (rukn), based on the Quranic sequence proof from Surah al-A'la.

Hand-Raising Height: Hanafi Position and Evidence
Hanafi ruling on hand-raising height with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hand-raising height during takbir, cite the evidence from hadith, and explain how the Hanafis reconcile conflicting narrations with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Men raise to earlobes, women to chest — Hanafis reconcile all hadith by assigning shoulder-raising to women for modesty.

This lesson examines a well-known difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: the height to which hands are raised during the opening takbir of prayer. The Hanafi position distinguishes between men and women, while the Shafi'i position is uniform. We will explore the hadith evidence and the Hanafi method of reconciling seemingly contradictory narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is raising hands at the opening takbir. The dispute is about the height: Hanafis say men to earlobes, women to chest; Shafi'is say both to shoulders.
This is a practical difference in salah.
2
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
Examine the hadith cited for men (earlobes) from Wail ibn Hujr and Malik ibn al-Huwayrith, and for women (chest) from Wail ibn Hujr specifically for women.
The Hanafis prioritize the explicit instruction for women.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i dalil
Examine the hadith from Ibn Umar and Salim ibn Abdullah raising to shoulders.
The Shafi'is rely on general practice of the Prophet.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafis do not reject the shoulder-raising hadith; they assign it to women, combining all proofs. The shoulder-raising hadith is interpreted for women for modesty.
This shows the Hanafi method of tawfiq (reconciliation).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi men raise to ears, Shafi'i men to shoulders. Women in Hanafi raise to chest, in Shafi'i to shoulders.
Both positions are based on authentic narrations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورفع يديه مع التكبير حتى يحاذي بابهامیه شحمتی اذنيه تكبیر کہنے کے ساتھ دونوں ہاتھوں کو اتنا اٹھائے کہ دونوں انگوٹھے کان کی لو کے برابر ہو جائے۔ حدیث میں دونوں طریقہ ہیں یعنی پہلے ہاتھ اٹھائے پھر تکبیر کہے اور یہ بھی ہے کہ پہلے تکبیر کہے پھر ہاتھ اٹھائے ۔ حنفیہ کے نزدیک بہتر یہ ہے کہ پہلے ہاتھ اٹھائے تا کہ عمل سے بھی اللہ کے علاوہ کا انکار ہو جائے پھر تکبیر کہے تا کہ اللہ کی وحدانیت کا اقرار ہو جائے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ان ابن عمر قال كان رسول الله الله الله اذا قام للصلوة رفع يديه حتى تكونا حذو منكبيه ثم كبر ... اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ پہلے ہاتھ اٹھائے پھر تکبیر کہے تو بہتر ہے۔ اور اگر پہلے تکبیر کہے پھر ہاتھ اٹھائے تب بھی کچھ حرج نہیں ہے۔ حدیث میں اس کا بھی ذکر ہے۔ انه رأی مالک بن الحویرث اذا صلى كبر ثم رفع يديه .... وحدث ان رسول الله له كان يفعل هكذا ... اس حدیث میں پہلے تکبیر کہی پھر ہاتھ اٹھائے۔ ہاتھ کان کی لو تک اٹھائے اس طرح کہ انگلیاں کان کی لو کے مد مقابل ہوں اور باقی ہاتھ گلے اور مونڈھے کے قریب ہوتا کہ تمام احادیث پر عمل ہو جائے ۔ کان کی لو تک انگلیاں رکھنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن مالک بن الحوريث ان رسول الله الا الله كان اذا كبر رفع يديه حتى يحاذى بهما اذنيه ... عن قتادة بهذا الاسناد انه رأى نبى الله لا و قال حتى يحاذى بهما فروع اذنيه ... عن وائل بن حجر قال رأيت النبي الا الله حين افتتح الصلوة رفع يديه حيال اذنيه ... ان سب احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تکبیر کے وقت ہاتھ کان کی لو تک مرد اٹھائے گا۔ مونڈھے تک اٹھانے کی جو حدیث ہے ہم کہتے ہیں کہ وہ عورتوں کے لئے ہے۔ اور اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن وائل بن حجر قال قال رسول الله له يا ابن حجر اذا صلیت فاجعل یدیک حذاء اذنيك والمرأة تجعلى يديها حذاء ثدييها ... اس حدیث میں عورتوں کے بارے میں آیا کہ وہ اپنے پستان تک ہاتھ اٹھائے۔ کیونکہ اس کے لئے یہی زیادہ ستر کی چیز ہے۔ امام شافعی اور دیگر ائمہ کے نزدیک ہاتھ مونڈھے تک اٹھا ئیں گے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ احادیث ہیں۔ عن سالم بن عبد الله عن ابيه ان رسول الله و كان يرفع يديه حذو منكبيه اذا افتتح الصلوة ... ان احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہاتھ مونڈھے تک اٹھاتے تھے ۔ حنفیہ اس طرح عمل کرتے ہیں کہ تمام احادیث پر عمل ہا جائے۔
And he raises his hands with the takbir until he aligns his thumbs with the lobes of his ears. With the takbir, he raises both hands so that both thumbs become level with the earlobes. There are two narrations in hadith: he raised hands first then said takbir, and also that he said takbir first then raised hands. According to the Hanafis, it is better to raise hands first so that the action signifies rejection of anything besides Allah, then say takbir to affirm Allah's oneness. The evidence is the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'When the Prophet stood for prayer, he raised his hands until they were level with his shoulders, then said takbir.' This hadith shows it is better to raise hands first then say takbir. And if he says takbir first then raises hands, there is no harm. There is also a hadith mentioning this. The hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith: he said takbir then raised hands... And it is narrated that the Prophet did this. So raising hands to the earlobes in a way that the fingers are opposite the earlobes and the rest of the hand is near the neck and shoulder, so that all hadith are acted upon. The evidence for placing fingers at the earlobes is the hadith from Malik ibn al-Huwayrith: 'When the Prophet said takbir, he raised his hands until they were level with his ears.' And from Qatadah with this chain: 'He saw the Prophet and said he raised them until they were level with the tops of his ears.' And from Wail ibn Hujr: 'I saw the Prophet when he began prayer raising his hands opposite his ears.' All these hadith indicate that a man should raise his hands to the earlobes during takbir. As for the hadith about raising to the shoulders, we say that is for women. The evidence is the hadith from Wail ibn Hujr: 'The Prophet said: O Ibn Hujr, when you pray, place your hands opposite your ears, and the woman should place her hands opposite her chest.' In this hadith, it comes about women that they raise their hands to their chest, because that is more concealing for her. According to Imam al-Shafi'i and other imams, they raise hands to the shoulders. Their evidence is the hadith from Salim ibn Abdullah from his father: 'The Prophet used to raise his hands level with his shoulders when beginning prayer.' These hadith show he raised to the shoulders. The Hanafis act in a way that all hadith are acted upon.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage details the method of raising hands during the opening takbir. The base matn states they are raised until the thumbs align with the earlobes. The commentator explains the order: it is better to raise first then say takbir, based on the hadith of Ibn Umar. However, if one says takbir first, it is also acceptable. The main dispute is about the height: men raise to the earlobes, women to the chest. The Hanafis reconcile conflicting hadith by assigning the shoulder-level raising to women, based on the hadith of Wail ibn Hujr where the Prophet specifically instructs women to raise to their chest. The Shafi'is use the hadith of Ibn Umar and others to raise to shoulders for both genders. The Hanafis combine all proofs by applying the shoulder-raising hadith to women and the earlobe-raising hadith to men. This practical compromise allows them to act on all authentic narrations.

Key Terms
شحمتی اذنيه (shahmatay udhunayhi): The lobes of the ears (the soft parts).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Raising Hands at Ruku': Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Hanafi position on raf' al-yadayn at ruku'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising hands at ruku', explain the Hanafi evidence for leaving it, and compare it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Raising hands at ruku' is permissible, but Hanafis leave it due to stronger hadith and Quranic emphasis on humility.

This passage addresses a well-known difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the gesture of raising the hands (raf' al-yadayn) during the transition into ruku' and upon rising from it. While both schools agree on raising the hands at the opening takbir, they diverge on the subsequent movements. Understanding this ikhtilaf requires examining the hadith evidence and the Hanafi principle of prioritizing the Quranic spirit over apparent hadith.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling on raising hands at ruku': it is permissible (ja'iz) but the preferred practice is not to do it. The mufta bihi is to leave it.
2
Identify the opposing school and view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that raising hands when going into ruku' and when rising from it is sunnah (recommended).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i rely on the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar that the Prophet raised his hands at each movement.
This hadith is considered authentic by many.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis present counter-hadith (Ibn Mas'ud, al-Bara') showing the Prophet only raised hands at the beginning. They also cite the Quranic command 'qumu lillahi qanitin' (stand before Allah with devotion) to emphasize stillness, preferring the hadith that support non-raising as more in line with the Quran.
The Hanafi usul principle: when hadith conflict, choose the one that aligns with the Quran.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in a Hanafi mosque, the imam and congregation do not raise hands at ruku'; in a Shafi'i mosque, they do. This affects those praying behind an imam of a different madhhab.
The Hanafi position is the relied upon practice in their school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رکوع کے وقت میں ہاتھ اٹھانا جائز ہے۔ احادیث سے ثابت ہے۔ البتہ حنفیہ اس پر عمل اس لئے نہیں کرتے ہیں کہ اس کے خلاف حدیث موجود ہے۔ اور اصل بات یہ ہے کہ حضرت امام اعظم کی نگاہ قوموا لله قانتین (و) کی طرف گئی ہے۔ اس لئے دوسری احادیث پر عمل کیا۔ حدیث یہ ہے (ا) قال عبد الله بن مسعود الا اصلي بكم صلوة رسول الله ا فصلى فلم يرفع يديه الا في اول مرة (ز) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ان النبی تم یرفع الا فی اول مرة ، ص ۵۹ نمبر ۲۵۷) عن البراء ان رسول الله الله كان اذا افتتح الصلوة رفع يديه الى قريب من اذنيه ثم لا يعود (ح) ( ابو داؤد شریف، باب من لم یذکر الرفع عند الرکوع ص ۱۶ نمبر ۷۴۹ رنسائی شریف ، باب رفع الیدین حذ والمنكبين عند الرفع من الركوع والرخصة في ترك ذلك ص ۱۲۰ نمبر ۱۰۵۹) ان احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ رکوع کے وقت رفع یدی کے چھوڑنے کی گنجائش ہے فائدہ امام شافعی اور دیگر ائمہ کے یہاں رکوع میں جاتے وقت اور رکوع سے اٹھتے وقت رفع یدین ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عبد الله بن عمر قال رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا قام في الصلوة رفع يديه حتى ...
Raising hands at the time of ruku' is permissible. It is established by hadith. However, the Hanafis do not act upon it because there is a hadith against it. And the fundamental point is that Imam Azam's gaze was towards 'Stand before Allah with devotion' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:238). Therefore, he acted upon other hadith. The hadith is: (1) Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said: 'Shall I not pray with you the prayer of the Prophet?' He prayed and did not raise his hands except at the first time.' (Tirmidhi). (2) From al-Bara': 'When the Prophet began prayer, he raised his hands near to his ears, then did not repeat.' (Abu Dawud, Nasa'i). These hadith show that there is leeway in leaving the raising of hands at the time of ruku'. Benefit: According to Imam al-Shafi'i and other imams, there is raising of hands when going into ruku' and when rising from ruku'. Their evidence is the hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar: 'I saw the Prophet, when he stood in prayer, raise his hands until...'
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage addresses the practice of raising hands during ruku' (reverence). The Hanafi position is that while it is established by some hadith, they do not practice it because there are contradictory hadith showing the Prophet did not raise hands except at the beginning. Imam Abu Hanifa gave priority to the Quranic command 'qumu lillahi qanitin' (stand before Allah in devotion) which implies stillness and humility, which is better than excessive movement. The Shafi'is, on the other hand, practice raising hands at ruku' based on the hadith of Ibn Umar and others. The Hanafis consider their practice as permissible but not preferable, and they follow the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and al-Bara'. This is a clear inter-madhhab difference in the prayer movements.

Key Terms
رفع الیدین (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands during prayer, specifically at takbir and ruku'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis not raise their hands when going into ruku'?
A) They consider it haram
B) Because of a hadith showing the Prophet did not do it
C) Because it is makruh
D) Because the Quran prohibits it

Key Takeaway
Raising hands at ruku' is permissible, but the Hanafi school prefers to leave it based on hadith showing the Prophet did not repeat the gesture and the Quranic emphasis on humility.

Salah — Prayer

Raising Hands in Prayer: Hanafi Position and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on hand raising in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising hands in prayer (position and at ruku), identify the key hadith evidence, and explain how the Hanafi school reconciles conflicting reports to derive its practice.

Core Idea
Men raise to ears, women to chest, and no raising at ruku: the Hanafi position reconciles all hadiths.

The raising of hands (raf' al-yadayn) in prayer is a practice that varies between schools. While all Muslims agree that the Prophet raised his hands at the opening takbir, there is disagreement on the exact position (ears vs shoulders) and whether to raise at ruku. This lesson explores the Hanafi position and its evidence, contrasting it with the Shafi'i view, and shows how the Hanafi school harmonizes apparently conflicting narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Sub-Issues
Note that the passage covers two distinct questions: (a) hand position at the opening takbir, and (b) raising hands at ruku and rising from ruku.
2
State the Hanafi Position
Men raise to earlobes; women raise to chest. No raising at ruku.
This is the mufta bihi (operative) position.
3
Examine the Hanafi Evidence
List the hadiths cited: Wa'il ibn Hujr (ears), Qatada, and the hadith specifying women's position. For ruku, the hadiths of Ibn Mas'ud and al-Bara'.
Key hadith: The Prophet told Ibn Hujr: 'When you pray, place your hands opposite your ears, and the woman should place her hands opposite her breasts.'
4
Examine the Opposing (Shafi'i) Evidence
Hadiths from Ibn Umar raising to shoulders and also at ruku and rising.
The Shafi'i school relies on these narrations for their practice.
5
Understand the Hanafi Reconciliation
The shoulder-raising hadiths are interpreted as applying to women (takhsis by gender). For ruku, the Qur'anic principle of 'qumuu lillahi qanitin' (standing in humility) is prioritized over some hadiths.
This demonstrates a principled method of harmonizing apparent contradictions.
6
Note the Practical Difference (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
Hanafi men raise to ears, women to chest, and do not raise at ruku. Shafi'i raise to shoulders and also at ruku and rising.
Both practices are valid; the difference is over a recommended act, not an obligation.

In this hadith it comes regarding women that they raise their hands to their breasts, because that is more concealing for her. Their proof is these hadiths: from Salim ibn Abdullah from his father that the Messenger of Allah used to raise his hands to his shoulders when he began prayer (e) (Bukhari, chapter on raising hands in the first takbir p. 102 no. 735; Muslim, chapter on desirability of raising hands to shoulders p. 68 no. 390). Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the raising of hands (raf' al-yadayn) in prayer. The author begins by presenting hadiths that show the Prophet raised his hands to his ears at the opening takbir. The Hanafi position: men raise hands to the earlobes; women raise hands to their chest (breasts) for greater modesty. This is supported by the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr which explicitly distinguishes between men and women. The Shafi'i and other schools hold that both men and women raise hands to the shoulders, citing hadiths from Ibn Umar. The author notes that the Hanafis reconcile all hadiths by assigning the shoulder-raising hadith to women. The passage also addresses raising hands during ruku. It states that raising hands at ruku is proven by some hadiths, but the Hanafis choose not to act upon it because of contrary hadiths—specifically the practice of Ibn Mas'ud and al-Bara' who reported that the Prophet only raised hands at the beginning. The author mentions that Imam Abu Hanifa's reasoning is based on the Qur'anic verse 'Stand before Allah in devout obedience' (Q. 2:238), implying stillness in prayer. Therefore, the Hanafis restrict raf' al-yadayn to the opening takbir only. Imam Shafi'i and others hold it as desirable at ruku and rising from ruku. The author concludes that this is a disagreement over desirability (istihbab), not obligation, so one should not argue about it.

Key Terms
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands during prayer; specifically at the opening takbir, and optionally at other points.
تكبير تحريمہ (takbir tahrimah): The initial 'Allahu Akbar' that marks the beginning of prayer and prohibits worldly actions.

The Hanafi school teaches that men raise hands to ears, women to chest at the opening takbir, and does not practice raising at ruku, harmonizing all authentic narrations.

Ruling on Raising Hands (Raf' al-Yadayn) in Prayer
Determines the ruling on raising hands during takbir and bowing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising hands during the prayer, identify the proof (dalil), and explain why the difference with other madhhabs is one of istihbab only.

Core Idea
Raising hands is mustahabb, not wajib – a difference of recommendation, not obligation.

You have likely seen some worshippers raise their hands when saying takbir, bowing, and rising from bowing, while others do not. This issue sometimes sparks unnecessary arguments. The passage before us settles the matter clearly: from the hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) and the commentary of our scholars, raising hands is a recommended act (mustahabb), not an obligation. Understanding this ruling helps preserve unity in prayer and prevents conflict over a non-essential element.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is raising the hands (raf' al-yadayn) at specific points in the prayer. The passage explicitly rules it as mustahabb (recommended). Note that it also says 'there is scope for not doing it' – meaning the prayer remains valid without it.
The ruling here is sunnah muakkadah according to the Hanafi position.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of the Prophet's practice: his hands were at shoulder level when he said takbir, when bowing, when rising from bowing, but not in prostration. This hadith is from Sahih Bukhari and Sahih Muslim.
The dalil is a hadith ahad, so its thubut is zanni – leading to a non-obligatory ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith describes the Prophet's action, which is the basis for the sunnah. The commentary states directly that this action is mustahabb, implying that the legal implication of the descriptive hadith is recommendation, not obligation.
In Hanafi usul, a mere action of the Prophet indicates a rank below wajib.
4
Note the ikhtilaf with other schools
The passage acknowledges that there is a difference of opinion (ikhtilaf) but only over istihbab (recommendation), not over the validity of the prayer. Other schools also consider it sunnah; they do not hold it to be wajib.
Thus, the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is minimal: whether one raises hands or not, the prayer is valid in all schools.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author advises against arguing about this issue, indicating that the Hanafi position is clear and should be followed with tolerance. The mufta bihi is that raf' al-yadayn is sunnah muakkadah; leaving it is permissible.
This ruling comes from the zahir al-riwayah (the six books of Imam Muhammad) and is the standard Hanafi position.

Source Text

(from Sahih Bukhari and Muslim) From this it is understood that raising the hands at the time of bowing is mustahabb. And there is also scope for not doing it. Therefore, one should not argue about this issue; it is only a difference of mustahabb.

Commentary
This passage from the sharh clarifies the ruling on raising the hands (raf' al-yadayn) during the prayer. The matn mentioned that the Prophet's hands were at the level of his shoulders when he said the takbir for bowing, when raising from bowing, but not in prostration. The hadith references provided confirm this practice. The commentary then explicitly states that this action is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory. Importantly, it notes that there is scope for not doing it, meaning the prayer remains valid without it. The author advises against disputing over this matter, as the difference is only regarding its recommendation, not its necessity. This reflects the Hanafi position that raf' al-yadayn is not wajib, unlike some other schools.

Key Terms
رفع الیدین (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands to the shoulders during the prayer at certain positions.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended act; omission is not sinful but gains reward.

Key Takeaway
Raising hands during prayer is a recommended sunnah, not an obligation; omitting it does not affect the prayer's validity, and differences among schools are only over its recommendation.

The Sunnah of Hand Placement: Under the Navel vs. on the Chest
Dispute over hand placement position and its evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi sunnah method of hand placement, cite the evidence from hadith, and explain the difference with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Hand placement in prayer is sunnah, and the Hanafi method is under the navel; both positions are valid.

This lesson examines the sunnah of placing the right hand on the left during prayer. The passage details the Hanafi method, including the specific grasping technique, and presents the evidence from hadith. It then introduces the Shafi'i position of placing hands on the chest and concludes with Imam Tirmidhi's verdict that both are permissible.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What exactly is the Hanafi method of hand placement? Note the specific grasping technique and the placement under the navel.
The Hanafi sunnah combines the hadiths of placing (wad') and grasping (akhdh).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Which school objects and on what grounds? State the Shafi'i position: hands on the chest.
Imam al-Shafi'i relies on the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
What is the dalil of the Shafi'i school? Quote the hadith of Wa'il and how they interpret it.
The hadith states the Prophet placed his right hand on his left then placed them on his chest.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut or accommodate this? They have their own hadith (Ali) and cite Tirmidhi's verdict that both positions are permissible.
The Hanafi school does not reject the Shafi'i hadith but interprets it differently; Tirmidhi's ruling allows flexibility.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical consequence of this difference? In prayer, Hanafis place hands under navel, Shafi'is on chest; both prayers are valid.
A Hanafi following a Shafi'i imam may place his hands on his chest to avoid discord, as the act is sunnah, not wajib.

ويعتمد بيده اليمنى على اليسرى [۱۸۱) (۱۱) اور پکڑے دائیں ہاتھ سے بائیں ہاتھ پر اور دونوں ہاتھوں کو ناف کے نیچے رکھے۔ شرح حدیث میں یہ بھی ہے کہ دائیں ہاتھ کو بائیں ہاتھ پر رکھے۔ اور یہ بھی ہے کہ دائیں (ابودا و شریف ، باب وضع ایمنی علی الیسری فی الصلوۃ میں ۷۵۹۱۱۷ رستن سیھتی ، باب وضع اليدين على الصدر في الصلوة من السنتيض خانی ص ۴۶، نمبر ۲۳۳۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہاتھ سینے پر رکھنا چاہئے۔ امام ۵۹ نمبر (۲۵۲) وآخر قیام میں جہاں جہاں ذکر مسنون ہے وہاں وہاں ہاتھ باندھنا بہتر ہے۔ اور جہاں جہاں ذکر مسنون نہیں ہے وہاں وہاں ہاتھ چھوڑنا
And he places his right hand on his left. [181] (11) And he should grasp his left hand with his right hand, and place both hands under the navel. Explanation: In the hadith, it is also mentioned that he placed his right hand on his left hand, and it is also mentioned that he grasped his left hand with his right hand. Therefore, according to the Hanafis, the sunnah method is to grasp the wrist of the left hand with the thumb and little finger of the right hand, and place the remaining three fingers on the left wrist, so that both hadiths are acted upon. Evidence: (1) Hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr... (2) Hadith of Qabisah ibn Hulb... (3) Hadith of Ali: 'It is from the sunnah in prayer to place palm upon palm under the navel.' These hadiths indicate that the hands should be placed under the navel. And according to Imam Shafi'i, placing hands on the chest is sunnah. Their evidence is the hadith of Wa'il that the Prophet placed his right on his left then placed them on his chest. Imam Tirmidhi gave the best verdict: both are permissible. Some scholars say above the navel, some below; all are acceptable. And in standing positions where dhikr is sunnah, it is better to fold the hands, and where dhikr is not sunnah, to leave them loose.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage covers the sunnah method of hand placement (wad' al-yadayn) during qiyam. The matn states the basic ruling: placing the right hand on the left. The sharh expands on this by combining multiple hadiths. The Hanafi method is to grasp the left wrist with the right hand, specifically using the thumb and little finger around the wrist, with the remaining three fingers extended along the forearm. This combines the hadiths that mention placing the hand (wad') and grasping (akhdh). The position is under the navel, based on the hadith of Ali. The dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i is then presented: Shafi'i holds that hands should be placed on the chest, based on a hadith of Wa'il. The passage then cites Imam al-Tirmidhi's opinion that both positions (above or below navel) are permissible and wide in scope. Finally, it notes that folding hands is recommended during standing when dhikr is sunnah, but when not, hands are left loose. This reflects the Hanafi position that hand placement is sunnah, not wajib.

Key Terms
وضع الیمین علی الیسری (wad' al-yamin 'ala al-yusra): The act of placing the right hand on the left hand during the standing position of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Right hand on left hand on the chest
B) Right hand grasps left wrist with thumb and little finger, placed under navel
C) Both hands held at the sides
D) Right hand on left hand above the navel

Key Takeaway
Hand placement is a sunnah act of prayer; the Hanafi method is under the navel, and the difference with the Shafi'i school is a valid ikhtilaf.

Hand Placement in Qiyam: Below the Navel
Explains Hanafi method with hadith proofs and Shafi'i opposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method of hand placement in qiyam, cite the hadith proofs, and distinguish the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Hand placement below the navel is an emphasized sunnah, not fard, and combining multiple hadiths yields the Hanafi grasp.

This lesson examines a well-known difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: where to place the hands during standing in prayer. The Hanafi school prescribes placing the right hand on the left below the navel with a specific grasp, while the Shafi'i school places them on the chest. The source passage presents the Hanafi proof from three hadiths and addresses the opposing view, citing Imam al-Tirmidhi's ruling that both methods are permissible.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact method described: right hand grasps left wrist below the navel with thumb and little finger around the wrist, three fingers on the forearm.
This combines the hadiths of Wa'il, Qabisa, and 'Ali.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that hands should be placed on the chest, based on a version of Wa'il's hadith.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i dalil: the hadith of Wa'il where the Prophet placed his right on his left and then placed them on his chest.
This hadith is reported by Abu Dawud and Bayhaqi.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Note that the Hanafi response here is to cite Tirmidhi's ruling that both are permissible, thereby defending the Hanafi method without direct rebuttal.
The Hanafi method is presented as the preferred practice, but the dispute is acknowledged as legitimate.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is that Hanafis place hands below the navel, Shafi'is on the chest; both are considered valid acts of worship.
Neither placement invalidates the prayer.

(۲۵۲
اوت قیام میں جہاں جہاں ذکر مسنون ہے وہاں وہاں ہاتھ باندھنا بہتر ہے۔ اور جہاں جہاں ذکر مسنون نہیں ہے وہاں وہاں ہاتھ چھوڑنا
حاشیہ : (الف) وائل بن حجر نے حضور کو دیکھا. پھر اپنے دائیں ہاتھ کو بائیں ہاتھ پر رکھا (ب ) آپ ہماری امامت کرتے تو بائیں ہاتھ کو دائیں ہاتھ سے پکڑتے (ج) حضرت علی نے فرمایا کہ نماز میں سنت یہ ہے کہ تھیلی کو تھیلی پر رکھے ناف کے نیچے (و) حضور نے دائیں ہاتھ کو بائیں ہاتھ پر رکھا پھر ان دونوں کو اپنے سینے پر رکھا (ہ) بعض علماء کی رائے ہے کہ دونوں ہاتھوں کو ناف کے اوپر رکھے اور بعض کی رائے ہے کہ ان دونوں کو ناف کے نیچے رکھے۔ اور علماء کے نزدیک ان میں سے ہر ایک کی گنجائش ہے۔
He leans with his right hand on his left [181] (11) And he grasps with his right hand the left hand, and places both hands below the navel. In Sharh al-Hadith it is also mentioned that he places his right hand on his left. And it is also mentioned that he grasps his left hand with his right hand. Therefore, according to the Hanafis, the Sunnah method is that he grasps the wrist of his left hand with his thumb and little finger of his right hand, and places the remaining three fingers on the forearm of his left hand, so that both hadiths are acted upon. Basis: (1) From Wa'il ibn Hujr: he saw the Prophet (ﷺ) ... then he placed his right hand on his left (a) (Muslim, chapter on placing right on left, p.173 no.40; Abu Dawud, chapter on placing right on left, p.17 no.755; Bukhari, chapter on placing right on left in prayer, no.740). From this hadith it is known that he places his right hand on his left. (2) Qabisa ibn Hulb from his father: he said: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) used to lead us in prayer, and he would take his left with his right (b) (Tirmidhi, chapter on placing right on left in prayer, p.59 no.225?; Nasa'i, chapter on placing right on left in prayer, p.133 no.809). From this hadith it is known that he should grasp his left hand with his right hand. Therefore, the Hanafis acted upon both hadiths. And the hadith for placing below the navel is: (3) From 'Ali: he said: Verily, from the Sunnah in prayer is placing palm upon palm in prayer below the navel (j) (Abu Dawud, chapter on placing right on left in prayer, p.17 no.756; Dar Qutni, chapter on taking the left with the right in prayer, vol.1 p.289 no.089; Bayhaqi, chapter on placing hands on chest in prayer from the Sunnah, vol.2 p.48 no.2341). From these hadiths it is known that he should place his hands below the navel. Now, Imam al-Shafi'i holds that placing hands on the chest is Sunnah. His evidence is the hadith from Wa'il: he saw the Prophet (ﷺ) place his right on his left, then he placed them on his chest (w) (Abu Dawud, chapter on placing right on left in prayer, no.759? p.17; Bayhaqi, chapter on placing hands on chest in prayer from the Sunnah, vol.2 p.46 no.2335). From this hadith it is known that he should place hands on the chest. Imam al-Tirmidhi gave an excellent ruling: both are permissible. "And some of them opined that he should place them above the navel, and some opined that he should place them below the navel, and all of that is expansive according to them" (h) (Tirmidhi, chapter on placing right on left in prayer, p.59 no.252?). And in standing, wherever the dhikr is prescribed (masnun), there it is better to tie the hands. And wherever the dhikr is not prescribed, there it is better to leave the hands loose. Footnote: (a) Wa'il ibn Hujr saw the Prophet (ﷺ), then he placed his right hand on his left. (b) He used to lead us in prayer and would grasp his left hand with his right. (j) 'Ali said that in prayer the Sunnah is to place palm on palm below the navel. (w) The Prophet (ﷺ) placed his right hand on his left, then placed both on his chest. (h) Some scholars opined that both hands should be placed above the navel, and some opined that they should be placed below the navel, and according to scholars each of these is permissible.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the placement of hands in qiyam (standing) during salah. The author first states the Hanafi position: the right hand grasps the left wrist (thumb and little finger around the wrist, three fingers on the forearm) and both are placed below the navel. The proof is based on three hadiths: (1) Wa'il ibn Hujr reports the Prophet placing his right on his left; (2) Qabisa reports the Prophet grasping his left with his right; (3) 'Ali reports that it is Sunnah to place palm on palm below the navel. The Hanafis combine these to specify the exact method. The Shafi'i school holds that hands should be placed on the chest, relying on a version of the hadith of Wa'il where the Prophet placed them on his chest. Imam al-Tirmidhi is cited for an expansive ruling: both positions are permissible. The passage also notes that during the recitation of prescribed dhikr (like tasbih in ruku and sujud), it is better to tie the hands, and during other parts of the prayer, it is better to leave them loose. The footnote provides Urdu translations of the hadith texts.

Key Terms
السرة (al-surrah): The navel. In this context, the location below which the hands are placed during qiyam.
يعتمد (ya'tamid): He leans or grasps. Here it means placing the right hand on the left with weight.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act in prayer; omission does not invalidate but is against the preferred practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where should the hands be placed during qiyam (standing) in prayer?
A) On the chest, with the right hand on the left.
B) Below the navel, with the right hand grasping the left wrist in the specific manner (thumb and little finger around wrist, three fingers on forearm).
C) On the thighs, with palms open.
D) Anywhere between the chest and navel.

Key Takeaway
Placing hands below the navel is the Hanafi sunnah method, but other placements are permissible per classical scholars.

The Hanafi Preferred Opening Supplication: Subhanaka
Presents Hanafi preference with intra- and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi preferred opening supplication, explain the intra-Hanafi difference (Abu Yusuf's view), and identify the thamarah al-khilaf between Hanafi and Shafi'i schools.

Core Idea
In Hanafi salah, the preferred opening supplication is Subhanaka; reciting it alone is mufta bihi, though combining with Wajjahtu is a valid intra-Hanafi variant.

After the opening takbir, the worshipper is recommended to recite an opening supplication. While many wordings are transmitted, the Hanafi school has a clear preference based on the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri. However, there is a notable intra-Hanafi opinion from Imam Abu Yusuf, who favored combining Subhanaka with the Shafi'i-preferred Wajjahtu. This lesson clarifies the positions and their practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling level
The act is the opening supplication (du'a al-istiftah) after takbirat al-ihram. Its ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah), not fard or wajib. This means omitting it does not invalidate the prayer.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school prefers reciting 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...' based on the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, which reports that the Prophet (ﷺ) recited it when standing for night prayer. This hadith is found in Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud.
The author states this is 'زيداد بہتر' (better) according to Hanafis.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Yusuf's view
Imam Abu Yusuf held that both Subhanaka and Wajjahtu should be recited together, because both hadiths are authentic. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
Combining was not the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ) according to the majority, but Abu Yusuf saw merit in including both.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i prefers 'Wajjahtu wajhiya' based on a hadith from 'Ali ibn Abi Talib. The Hanafi school does not accept this as the preferred supplication because the hadith of Abu Sa'id is more specific to the opening supplication.
This is a cross-madhhab difference with practical implications.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The mufta bihi (operative position for fatwa) is to recite Subhanaka alone. The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is that Hanafis recite Subhanaka, Shafi'is recite Wajjahtu, and followers of Abu Yusuf may combine both.
In congregation, following the imam's practice is key; but individually, one may follow preferred view.

تحریمہ باندھنے کے بعد پڑھے سبحانک اللهم وبحمدک و تبارک اسمک و تعالى جدك ولا اله غیرک تحریمہ باندھنے کے بعد اور بھی بہت سی دعائیں منقول ہیں لیکن حنفیہ کے نزدیک سبحانک اللهم الخ پڑھنازیادہ بہتر ہے
یہ حدیث ہے عن ابي سعيد الخدري قال كان رسول الله الله اذا قام الى الصلوة بالليل كبر ثم يقول سبحانك اللهم الخ (الف) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما یقول عند افتتاح الصلوۃ ص ۵۷ نمبر ۲۴۲ / ابوداؤد شریف، باب من رأی الاستفتاح بسماتک ص ۱۹ انمبر ۷۷۵ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سبحانک اللھم الخ پڑھنا چاہئے ۔ فائدہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک اللهم وجهت وجهی الخ پڑھنا زیادہ بہتر ہے۔ اس کا ثبوت یہ حدیث ہے عن علی بن ابی طالب قال كان رسول الله اذا قام الى الصلوة كبر ثم قال وجهت وجهي الخ (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب ما تسمح به الصلوة من الدعاء ص ۱۷ انمبر ۷۶۰) امام ابو یوسف ان دونوں احادیث کی وجہ سے دونوں دعاؤں کے ملانے کے قائل ہیں۔
Then he says: Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika wa tabarakasmuka wa ta'ala jadduka wa la ilaha ghayruka [183] (13) After tying the tahrimah, he should recite Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika wa tabarakasmuka wa ta'ala jadduka wa la ilaha ghayruka. After tying the tahrimah, many other supplications are also transmitted, but according to the Hanafis, reciting Subhanaka Allahumma... is better. This is a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: he said, When the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) stood for prayer at night, he would say the takbir, then say Subhanaka Allahumma... (a) (Tirmidhi, chapter on what to say when opening prayer, p.57 no.242; Abu Dawud, chapter on those who saw opening with Subhanaka, p.19 no.775). From this hadith it is known that he should recite Subhanaka Allahumma... Benefit: According to Imam al-Shafi'i, reciting 'Allahumma wajjahtu wajhiya...' is better. Its proof is the hadith from 'Ali ibn Abi Talib: he said, When the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) stood for prayer, he would say the takbir, then say 'Wajjahtu wajhiya...' (b) (Abu Dawud, chapter on what supplication is permitted in prayer, p.17 no.760). Imam Abu Yusuf, due to both hadiths, held the opinion of combining both supplications.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage discusses the opening supplication (du'a al-istiftah) after the takbirat al-ihram. The matn states that the worshipper should recite 'Subhanaka Allahumma...'. The commentary explains that many supplications are reported, but Hanafis prefer Subhanaka because it is established from the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri. It then presents an inter-madhhab difference: Imam al-Shafi'i prefers 'Wajjahtu wajhiya' based on a hadith from 'Ali. Additionally, there is an intra-Hanafi opinion: Imam Abu Yusuf suggests combining both supplications. The passage does not explicitly resolve which is the mufta bihi, but the Hanafi position is clearly Subhanaka as the preferred and more widely practiced choice, while Abu Yusuf's view is a minority within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
تحریمہ (tahrimah): The opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram) that makes the prayer sacred and prohibits worldly actions.
دعاء الاستفتاح (du'a al-istiftah): The opening supplication recited immediately after the opening takbir before the Fatiha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika
C) Both recited together
D) No supplication is preferred

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's preferred opening supplication is Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika, though other wordings are permissible and one intra-Hanafi view recommends combining.
