Isti'adha and Basmalah Before Recitation
Ruling on reciting ta'awwudh and basmalah before Quran recitation in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting isti'adha and basmalah before Quran recitation in prayer, identify the proofs from Quran and Sunnah, and explain why they are recited silently in every rak'ah.

Core Idea
Isti'adha and basmalah are sunnah before Quran recitation in every rak'ah, recited silently.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on two important sunan of salah: seeking refuge from Shaytan (isti'adha) and saying Bismillah (basmalah) before reciting the Quran. The author presents clear proofs from the Quran and hadith, and addresses the issue of whether these should be recited aloud or silently. Understanding the evidence and the reasoning behind silent recitation helps you follow the sunnah correctly and avoid common mistakes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting 'A'udhu billahi min ash-shaytan ir-rajim' and 'Bismillah ir-Rahman ir-Rahim' before the Fatiha. The ruling according to the Hanafi school: sunnah, not fard or wajib.
This applies to every rak'ah, not only the first.
2
Locate the primary dalil for isti'adha
The Quranic verse 16:98 commands 'So when you recite the Quran, seek refuge with Allah from the accursed Shaytan.' This is the foundational proof.
The imperative (fasta'idh) indicates a command, but Hanafis interpret it as sunnah due to other evidence.
3
Locate the primary dalil for basmalah and silent recitation
The hadith of Ibn Abbas shows the Prophet began prayers with 'Bismillah ir-Rahman ir-Rahim'. The hadith of Abdullah ibn Mughaffal shows that the Prophet and the first three caliphs did not recite it aloud, indicating silent recitation.
The hadith of Mughaffal is critical for the Hanafi ruling on silent recitation.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
For isti'adha: the imperative is a command, but the Prophet's practice (fi'l) shows it was done as a sunnah, not an obligatory act. For basmalah: the Prophet's practice and the silence of the companions establish it as sunnah and silent.
Hanafi usul holds that the Prophet's fi'l can specify the modality of an amr.
5
Note the ikhtilaf with the Shafi'i school
Shafi'is recite isti'adha only in the first rak'ah and recite basmalah aloud in audible prayers. Hanafis rely on the hadith of Mughaffal for silent recitation and on the general application of the Quranic verse for every rak'ah.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the number of rak'ahs for isti'adha and the volume of basmalah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستعيذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم [١٨٣] (١٣) اور اعوذ باللہ من الشیطان الرجیم اور بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم پڑھے۔ آیت میں ہے فاذا قرأت القرآن فاستعذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم (ج) ( آیت ۹۸ سورۃ النحل (۱۶) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا که قرآت قرآن سے پہلے اعوذ باللہ الخ پڑھے۔ عن ابي سعيد الخدري قال كان رسول الله الله اذا قام الى الصلوة ثم يقول اعوذ بالله السميع العليم من الشيطان الرجيم ( ترمذی شریف ، باب ما یقول عند افتتاح الصلوۃ ص ۵۷ نمبر ۲۴۲) اسی لئے حنفیہ کے نزدیک اعوذ باللہ قرآت قرآن کی سنت ہے۔ ثنا کی سنت نہیں ہے اس لئے ہر رکعت میں قرآت قرآن سے اعوذ باللہ الخ اور بسم اللہ الح پڑھے جائیں گے۔ بسم اللہ الخ پڑھنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابن عباس قال كان النبي يفتتح صلواته ببسم الله الرحمن الرحيم (د) ( ترندی شریف، باب من رأی انبهر بسم الله الرحمن الرحیم ص ۵۷ نمبر ۲۳۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ قرآت سے پہلے بسم اللہ پڑھنا چاہئے۔ لیکن ہمیں یہ تذکرہ نہیں ہے کہ زور سے پڑھنا چاہئے ۔ ہو سکتا ہے کہ حضور مبسم اللہ تو پڑھتے ہوں لیکن آہستہ پڑھتے ہوں۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عبد الله بن مغفل قال سمعنى ابى والا في الصلوة اقول بسم ا الله الرحمن الرحيم فقال لی بنی محدث ایاک والحدث ... وقال وقد صليت مع النبي ، و مع ابي بكر وعمر ومع عثمان فلم
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ جب رات میں نماز کے لئے کھڑے ہوتے تو تکبیر کہتے پھر سبحانک العم الخ کہتے (ب) آپ جب نماز کے لئے کھڑے ہوتے تو تکبیر کہتے پھر جھت و جبھی الخ پڑھتے (ج) جب قرآن پڑھو تو اعوذ باللہ پڑھو ( و ) آپ اپنی نماز کو بسم اللہ سے شروع فرماتے ۔
And he seeks refuge with Allah from the accursed Shaytan [183] (13) And he should recite A'udhu billahi min ash-shaytan ir-rajim and Bismillah ir-Rahman ir-Rahim. In the verse it is: 'So when you recite the Quran, seek refuge with Allah from the accursed Shaytan' (c) (Quran 16:98). From this verse it is known that before Quranic recitation, one should recite A'udhu billah... From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: he said, When the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) stood for prayer, he would then say 'A'udhu billah is-sami' il-'alim min ash-shaytan ir-rajim' (Tirmidhi, chapter on what to say when opening prayer, p.57 no.242). Therefore, according to the Hanafis, A'udhu billah is a sunnah for Quran recitation, not for thana (opening supplication). Hence in every rak'ah, before reciting the Quran, A'udhu billah... and Bismillah... should be recited. The proof for reciting Bismillah... is the hadith from Ibn 'Abbas: he said, The Prophet (ﷺ) used to begin his prayers with Bismillah ir-Rahman ir-Rahim (d) (Tirmidhi, chapter on those who saw commencing with Bismillah, p.57 no.235). From this hadith it is known that one should recite Bismillah before recitation. However, we do not have mention that it should be recited aloud. It is possible that the Prophet (ﷺ) recited Bismillah but softly. The proof for this is the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Mughaffal: he said, My father heard me saying in prayer 'Bismillah ir-Rahman ir-Rahim' and said, 'O my son, it is an innovation, beware of innovation...' and he said, 'I have prayed with the Prophet (ﷺ), with Abu Bakr, with 'Umar, and with 'Uthman, and I did not hear any of them recite it aloud.' [End of quoted hadith] Footnote: (a) When he stood for prayer at night, he would say the takbir, then say Subhanak Allahumma... (b) When he stood for prayer, he would say the takbir, then say Wajjahtu wajhiya... (c) When you recite the Quran, seek refuge with Allah. (d) He used to begin his prayers with Bismillah.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on seeking refuge (isti'adha) and saying Bismillah before Quran recitation in salah. The matn instructs to recite 'A'udhu billah...' and 'Bismillah...'. The commentary first gives the Quranic proof from Surah an-Nahl (16:98) commanding isti'adha before recitation. Then a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri shows the Prophet would say 'A'udhu billah is-sami' il-'alim...' when standing for prayer. The Hanafis conclude that isti'adha is a sunnah specifically for Quran recitation, not for the opening supplication (thana). Therefore, it should be recited in every rak'ah before the Fatiha, along with Bismillah. The proof for Bismillah is the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas that the Prophet began his prayer with 'Bismillah ir-Rahman ir-Rahim'. The commentary then addresses an issue: should Bismillah be recited aloud or silently? It cites the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Mughaffal, which indicates that the Prophet and the first three caliphs did not recite Bismillah aloud. Hence, the Hanafi school holds that Bismillah is recited silently before the Fatiha. The footnote clarifies the hadith references.

Key Terms
الاستعاذة (al-isti'adha): Seeking refuge with Allah from the accursed Shaytan by saying 'A'udhu billahi min ash-shaytan ir-rajim'.
البسملة (al-basmalah): Reciting 'Bismillah ir-Rahman ir-Rahim' before the Fatiha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Only in audible prayers
D) It is not recited at all

Key Takeaway
Reciting isti'adha and basmalah before the Fatiha in every rak'ah is a confirmed sunnah, to be done silently.

The Opening Supplication (Thana) in Prayer
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute on thana

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the opening supplication (thana) and evaluate the inter-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school prefers 'Subhanaka' for the opening supplication; the Shafi'i prefers 'Wajjahtu', and Abu Yusuf reconciles both.

After the opening takbir, the worshipper begins the prayer with a supplication. This lesson examines the Hanafi position on which supplication is best, the proofs from hadith, and the disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i and within the Hanafi school itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the opening supplication (thana) after takbir. The Hanafi ruling is that it is sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
Locate the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi school cites a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that the Prophet recited 'Subhanaka...' when standing for prayer at night.
3
Identify the opposing school's proof
Imam al-Shafi'i prefers 'Wajjahtu wajhi' based on a hadith from Ali ibn Abi Talib.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Imam Abu Yusuf, respecting both hadiths, recommends combining both supplications.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon Hanafi position is to recite 'Subhanaka' alone, but combining is acceptable.

Source Text

ويضعها تحت السرة (۱) ثم يقول سبحانك اللهم وبحمدک و تبارک اسمک و تعالى جدك ولا اله غیرک [۱۸۳] (۱۳) ويستعيذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم

مسنون ہے۔
يعتمد : پکڑیگا، السرة : ناف۔
(۱۸۲) (۱۲) تحریمہ باندھنے کے بعد پڑھے سبحانک اللهم وبحمدک و تبارک اسمک و تعالى جدك ولا اله غیرک تحریمہ باندھنے کے بعد اور بھی بہت سی دعائیں منقول ہیں لیکن حنفیہ کے نزدیک سبحانک اللهم الخ پڑھنازیادہ بہتر ہے
یہ حدیث ہے عن ابي سعيد الخدري قال كان رسول الله الله اذا قام الى الصلوة بالليل كبر ثم يقول سبحانك اللهم الخ (الف) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما یقول عند افتتاح الصلوۃ ص ۵۷ نمبر ۲۴۲ / ابوداؤد شریف، باب من رأی الاستفتاح بسماتک ص ۱۹ انمبر ۷۷۵ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سبحانک اللھم الخ پڑھنا چاہئے ۔ فائدہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک اللهم وجهت وجهی الخ پڑھنا زیادہ بہتر ہے۔ اس کا ثبوت یہ حدیث ہے عن علی بن ابی طالب قال كان رسول الله اذا قام الى الصلوة كبر ثم قال وجهت وجهي الخ (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب ما تسمح به الصلوة من الدعاء ص ۱۷ انمبر ۷۶۰) امام ابو یوسف ان دونوں احادیث کی وجہ سے دونوں دعاؤں کے ملانے کے قائل ہیں۔
يستو
[۱۸۳) (۱۳) اور اعوذ باللہ من الشیطان الرجیم اور بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم پڑھے۔ آیت میں ہے فاذا قرأت القرآن فاستعذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم (ج) ( آیت ۹۸ سورۃ النحل (۱۶) اس آیت سے معلوم هے که قرآت قرآن سے پہلے اعوذ باللہ الخ پڑھے۔ عن ابي سعيد الخدري قال كان رسول الله الله اذا قام الى الصلوة ثم يقول اعوذ بالله السميع العليم من الشيطان الرجيم ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما یقول عند افتتاح الصلوۃ ص ۵۷ نمبر ۲۴۲) اسی لئے حنفیہ کے نزدیک اعوذ باللہ قرآت قرآن کی سنت ہے۔ ثنا کی سنت نہیں ہے اس لئے ہر رکعت میں قرآت قرآن سے اعوذ باللہ الخ اور بسم اللہ الح پڑھے جائیں گے۔
He places them below the navel. Then he says: 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika, wa tabaraka ismuka, wa ta'ala jadduka, wa la ilaha ghayruka.' And he seeks refuge with Allah from the accursed Satan. It is sunnah. He relies: he grips, the navel. After tying the tahrima, he recites Subhanaka... After tying the tahrima, many other supplications are transmitted, but according to the Hanafis, reciting Subhanaka... is better. This is a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'When the Messenger of Allah stood for prayer at night, he would say the takbir and then say Subhanaka...' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud). This hadith indicates that Subhanaka... should be recited. Benefit: According to Imam al-Shafi'i, reciting 'Allahumma wajjahtu wajhi...' is better. Its proof is the hadith from 'Ali ibn Abi Talib: 'When the Messenger of Allah stood for prayer, he would say the takbir and then say Wajjahtu wajhi...' (Abu Dawud). Imam Abu Yusuf, due to these two hadiths, holds that both supplications should be combined. And he seeks refuge with Allah from the accursed Satan and recites Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim. The verse says: 'So when you recite the Quran, seek refuge with Allah from the accursed Satan' (Surah al-Nahl, 16:98). This verse indicates that before reciting the Quran, one should seek refuge. From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'When the Messenger of Allah stood for prayer, he would say A'udhu billahi al-sami' al-'alim min al-shaytan al-rajim' (Tirmidhi). For this reason, according to the Hanafis, ta'awwudh is sunnah for Quran recitation, not for thana. Therefore, in every rak'ah before reciting the Quran, ta'awwudh and Bismillah should be recited.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the opening supplication (thana) and seeking refuge (ta'awwudh) in prayer. The matn states that after placing hands below the navel, the worshipper recites the thana: 'Subhanaka...'. The commentary explains that this is sunnah, and the Hanafi school prefers this specific supplication over others that are also transmitted. A hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri is cited as proof. Then an inter-madhhab dispute is presented: Imam al-Shafi'i prefers the supplication 'Wajjahtu wajhi' based on a hadith from 'Ali. Imam Abu Yusuf, respecting both proofs, recommends combining the two supplications. The passage then addresses ta'awwudh (isti'adha), stating that it is sunnah to recite before Quran recitation in each rak'ah, not before the thana. This is supported by the Quranic verse (16:98) and a hadith from Abu Sa'id. The commentary emphasizes that according to the Hanafis, ta'awwudh is specifically for Quran recitation, not for the initial supplication, and it should be recited silently along with Bismillah in every rak'ah.

Key Terms
ثناء (thana): The opening supplication recited after the takbir tahrima, specifically 'Subhanaka Allahumma...'
تحریمہ (tahrima): The initial takbir (takbir al-ihram) that begins the prayer

Key Takeaway

Seeking Refuge (Ta'awwudh) Before Quran Recitation
Ruling with proof on ta'awwudh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) in prayer and its timing.

Core Idea
Ta'awwudh is sunnah before Quran recitation in every rak'ah, not before the opening supplication.

The Quran commands seeking refuge from Satan before reciting the Quran. In prayer, the Hanafi school applies this command by reciting 'A'udhu billah...' silently before the Fatiha in each rak'ah. This lesson clarifies the proof and the distinction from the thana.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) is sunnah before Quran recitation.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
Verse 16:98 commands seeking refuge before reciting the Quran.
3
Locate the sunnah proof
Hadith from Abu Sa'id that the Prophet would say 'A'udhu billahi al-sami' al-'alim' when standing for prayer.
4
Determine the Hanafi ruling
Ta'awwudh is for Quran recitation, not for thana; therefore it is recited before the Fatiha in every rak'ah.
5
Apply in practice
In each rak'ah, after the thana, before starting Qur'an, the worshipper silently recites the ta'awwudh and then basmalah.

ويضعها تحت السرة (۱) ثم يقول سبحانك اللهم وبحمدک و تبارک اسمک و تعالى جدك ولا اله غیرک [۱۸۳] (۱۳) ويستعيذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم

مسنون ہے۔
يعتمد : پکڑیگا، السرة : ناف۔
(۱۸۲) (۱۲) تحریمہ باندھنے کے بعد پڑھے سبحانک اللهم وبحمدک و تبارک اسمک و تعالى جدك ولا اله غیرک تحریمہ باندھنے کے بعد اور بھی بہت سی دعائیں منقول ہیں لیکن حنفیہ کے نزدیک سبحانک اللهم الخ پڑھنازیادہ بہتر ہے
یہ حدیث ہے عن ابي سعيد الخدري قال كان رسول الله الله اذا قام الى الصلوة بالليل كبر ثم يقول سبحانك اللهم الخ (الف) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما یقول عند افتتاح الصلوۃ ص ۵۷ نمبر ۲۴۲ / ابوداؤد شریف، باب من رأی الاستفتاح بسماتک ص ۱۹ انمبر ۷۷۵ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سبحانک اللھم الخ پڑھنا چاہئے ۔ فائدہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک اللهم وجهت وجهی الخ پڑھنا زیادہ بہتر ہے۔ اس کا ثبوت یہ حدیث ہے عن علی بن ابی طالب قال كان رسول الله اذا قام الى الصلوة كبر ثم قال وجهت وجهي الخ (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب ما تسمح به الصلوة من الدعاء ص ۱۷ انمبر ۷۶۰) امام ابو یوسف ان دونوں احادیث کی وجہ سے دونوں دعاؤں کے ملانے کے قائل ہیں۔
يستو
[۱۸۳) (۱۳) اور اعوذ باللہ من الشیطان الرجیم اور بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم پڑھے۔ آیت میں ہے فاذا قرأت القرآن فاستعذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم (ج) ( آیت ۹۸ سورۃ النحل (۱۶) اس آیت سے معلوم هے که قرآت قرآن سے پہلے اعوذ باللہ الخ پڑھے۔ عن ابي سعيد الخدري قال كان رسول الله الله اذا قام الى الصلوة ثم يقول اعوذ بالله السميع العليم من الشيطان الرجيم ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما یقول عند افتتاح الصلوۃ ص ۵۷ نمبر ۲۴۲) اسی لئے حنفیہ کے نزدیک اعوذ باللہ قرآت قرآن کی سنت ہے۔ ثنا کی سنت نہیں ہے اس لئے ہر رکعت میں قرآت قرآن سے اعوذ باللہ الخ اور بسم اللہ الح پڑھے جائیں گے۔
He places them below the navel. Then he says: 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika, wa tabaraka ismuka, wa ta'ala jadduka, wa la ilaha ghayruka.' And he seeks refuge with Allah from the accursed Satan. It is sunnah. He relies: he grips, the navel. After tying the tahrima, he recites Subhanaka... After tying the tahrima, many other supplications are transmitted, but according to the Hanafis, reciting Subhanaka... is better. This is a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'When the Messenger of Allah stood for prayer at night, he would say the takbir and then say Subhanaka...' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud). This hadith indicates that Subhanaka... should be recited. Benefit: According to Imam al-Shafi'i, reciting 'Allahumma wajjahtu wajhi...' is better. Its proof is the hadith from 'Ali ibn Abi Talib: 'When the Messenger of Allah stood for prayer, he would say the takbir and then say Wajjahtu wajhi...' (Abu Dawud). Imam Abu Yusuf, due to these two hadiths, holds that both supplications should be combined. And he seeks refuge with Allah from the accursed Satan and recites Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim. The verse says: 'So when you recite the Quran, seek refuge with Allah from the accursed Satan' (Surah al-Nahl, 16:98). This verse indicates that before reciting the Quran, one should seek refuge. From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'When the Messenger of Allah stood for prayer, he would say A'udhu billahi al-sami' al-'alim min al-shaytan al-rajim' (Tirmidhi). For this reason, according to the Hanafis, ta'awwudh is sunnah for Quran recitation, not for thana. Therefore, in every rak'ah before reciting the Quran, ta'awwudh and Bismillah should be recited.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the opening supplication (thana) and seeking refuge (ta'awwudh) in prayer. The matn states that after placing hands below the navel, the worshipper recites the thana: 'Subhanaka...'. The commentary explains that this is sunnah, and the Hanafi school prefers this specific supplication over others that are also transmitted. A hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri is cited as proof. Then an inter-madhhab dispute is presented: Imam al-Shafi'i prefers the supplication 'Wajjahtu wajhi' based on a hadith from 'Ali. Imam Abu Yusuf, respecting both proofs, recommends combining the two supplications. The passage then addresses ta'awwudh (isti'adha), stating that it is sunnah to recite before Quran recitation in each rak'ah, not before the thana. This is supported by the Quranic verse (16:98) and a hadith from Abu Sa'id. The commentary emphasizes that according to the Hanafis, ta'awwudh is specifically for Quran recitation, not for the initial supplication, and it should be recited silently along with Bismillah in every rak'ah.

Key Terms
تعوذ (ta'awwudh): Seeking refuge with Allah from Satan before Quran recitation, recited as 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim'
بسم اللہ (basmalah): The phrase 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' recited before Quranic recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafis, when is the ta'awwudh recited?
A) Only in the first rak'ah after thana
B) Before Quran recitation in every rak'ah
C) Only before the thana
D) Only in the last rak'ah

Key Takeaway
Ta'awwudh is sunnah before Quran recitation in every rak'ah, not before the thana.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Recitation of Basmala and Fatiha: Hanafi Rulings and Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling on silent basmala and wajib Fatiha with Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting Basmala (silent) and Surah al-Fatiha (wajib) in prayer, and explain the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Basmala is recited silently and is not part of al-Fatiha; reciting Fatiha is wajib, any verse fulfills fard.

This lesson examines the rulings on recitation in prayer. We will see why Hanafis recite Basmala silently and consider it separate from the surahs, and why they hold that reciting Surah al-Fatiha is a wajib that, if omitted, requires sajdah al-sahw. We will also explore the Shafi'i position that Basmala is part of al-Fatiha and should be recited aloud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: reciting Basmala in prayer and reciting Surah al-Fatiha. State the Hanafi ruling: Basmala is recited silently, not part of surahs; reciting any Quran verse is fard, but reciting Fatiha specifically is wajib.
The distinction between fard and wajib is crucial: fard omission invalidates prayer; wajib omission requires sajdah al-sahw.
2
Locate the dalil for Basmala
Identify the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Mughaffal (Tirmidhi, Bukhari, Muslim) where he reports that the Prophet and the caliphs did not recite Basmala aloud. Understand how this proves silent recitation.
The hadith explicitly states 'I did not hear any of them say it', indicating inaudible recitation.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i ikhtilaf
State the Shafi'i position: Basmala is part of al-Fatiha and each surah, so it must be recited aloud in loud prayers. Cite their proofs: hadith of Anas (Surah al-Kawthar) and Darqutni hadith of jahr.
The thamarah al-khilaf is practical: Hanaif recites silently, Shafi'is aloud in certain prayers.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi position on Fatiha
Understand that the fard of qira'ah is fulfilled by any verse (one long or three short), but reciting Fatiha is an additional wajib. If Fatiha is omitted, the prayer is valid but deficient, requiring sajdah al-sahw.
Proofs: Quran 73:20, hadith of Abu Sa'id, and hadith of the Bedouin in Bukhari.
5
Apply the recommendation
The text recommends reciting Basmala silently before each surah to avoid disagreement and act on caution. Recognize this as a tarjih based on caution.
This reflects the Hanafi principle of avoiding ikhtilaf where possible.

بسم اللہ الخ پڑھنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابن عباس قال كان النبي يفتتح صلواته ببسم الله الرحمن الرحيم (د) ( ترندی شریف، باب من رأی انبهر بسم الله الرحمن الرحیم ص ۵۷ نمبر ۲۳۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ قرآت سے پہلے بسم اللہ پڑھنا چاہئے۔ لیکن ہمیں یہ تذکرہ نہیں ہے کہ زور سے پڑھنا چاہئے ۔ ہو سکتا ہے کہ حضور مبسم اللہ تو پڑھتے ہوں لیکن آہستہ پڑھتے ہوں۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عبد الله بن مغفل قال سمعنى ابى والا في الصلوة اقول بسم ا الله الرحمن الرحيم فقال لی ای بنی محدث ایاک والحدث ... وقال وقد صليت مع النبي ، و مع ابي بكر وعمر ومع عثمان فلم اسمع احدا منهم يقولها فلا تقلها ، اذا انت صليت فقل الحمد لله رب العالمين (الف) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی ترک الجهر بسم الله الرحمان الرحیم ص نے ۵ نمبر ۲۴۴ بخاری شریف، باب ما یقول بعد التکبیر ص۱۰۳نمبر ۷۴۳ مسلم شریف ، باب حجته من قال لا گھر بالبسمات ص ۷۲ انمبر ۳۹۹) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ صحابہ بسم اللہ آہستہ پڑھتے تھے۔
وں یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ بسم اللہ الحمد للہ یا دوسری سورتوں کا جز نہیں ہے ورنہ بسم اللہ زور سے پڑھتے ۔
امام شافعی کے نزدیک بسم اللہ زور سے پڑھی جائے گی ۔ کیوں کہ وہ بسم اللہ والحمد کا جز مانتے ہیں اور سورت کا بھی جز مانتے ہیں۔ ان کی دلیل کی حدیث او پرگزری (۲) عن انس بن مالک قال بینا رسول الله ذات يوم بين اظهرنا اذا غفى اغفاء ة ثم رفع رأسه
متبسما فقلنا ما اضحكک یا رسول الله قال انزلت على انفا سورة فقرء بسم الله ارحمن الرحیم انا اعطیناک الكوثر الخ ( ب ) ( مسلم شریف ، باب حجبته من قال البسملة آیة من اول کل سورۃ سوی برائی ص ۷۲ انمبر ۴۰۰ را ابوداؤد شریف ، باب ما جاء من جهر بسم اللہ ص ۱۲۱ نمبر ۷۸۴ ) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ بسم اللہ سورۃ کا جز ہے۔ اس لئے اس کو جہری نماز میں جہر سے پڑھنا چاہئے۔ اس سے بھی واضح دلیل دار قطنی میں ہے عن ابن عباس ان رسول الله عمال اللي كان يجهر ببسم الله الرحمن الرحيم (ج) ( دارقطنی، باب وجوب قراءة بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم ج اول ص ۳۰۸ نمبر ۱۱۴۷) ان احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بسم اللہ کو جہری نماز میں جہری پڑھنا چاہئے ۔ بسم اللہ ہر سورۃ سے پہلے آہستہ سے پڑھ لے تو بہتر ہے تا کہ اختلاف سے بچ جائے اور احتیاط پر عمل ہو جائے۔
[۱۸] (۱۴) پھر سورۂ فاتحہ پڑھے۔ تشریح حنفیہ کے نزدیک قرآن کی کسی جگہ سے ایک بڑی آیت یا تین چھوٹی آیتیں پڑھنا فرض ہے۔ اگر اتنا بھی نہیں پڑھیگا تو نماز نہیں ہوگی۔ البتہ اس پر سورہ فاتحہ پڑھنا واجب ہے۔ اگر نہیں پڑھے گا تو کمی رہ جائے گی اور سجدہ سہو کرنا پڑے گا۔
(۱) کہیں سے بھی قرآن پڑھنے کی فرضیت کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے فقرء ما تيسر من القرآن (آیت ۲۰ سورة المزمل ۷۳) (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابن سعيد قال امرنا ان تقرء بفاتحة الكتاب وما تيسر (د) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب من ترك القراءة (الفاتحة) في صلوتہ بفاتحه الکتاب، ص ۱۲۵ نمبر ۸۱۸ر نسائی شریف، باب ایجاب قراءة فاتحة الكتاب في الصلوۃ ص ۱۰۵ نمبر ۹۱۲) (۳) بخاری شریف میں ہے آپ نے اس دیہاتی سے فرمایا جس نے جلدی جلدی نماز پڑھی ثم اقرء ما تيسر معك من القرآن (ه) ( بخاری )
The proof for reciting Bismillah is the hadith from Ibn 'Abbas: 'The Prophet used to begin his prayers with Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' (Tirmidhi). This hadith indicates that Bismillah should be recited before recitation. But we have no mention that it should be recited aloud. It is possible that the Prophet recited Bismillah but silently. The proof for this is the hadith from 'Abdullah ibn Mughaffal: 'My father heard me saying Bismillah in prayer and said: O my son, this is an innovation; beware of innovation... And he said: I prayed with the Prophet, Abu Bakr, 'Umar, and 'Uthman, and I did not hear any of them say it, so do not say it. When you pray, say Alhamdulillah...' (Tirmidhi, Bukhari, Muslim). From this it is known that the Companions recited Bismillah silently. It also became known that Bismillah is not part of Alhamdulillah or other surahs; otherwise they would have recited it aloud. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, Bismillah should be recited aloud because he considers it part of al-Fatiha and also part of the surah. Their proof is the hadith from Anas ibn Malik: 'While the Messenger of Allah was among us, he dozed off, then raised his head smiling... He said: A surah was just revealed to me, and he recited Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim, Inna a'tayna al-kawthar...' (Muslim, Abu Dawud). This indicates that Bismillah is part of the surah, so it should be recited aloud in loud prayers. An even clearer proof is in Darqutni from Ibn 'Abbas: 'The Messenger of Allah used to recite Bismillah aloud' (Darqutni). These hadiths indicate that Bismillah should be recited aloud in loud prayers. If one recites Bismillah silently before every surah, it is better to avoid disagreement and act on caution. Then he recites Surah al-Fatiha. Explanation: According to the Hanafis, reciting one long verse or three short verses from anywhere in the Quran is fard. If one does not recite even that, the prayer is not valid. However, reciting Surah al-Fatiha specifically is wajib. If one does not recite it, there is a deficiency and sajdah al-sahw becomes necessary. (1) The proof for the obligation of reciting some Quran is the verse: 'So recite what is easy from the Quran' (Surah al-Muzzammil, 73:20). (2) A hadith from Abu Sa'id: 'He commanded us to recite the Opening of the Book and whatever is easy' (Abu Dawud, Nasa'i). (3) In Bukhari, he said to the Bedouin who prayed hastily: 'Then recite what is easy from the Quran.'
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage covers the rulings on reciting Bismillah and Surah al-Fatiha in prayer. It begins by proving that Bismillah is recited before Quran recitation based on a hadith from Ibn 'Abbas. However, the text clarifies that the Prophet recited it silently, citing a hadith from 'Abdullah ibn Mughaffal, who reported that the Prophet and the first three caliphs did not recite Bismillah aloud. This shows that the Companions recited it silently, and that Bismillah is not part of al-Fatiha or other surahs; otherwise they would have recited it aloud. Then a major inter-madhhab dispute is presented: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that Bismillah is part of al-Fatiha and each surah, and therefore should be recited aloud in loud prayers. His proof includes the hadith of Anas where the Prophet recited Bismillah when Surah al-Kawthar was revealed, and a hadith from Darqutni that the Prophet recited Bismillah aloud. The text then gives a practical recommendation: reciting Bismillah silently before each surah is better to avoid disagreement and act on caution. After discussing Bismillah, the passage addresses Surah al-Fatiha. According to the Hanafis, reciting any portion of the Quran (one long verse or three short verses) is fard (obligatory) for the prayer's validity. However, reciting Surah al-Fatiha specifically is wajib; if one omits it, the prayer is valid but requires sajdah al-sahw. This is supported by the Quranic verse 'So recite what is easy from the Quran' and hadiths commanding recitation of Fatiha and whatever is easy.

Key Terms
فاتحة الكتاب (fatihah al-kitab): Surah al-Fatiha, which is wajib to recite in prayer according to Hanafis.
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم (bismillah al-rahman al-rahim): The basmala, recited silently before Quran recitation in prayer; not considered part of surahs.
سجدہ سہو (sajdah al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness required when a wajib act is omitted inadvertently.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person prays without reciting Surah al-Fatiha but recites another verse of the Quran?
A) The prayer is invalid (batil) because Fatiha is fard.
B) The prayer is valid but deficient, requiring sajdah al-sahw.
C) The prayer is valid and complete without any extra act.
D) The prayer is makruh and should be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Basmala is recited silently and is not part of any surah; reciting any verse is fard, but Fatiha is a wajib that requires sajdah al-sahw if omitted.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Reciting Basmalah Aloud vs Silently
Inter-madhhab dispute on basmalah recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on basmalah recitation, identify the opposing Shafi'i proof, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence of the dispute).

Core Idea
Basmalah is recited silently in Hanafi prayer; it is not part of the surah.

This passage addresses a well-known dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the recitation of the basmalah (بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم) in prayer. Understanding this dispute is crucial because it affects the actual performance of salah: whether the imam recites aloud or silently. Let us examine the evidence and reasoning on both sides.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
State clearly what the schools disagree on: is the basmalah recited aloud (jahr) or silently (israr) in loud prayers?
The disagreement stems from whether basmalah is considered a verse of the surah or an independent verse.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school holds that basmalah is recited silently in all prayers. Their primary evidence is the practice of the Companions, including a hadith that the Prophet recited it silently.
The hadith of Abdullah ibn Mughaffal explicitly says 'yukhfiha' (he concealed it).
3
Present the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that basmalah must be recited aloud in loud prayers because he considers it part of the surah. His evidence includes the hadith of Anas where the Prophet recited basmalah when Surah al-Kawthar was revealed, and a report from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet recited it aloud.
The Shafi'i proof relies on the assumption that reciting basmalah in these contexts proves it is part of the surah.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and thamarah al-khilaf
The Hanafi response is that those ahadith do not prove basmalah is part of the surah; the silent practice is more authentic and was followed by the Rightly Guided Caliphs. The practical consequence: in Hanafi prayer, the basmalah is never recited aloud; in Shafi'i prayer, it is recited aloud in jahr prayers.
This difference affects the imam's recitation and the follower's response.

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الاول ۱۳۶ كتاب الصلوة ويقرأ بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم ويسر بهما ( ۱۸۴](۱۴) ثم يقرأ فاتحة الكتاب اسمع احدا منهم يقولها فلا تقلها ، اذا انت صليت فقل الحمد لله رب العالمين (الف) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی ترک الجهر بسم الله الرحمان الرحیم ص نے ۵ نمبر ۲۴۴ بخاری شریف، باب ما یقول بعد التکبیر ص۱۰۳نمبر ۷۴۳ مسلم شریف ، باب حجته من قال لا گھر بالبسمات ص ۷۲ انمبر ۳۹۹) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ صحابہ بسم اللہ آہستہ پڑھتے تھے۔ وہ یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ بسم اللہ الحمد للہ یا دوسری سورتوں کا جز نہیں ہے ورنہ بسم اللہ زور سے پڑھتے ۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک بسم اللہ زور سے پڑھی جائے گی ۔ کیوں کہ وہ بسم اللہ والحمد کا جز مانتے ہیں اور سورت کا بھی جز مانتے ہیں۔ ان کی دلیل کی حدیث او پرگزری (۲) عن انس بن مالک قال بینا رسول الله ذات يوم بين اظهرنا اذا غفى اغفاء ة ثم رفع رأسه متبسما فقلنا ما اضحكک یا رسول الله قال انزلت على انفا سورة فقرء بسم الله ارحمن الرحیم انا اعطیناک الكوثر الخ ( ب ) ( مسلم شریف، باب حجبته من قال البسملة آیة من اول کل سورۃ سوی برائی ص ۷۲ انمبر ۴۰۰ را ابوداؤد شریف ، باب ما جاء من جهر بسم اللہ ص ۱۲۱ نمبر ۷۸۴ ) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ بسم اللہ سورۃ کا جز ہے۔ اس لئے اس کو جہری نماز میں جہر سے پڑھنا چاہئے۔ اس سے بھی واضح دلیل دار قطنی میں ہے عن ابن عباس ان رسول الله عمال اللي كان يجهر ببسم الله الرحمن الرحيم (ج) ( دارقطنی، باب وجوب قراءة بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم ج اول ص ۳۰۸ نمبر ۱۱۴۷) ان احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بسم اللہ کو جہری نماز میں جہری پڑھنا چاہئے ۔ بسم اللہ ہر سورۃ سے پہلے آہستہ سے پڑھ لے تو بہتر ہے تا کہ اختلاف سے بچ جائے اور احتیاط پر عمل ہو جائے۔
The Sharh al-Thamiri, part one, page 136, Book of Prayer. And he recites: 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' and recites them silently. (184)(14) Then he recites Fatiha al-Kitab. [Hadith: I never heard any one of them saying it, so do not say it. When you pray, say 'Alhamdu lillahi Rabbil alameen'.] (Al-Tirmidhi, chapter on leaving jahr with bismillah; al-Bukhari, chapter on what to say after takbir; Muslim, chapter on proof of those who say no jahr with basmalah) From this it is learned that the Companions recited bismillah silently. And it is also learned that bismillah is not part of 'Alhamdu lillah' or other surahs, otherwise they would have recited it aloud. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, bismillah should be recited loudly, because he considers bismillah part of 'Alhamd' and also part of the surah. His proof is the hadith mentioned earlier: (2) from Anas ibn Malik: 'One day while the Messenger of Allah was among us, he dozed off, then raised his head smiling. We asked, 'What makes you smile, O Messenger of Allah?' He said, 'A surah has just been revealed to me.' Then he recited: 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim, Inna a'taynakal kawthar...'' (Muslim, chapter on his proof that basmalah is a verse at the beginning of every surah except Bara'ah; Abu Dawud, chapter on what is reported about jahr with bismillah) From this it is learned that bismillah is part of the surah. Therefore it should be recited aloud in loud prayers. An even clearer proof is in al-Daraqutni: from Ibn Abbas that the Messenger of Allah used to recite 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' aloud. (Al-Daraqutni, chapter on obligation of reciting bismillah) From these ahadith it is learned that bismillah should be recited aloud in loud prayers. It is better to recite bismillah silently before every surah to avoid disagreement and act with caution.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the recitation of the basmalah (بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم) in prayer. The Hanafi position, based on the practice of the Companions as reported in authentic hadith, is that the basmalah should be recited silently (israr) in both loud and silent prayers. The text explains that Abdullah ibn Mughaffal reported that he never heard the Prophet or the Rightly Guided Caliphs recite it aloud, and he advised his son not to recite it aloud. This indicates that the basmalah is not part of Surah al-Fatiha or any other surah; rather, it is an independent verse for separation and blessing. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the basmalah must be recited aloud in loud prayers because he considers it a verse of both Surah al-Fatiha and every other surah (except Surah al-Tawbah). His evidence includes the hadith of Anas where the Prophet recited basmalah when reciting Surah al-Kawthar, and the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet used to recite it aloud. The Hanafi response is implicit: these ahadith show that the basmalah was recited by the Prophet, but they do not prove that it is part of the surah. The Hanafis consider it a separate verse, and the silent recitation is the established practice of the Companions, which takes precedence. The text concludes that it is better to recite the basmalah silently before every surah to avoid the difference of opinion and to act with caution.

Key Terms
بسملة (basmalah): The phrase 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' recited before Quranic surahs.
جهر (jahr): Reciting aloud such that others can hear.
إسرار (israr): Reciting silently such that only the reciter can hear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for the Hanafi position that basmalah is recited silently?
A) The hadith that the Prophet recited basmalah when Surah al-Kawthar was revealed.
B) The practice of the Companions and the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mughaffal that the Prophet recited basmalah silently.
C) The Quranic verse commanding silence during prayer.
D) The consensus of all four imams.

Key Takeaway
The basmalah is recited silently in Hanafi prayer because it is not part of the surah, a position supported by the practice of the Companions.

Ruling on Saying Ameen Softly
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on saying Ameen softly, identify the proofs from Quran and Hadith, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i/Maliki position, including the practical consequence of the difference.

Core Idea
Ameen is a supplication; all non-Quranic supplications in prayer are said softly.

This lesson addresses a common point of difference between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i/Maliki schools: whether Ameen should be said softly or loudly after Surah al-Fatiha. The source text presents the Hanafi position with its proofs, then fairly states the opposing view and explains why the Hanafi school prefers softness. You will learn not only the ruling but also the method of weighing evidence in fiqh disputes.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school rules regarding saying Ameen: it is said softly by both the imam and the follower.
2
Identify the Hanafi proofs
Locate the three proofs the text presents: the Quranic verse (7:55), the hadith of lowering the voice (Tirmidhi), and the analogy (qiyas) to other supplications in prayer.
The Quranic verse is used to establish the general principle that supplication is done in secret.
3
State the opposing position
Identify the views of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik: saying Ameen loudly is better.
4
Identify the opposing proofs
Locate the two proofs the opposing school uses: the general hadith from Bukhari/Muslim (without mention of loudness) and the hadith of loud Ameen from Ibn Majah.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response and conclude
Understand the Hanafi critique: the Bukhari/Muslim hadith does not specify volume, and the loudness narration is not in the most authentic sources; moreover, Abu Hurayrah himself said the Companions abandoned it. Conclude that this is a difference in preference (istihbab) and not a matter of rebuke.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is that a Hanafi imam says Ameen softly, while a Shafi'i imam says it loudly. Both are valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۸۶) (۱۶) اور جب امام کہے ولا الضالین تو وہ آمین کہے اور مقتدی بھی آمین کہے اور اس کو آہستہ کہے۔ امام سورہ فاتحہ پڑھ کر آمین کہے اور مقتدی بھی آمین کہے۔ لیکن دونوں آمین آہستہ کہے۔ (۱) عن ابي هريرة ان رسول الله الله اذا امن الامام فامينوا فانه من وافق تأمينه تأمين الملائكة غفر له ما تقدم من ذنبه وقال ابن شهاب وكان رسول الله الله يقول آمين (د) ( بخاری شریف ، باب جهر الامام بالتا مين ص ۰۷ انمبر ۷۸۰ مسلم شریف ، باب ا ب التسميع والتحميد والتأمین ص ۷۶ انمبر ۴۱۰ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آمین کہے ۔ اور آہستہ آمین کہنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے (۱) حضرت امام اعظم کی نگاہ اس بات کی طرف گئی کہ آمین دعا ہے اور نماز میں قرآت کے علاوہ جتنی دعائیں کی جاتی ہیں سب آہستہ ہیں۔ اس لئے آمین بھی آہستہ ہونی چاہئے ۔ چنانچہ حضرت نے آہستہ والی حدیث پر عمل کیا۔ آداب دعا یہ ہیں کہ گڑ گڑا کر آہستہ کی جائے ۔ آیت یہ ہے ادعوا ربكم تضرعا و خفية انه لا يحب المعتدين (الف) ( آیت ۵۵ سورة الاعراف ۷ ) (۲) حدیث میں بھی ہے عن بن وائل عن ابيه ان النبي عل الله قرء غير المغضوب عليهم ولا الضالين فقال آمين و خفض بها صوته (ب) (ترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الامین ص ۵۸ نمبر ۲۴۸ / دار قطنی ، باب التامين في الصلوة بعد فاتحته الكتاب والمجهر بها، ج اول ص ۳۲۸ نمبر ۱۲۵۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آمین آہستہ کہنا چاہئے ۔ بخاری، مسلم وغیرہ میں زور سے آمین کہنے کی باضابطه حدیث نہیں ہے۔ نامه امام شافعی اور امام مالک کی نزد یک آمین زور سے کہنا بہتر ہے۔ ان کی دلیل (۱) اوپر کی حدیث سے امام بخاری اور امام مسلم نے استدلال کیا ہے کہ زور سے آمین کہے (اگر چہ اس میں زور کا لفظ نہیں ہے ) (۲) عن ابی ھریرة قــال تــرك الناس التأمين وكان رسول الله اذا قال غير المغضوب عليهم ولا الضالين قال آمين حتى يسمعها اهل الصف الاول فيرتج بها المسجد ( ج ) (ابن ماجہ شریف، باب الجهر بآمین ص ۱۲۱ نمبر ۸۵۳ر دار قطنی ، باب التأمین فی الصلوۃ ج اول ص ۳۲۸ نمبر ۱۲۵۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آمین زور سے کہنا چاہئے۔ لیکن خود ابو ہریرہ فرماتے ہیں کہ صحابہ نے زور سے آمین کہنا چھوڑ دیا تھا۔ یہ استحباب کا اختلاف ہے۔ کوئی زور سے آمین کہتا ہو تو اس پر نکیر نہیں کرنا چاہئے۔
[186] (16) And when the imam says '...wa la al-dallin', he should say Ameen, and the follower should also say Ameen, and he should say it softly. The imam, after reciting Surah al-Fatiha, should say Ameen, and the follower also says Ameen, but both say Ameen softly. (1) From Abu Hurayrah that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'When the imam says Ameen, then say Ameen, for indeed whoever's Ameen coincides with the Ameen of the angels, his previous sins will be forgiven.' And Ibn Shihab said: 'The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) used to say Ameen.' (d) (Bukhari, chapter on imam saying Ameen aloud, p. 107 no. 780; Muslim, chapter on hearing and praising and Ameen, p. 76 no. 410). From this hadith it is known that one should say Ameen. And the proof for saying Ameen softly is the following: Imam al-A'zam's consideration was that Ameen is a supplication, and all supplications in prayer other than Quranic recitation are said softly, so Ameen should also be said softly. Accordingly, he acted on the hadith indicating softness. The etiquette of supplication is to supplicate humbly and softly. The verse is: 'Call upon your Lord in humility and privately; indeed, He does not like transgressors.' (a) (Surah al-A'raf 7:55). (2) Also in the hadith from Ibn Wa'il from his father that the Prophet (ﷺ) recited 'ghayr al-maghdubi 'alayhim wa la al-dallin' and said Ameen, lowering his voice with it. (b) (Tirmidhi, chapter on what has come about Ameen, p. 58 no. 248; Darqutni, chapter on saying Ameen in prayer after Fatiha and aloud, vol. 1 p. 328 no. 1256). This hadith indicates that Ameen should be said softly. In Bukhari, Muslim, etc., there is no explicit hadith for saying Ameen loudly. However, Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik hold that saying Ameen loudly is better. Their evidence: (1) The above hadith from Bukhari and Muslim, from which they infer that Ameen should be said loudly (even though the word 'loudly' is not in it). (2) From Abu Hurayrah who said: 'The people left Ameen, and the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) when he said '...ghayr al-maghdubi 'alayhim wa la al-dallin', he said Ameen such that the people of the first row could hear it, and the mosque would reverberate with it.' (c) (Ibn Majah, chapter on saying Ameen aloud, p. 121 no. 853; Darqutni, chapter on saying Ameen in prayer, vol. 1 p. 328 no. 1253). This hadith indicates that Ameen should be said loudly. But Abu Hurayrah himself states that the Companions had left saying Ameen aloud. This is a difference in istihbab (preference). If someone says Ameen loudly, one should not rebuke him.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with evidence and an inter-madhhab dispute on the manner of saying Ameen in prayer. The matn instructs that both the imam and the follower should say Ameen softly after completing Surah al-Fatiha. The commentary first cites the famous hadith from Abu Hurayrah commanding Ameen when the imam says it, but notes that the proof for saying it softly is based on Imam Abu Hanifa's reasoning: Ameen is a supplication, and all non-Quranic supplications in prayer are said softly. This is supported by the Quranic verse (7:55) and a hadith from Ibn Wa'il where the Prophet lowered his voice when saying Ameen. The commentator then addresses the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik, who prefer saying Ameen loudly, citing the general hadith and another narration where the Prophet's Ameen was heard by the first row. The commentator notes that the loudness narration is not explicit in Bukhari and Muslim, and that even Abu Hurayrah, who transmitted it, later said the Companions abandoned loud Ameen. The passage concludes by recognizing this as a difference in preference (istihbab), not a matter of obligation or prohibition, and discourages rebuking those who say it loudly.

Key Terms
آمین (āmīn): A word said after Fatiha, meaning 'O Allah, respond' or 'accept our supplication'.
آہستہ (āhistah): Softly, in a low voice, not audible to others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why should Ameen be said softly?
A) Because the Prophet always said it softly.
B) Because Ameen is a supplication, and supplications in prayer are said softly.
C) Because the Quran commands to make the prayer audible.
D) Because the followers cannot hear the imam otherwise.

Key Takeaway
Saying Ameen softly is the established Hanafi position, but it is a difference of preference; one should not rebuke those who say it loudly.

Takbir When Going into Ruku' (تکبیر رکوع)
Ruling statement with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that saying takbir when going into ruku' is sunnah muakkadah and cite the hadith proof from Bukhari.

Core Idea
Saying 'Allahu Akbar' when moving into ruku' is the Prophet's sunnah, not a wajib requirement.

This lesson examines a brief but key ruling from the chapter on salah: the takbir for ruku'. The matn instructs the imam to say takbir when going into ruku, and the commentary provides a hadith from Abu Hurayrah to support it. Understanding this ruling clarifies the nature of the takbirat al-intiqal in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is saying 'Allahu Akbar' when moving into ruku'. The ruling level is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah).
This is not wajib or fard in the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentary cites a hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari (no. 789) in which Abu Hurayrah describes the Prophet's practice.
The hadith is sahih and muttasil.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith states 'then he would say takbir when he went into ruku’.' This indicates consistent action, establishing sunnah.
The phrase 'thumma yukabbiru hina yarka‘u' is the operative evidence.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g. Shafi‘is) consider takbir al-intiqal wajib. The Hanafi view is sunnah based on the zanni dalala of the hadith.
This difference affects whether sajdah al-sahw is needed if omitted.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that it is sunnah muakkadah; the prayer remains valid if omitted.
All Hanafi authorities agree on this.

(w) (Bukhari, chapter on takbir when rising from prostration, p. 109 no. 789). From this hadith it is known that one should say takbir when going into ruku'.

Commentary
This is a brief ruling statement with a proof. The matn instructs that after recitation, the imam should say takbir (Allahu Akbar) while moving into ruku'. The commentary provides a hadith from Abu Hurayrah that the Prophet would say takbir upon standing and then when going into ruku'. The hadith establishes the practice (sunnah) of saying takbir for the transitions in prayer. The phrasing 'then he would say takbir when he went into ruku'' is the specific evidence for this action.

Key Terms
تکبیر (takbīr): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' to mark the transition between postures in prayer.
رکوع (rukūʿ): Bowing posture in prayer, where the hands are placed on the knees and the back is straight.

Posture of Ruku' in Salah
Ruling statement detailing the sunnah posture of ruku'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the sunnah posture of ruku' and apply it to your salah.

Core Idea
Ruku' is performed with straight back, spread fingers on knees, and a balanced head position.

The proper posture in ruku' is not just bending forward; it is a deliberate act of humility with specific sunnah details. This lesson outlines the recommended hand placement, finger spread, back alignment, and head level, all of which contribute to a complete and mindful bow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four actions
Read the text and list the four explicit instructions: (1) both hands on both knees, (2) spread fingers, (3) make back straight, (4) do not raise or lower head excessively.
These are the sunnah components of ruku' posture.
2
Understand the hand placement
The hands are placed firmly on the knees, as if leaning on them. This provides stability and indicates the degree of bowing.
The fingers are spread, not clenched, to maximize contact and humility.
3
Visualize the back and head
The back must be straight, forming a flat surface. The head should be level with the back—neither raised nor lowered excessively.
Excessive raising or lowering breaks the natural alignment.
4
Recognize the ruling level
These actions are sunnah (recommended), not fard or wajib. Omitting them does not invalidate salah but reduces its perfection.
The obligatory element of ruku' is the act of bowing itself.

Saying Ameen Quietly in Prayer: Hanafi vs Shafi'i/Maliki
Inter-madhhab dispute on saying Ameen in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prefers saying Ameen quietly and evaluate the Shafi'i/Maliki counter-argument.

Core Idea
Ameen is a supplication; all supplications in prayer are whispered – therefore Ameen is said quietly.

In the Hanafi school, saying Ameen after Surah al-Fatihah is a sunnah act. However, the manner of saying it – quietly or loudly – is a matter of scholarly difference. This lesson examines the evidence from both sides and the Hanafi position based on the nature of Ameen as a supplication.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its ruling level
Identify that the Hanafi school considers saying Ameen quietly as the preferred (afdal) practice, with a ruling level of sunnah muakkadah.
This is not a fard or wajib; it is a recommended act.
2
Identify the proof for quiet Ameen
Locate the Hanafi evidence: the Quranic verse commanding humble and quiet supplication (Surah al-A'raf 7:55) and the hadith where the Prophet lowered his voice when saying Ameen.
The hadith is from Tirmidhi and Dar Qutni.
3
Identify the Shafi'i/Maliki position and their proof
Note that Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik consider saying Ameen loudly as better. Their evidence is a deduction from Bukhari/Muslim and the hadith of Abu Hurairah that the mosque reverberated with Ameen.
The word 'loud' is not explicit in their primary sources.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to the opposing proofs
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal: the hadith of Abu Hurairah actually shows that the Companions later stopped saying loudly, and the general principle of quiet du'a takes precedence over weak implication.
The principle is derived from Quran 7:55 and the general practice of the Prophet.
5
Note the practical consequence and proper attitude
Recognize the thamarah: a Hanafi follower says Ameen quietly; a Shafi'i follower says it loudly. Both prayers are valid, and one should not criticize the other, as it is a difference of preference (istihbab).
The author emphasizes that this is not a fundamental difference.

Source Text

And not of those who go astray, he says Ameen, and the follower says it and conceals it. Then he says takbeer and bows. And places his hands on his knees, spreads his fingers, straightens his back, and does not raise his head nor lower it. From this hadith it is known that one should say Ameen. And the proof for saying Ameen quietly is this hadith: (1) Imam Abu Hanifa considered that Ameen is a supplication, and all supplications in prayer besides recitation are quiet. Therefore, Ameen should also be quiet. So the Imam acted upon the hadith that indicates quietness. The etiquette of supplication is to plead quietly. The verse is: 'Call upon your Lord humbly and quietly; indeed, He does not like transgressors.' (Surah al-A'raf, 7:55) (2) Also in hadith: from 'Alqamah from his father that the Prophet recited 'Ghairil maghdubi alaihim walad-dallin' and said Ameen, lowering his voice with it. From this hadith it is known that Ameen should be said quietly. In Bukhari and Muslim, there is no explicit hadith for saying Ameen loudly. As for Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik, according to them saying Ameen loudly is better. Their evidence: (1) From the above hadith, Imam Bukhari and Imam Muslim deduced that Ameen is said loudly (even though the word 'loud' is not in it). (2) From Abu Hurairah who said: 'The people had left saying Ameen, and when the Messenger of Allah said 'Ghairil maghdubi alaihim walad-dallin', he would say Ameen until the people of the first row would hear it and the mosque would reverberate with it.' From this hadith it is known that Ameen should be said loudly. But Abu Hurairah himself says that the Companions had left saying Ameen loudly. This is a difference of preference. If someone says Ameen loudly, one should not criticize him.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether Ameen is said quietly or loudly in prayer. The author first states the Hanafi position: the follower says Ameen quietly after the Imam. The Hanafi proof is based on two sources: (1) a general principle that Ameen is a supplication, and all supplications in prayer except Quran recitation are whispered, supported by the verse 'Call upon your Lord humbly and quietly'; (2) a specific hadith where the Prophet lowered his voice when saying Ameen. The opposing view of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik is then presented: they consider it better to say Ameen loudly. Their evidence includes (1) a deduction from a hadith in Bukhari and Muslim that implies loudness, and (2) a hadith from Abu Hurairah stating that the mosque would reverberate with the sound of Ameen. The author notes that Abu Hurairah himself later reported that the Companions had stopped saying Ameen loudly. The passage concludes that this is a difference in istihbab (preference), and one should not criticize someone who chooses the other opinion.

Key Terms
آمین (Ameen): A word said after reciting Surah al-Fatihah meaning 'O Allah, respond'.
تضّرعاً و خفیة (tadharru'an wa khufyah): Supplication with humility and quietly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because Ameen is a supplication, and all supplications in prayer are whispered
C) Because the Prophet never said Ameen aloud
D) Because the follower should not be heard

Key Takeaway
Saying Ameen quietly is the preferred Hanafi position based on the principle that all supplications in prayer are whispered; the difference with Shafi'is is one of recommendation, not obligation.

Takbeer and Posture of Ruku'
Ruling and proof for takbeer at ruku' and the posture.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah muakkadah of saying takbeer when going into ruku' and describe the proper posture (hands on knees, fingers spread, back straight) with their hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Saying takbeer when bowing and adopting a balanced posture are sunnah muakkadah confirmed by the Prophet's practice.

This passage provides clear hadith evidence for two important sunan of ruku': the opening takbeer and the bodily posture. While ruku' itself is a pillar, these actions complete its sunnah form and are emphasized in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the action and its ruling
Recognize that the takbeer for ruku' and the specific posture are sunnah muakkadah, not obligatory. The ruku' itself is a pillar.
2
Locate the hadith for takbeer
Find the hadith of Abu Hurairah (Bukhari) where the Prophet said takbeer when bowing.
This proves the takbeer is sunnah.
3
Analyze the posture hadith
From Abu Humaid's hadith (Tirmidhi, Nasa'i), extract the elements: hands on knees, fingers spread, back straight, head neither raised nor lowered.
The hands resemble a bowstring.
4
Distinguish rukn from sunnah
Note that omitting the takbeer or perfect posture does not invalidate the prayer; these are not pillars.

(187) (17) Then he says takbeer and bows. In a hadith: He used to say takbeer in ruku' and sujud: I heard Abu Hurairah saying: When the Messenger of Allah stood for prayer, he said takbeer when standing, then he said takbeer when bowing. From this hadith it is known that one says takbeer while going into ruku'. [188] (18) He places both hands on both knees, spreads his fingers, straightens his back, does not raise his head nor lower it excessively. In ruku', he grips his knees with his hands as if leaning on them, and keeps his fingers spread on the knees. His back straight and [he does not lower it?] (1) This is a hadith: They mentioned the prayer of the Messenger of Allah, and Abu Humaid said: I am the most knowledgeable among you of the prayer of the Messenger of Allah. The Messenger of Allah bowed, placed his hands on his knees, as if he was gripping them, and he made his hands like a bowstring and kept them away from his sides. From this hadith it is known that he grips the knees with his hands in a manner resembling a bowstring. (2) In a hadith from Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi: The Prophet, when he bowed, would keep his back straight, not raise his head nor lower it, and placed his hands on his knees. From this hadith it is known that in ruku' one should not let the head be level with the back nor lower it excessively. [189] (19) And in his ruku', he says: 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azeem' three times, and this is the minimum. Saying 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azeem' at least three times is sunnah. He may say more, but odd numbers are better. From Ibn Mas'ud: The Prophet said: When one of you bows and says in his ruku' 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azeem' three times, his ruku' is complete, and that is the minimum. [190] (20) Then he raises his head and says: 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah', and the follower says: 'Rabbana lakal hamd'. Explanation: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the imam says only 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah', and the follower says only 'Rabbana lakal hamd'. In a hadith from Abu Hurairah: The Messenger of Allah said: When the imam says 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah', then say 'Allahumma Rabbana lakal hamd'. From this it is known that the imam says 'Sami'a Allahu' and the follower says 'Rabbana lakal hamd'. If one prays alone, since he is both imam and follower, he says both.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage presents several rulings concerning the act of ruku' in prayer. First, when going into ruku', one says the takbeer (Allahu Akbar), based on the hadith of Abu Hurairah. Second, the posture of ruku': the hands are placed on the knees, fingers spread, back straight, head neither raised nor lowered. The hadith of Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi describes that the Prophet's hands on his knees looked like a bowstring, and another hadith emphasizes keeping the back level. Third, the tasbeeh in ruku': the minimum is to say 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azeem' three times, and it is preferred to say odd numbers higher than three. Fourth, when rising from ruku', the imam says 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' and the follower says 'Rabbana lakal hamd'. The munfarid (one praying alone) says both. These rulings are supported by explicit hadith from Bukhari, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i, and Abu Dawud.

Key Terms
رکوع (ruku'): Bowing in prayer, a pillar (rukn).
تکبیر (takbeer): Saying 'Allahu Akbar'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Tasbeeh in Ruku': Minimum and Preferred Count
Ruling and proof for the tasbeeh in ruku'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum number of tasbeeh in ruku' (three times), explain why odd numbers are preferred, and cite the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud.

Core Idea
The minimum tasbeeh in ruku' is three; more in odd numbers is sunnah.

This passage addresses the tasbeeh recited during ruku'. It establishes the minimum as three times, with the option to say more, preferably in odd numbers. The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud provides the direct proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the action and its ruling
The tasbeeh 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azeem' in ruku' is sunnah muakkadah.
2
Extract the minimum
The text states 'three times' as the minimum (adna).
This is the least required to fulfill the sunnah.
3
Note the preference for odd numbers
Odd numbers (5, 7, 9, etc.) are better based on general sunnah.
This is consistent with other acts of dhikr.
4
Locate the hadith
The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (Tirmidhi) says three times completes the ruku'.
This establishes the minimum.

Then he says takbeer and bows (1) (18) And he rests his hands on his knees, spreads his fingers, straightens his back, and does not raise his head nor lower it. (187) (17) Then he says takbeer and bows. In a hadith: He used to say takbeer in ruku' and sujud: I heard Abu Hurairah saying: When the Messenger of Allah stood for prayer, he said takbeer when standing, then he said takbeer when bowing. From this hadith it is known that one says takbeer while going into ruku'. [188] (18) He places both hands on both knees, spreads his fingers, straightens his back, does not raise his head nor lower it excessively. In ruku', he grips his knees with his hands as if leaning on them, and keeps his fingers spread on the knees. His back straight and [he does not lower it?] (1) This is a hadith: They mentioned the prayer of the Messenger of Allah, and Abu Humaid said: I am the most knowledgeable among you of the prayer of the Messenger of Allah. The Messenger of Allah bowed, placed his hands on his knees, as if he was gripping them, and he made his hands like a bowstring and kept them away from his sides. From this hadith it is known that he grips the knees with his hands in a manner resembling a bowstring. (2) In a hadith from Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi: The Prophet, when he bowed, would keep his back straight, not raise his head nor lower it, and placed his hands on his knees. From this hadith it is known that in ruku' one should not let the head be level with the back nor lower it excessively. [189] (19) And in his ruku', he says: 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azeem' three times, and this is the minimum. Saying 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azeem' at least three times is sunnah. He may say more, but odd numbers are better. From Ibn Mas'ud: The Prophet said: When one of you bows and says in his ruku' 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azeem' three times, his ruku' is complete, and that is the minimum. [190] (20) Then he raises his head and says: 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah', and the follower says: 'Rabbana lakal hamd'. Explanation: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the imam says only 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah', and the follower says only 'Rabbana lakal hamd'. In a hadith from Abu Hurairah: The Messenger of Allah said: When the imam says 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah', then say 'Allahumma Rabbana lakal hamd'. From this it is known that the imam says 'Sami'a Allahu' and the follower says 'Rabbana lakal hamd'. If one prays alone, since he is both imam and follower, he says both.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage presents several rulings concerning the act of ruku' in prayer. First, when going into ruku', one says the takbeer (Allahu Akbar), based on the hadith of Abu Hurairah. Second, the posture of ruku': the hands are placed on the knees, fingers spread, back straight, head neither raised nor lowered. The hadith of Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi describes that the Prophet's hands on his knees looked like a bowstring, and another hadith emphasizes keeping the back level. Third, the tasbeeh in ruku': the minimum is to say 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azeem' three times, and it is preferred to say odd numbers higher than three. Fourth, when rising from ruku', the imam says 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' and the follower says 'Rabbana lakal hamd'. The munfarid (one praying alone) says both. These rulings are supported by explicit hadith from Bukhari, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i, and Abu Dawud.

Key Terms
سبحان ربی العظیم (Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azeem): Glory be to my Lord, the Magnificent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, what indicates that three tasbeehs complete the ruku'?
A) The Prophet said 'that is the minimum'.
B) The Prophet said 'his ruku' is complete'.
C) The Prophet said 'it is wajib'.
D) The Prophet demonstrated it.

Key Takeaway
Saying 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azeem' three times in ruku' is the sunnah minimum; more in odd numbers is preferred.

Salah — Prayer

Rising from Ruku': Phrases for Imam, Follower, and Munfarid
Ruling and proof for the phrases said when rising from ruku'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the phrases said by the imam (Sami'a Allahu), the follower (Rabbana lakal hamd), and the one praying alone (both), with the hadith proof.

Core Idea
When rising from ruku', the imam says Sami'a Allahu; the follower says Rabbana lakal hamd; the munfarid says both.

This passage clarifies the distinct phrases recited when rising from ruku'. It provides a clear division of roles based on the hadith of Abu Hurairah, and explains the position of the one praying alone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the role of the imam
The imam says 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' upon rising.
This is a dhikr and also informs the followers.
2
Identify the role of the follower
The follower says 'Rabbana lakal hamd' (or 'Allahumma Rabbana lakal hamd').
The hadith commands the followers to say this.
3
Apply to the munfarid
The one praying alone combines both phrases because he acts as both imam and follower.
Says 'Sami'a Allahu' then 'Rabbana lakal hamd'.
4
Locate the hadith
The hadith of Abu Hurairah (Bukhari, Tirmidhi) states: 'When the imam says Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, then say Allahumma Rabbana lakal hamd.'
This is the proof for the distinction.

Ruku' Posture and Tasbih: Sunnah Acts Backed by Prophetic Practice
Describes correct ruku' posture and threefold tasbih recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi sunnah rulings for ruku' posture and tasbih, and explain how the hadith proofs establish these as sunnah rather than obligatory.

Core Idea
In ruku', sunnah posture has head level with buttocks; sunnah tasbih is three times 'Subhana Rabbiya al-'Azim'.

Ruku' is a pillar of prayer, but its perfect form includes specific postures and recitations established by the Prophet's practice. This lesson examines the two key sunnah acts within ruku': the correct alignment of the head and hands, and the minimum tasbih. You will learn how the Hanafi school derives these rulings from authentic hadith and why they are considered sunnah mu'akkadah rather than wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sunnah acts
Read the passage carefully and note that it covers two distinct aspects of ruku': (a) the posture (head level, hands on knees) and (b) the recitation (tasbih three times).
These are separate sunnah, each with its own proof.
2
Examine the dalil for posture
The author cites two hadith from Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi describing the Prophet's ruku': he placed his hands on his knees and kept his back straight, not raising or lowering his head. This describes the ideal form.
The absence of an explicit command indicates sunnah, not fard.
3
Examine the dalil for tasbih
The hadith from Ibn Mas'ud states that saying 'Subhana Rabbiya al-'Azim' three times completes the ruku', and that is its minimum. The author notes that more is allowed but odd numbers are preferred.
The hadith uses 'fala ka' structure indicating a recommended minimum.
4
Determine the hukm level using Hanafi usul
Neither hadith contains an imperative (amr) that would indicate obligation. Hanafi usul classifies actions described without commands as sunnah (recommended). Thus both the posture and the threefold tasbih are sunnah mu'akkadah.
If there were a command, it would be wajib. The absence makes it sunnah.

ینکسه [۱۹۱۸۹) ويقول في ركوعه سبحان ربی العظيم ثلثا و ذلک ادناه [۱۹۰] شرح: رکوع میں سر کو سرین کے برابر رکھے۔ سر کو نہ زیادہ جھکائے اور نہ پیٹھ سے اٹھا کر رکھے۔ بلکہ پیٹھ کے برابر رکھے۔ صلى (۱) یہ حدیث ہے فذكروا صلوة رسول الله الله فقال ابو حميد انا اعلمكم بصلوة رسول الله الله ان رسول لله ركع فوضع يديه على ركبتيه كانه قابض عليهما و وتريديه فنحاهما عن جنبيه (الف) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء يجافی یدیہ عن جنبیہ فی الرکوع ص ۶۰ نمبر ۲۶۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہاتھ سے گھٹنوں کو اس طرح پکڑے کہ کمان کی رسی کی طرح معلوم ہو (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابی حمید الساعدى قال كان النبي الا الله اذا ركع اعتدل فلم ينصب رأسه ولم يقنعه ووضع يديه على ركبتيه (ب) ( نسائی شریف، باب الاعتدال فی الرکوع ص ۱۸ امبر ۱۰۴۰ را ابوداؤد شریف ، بان صلوۃ من لا یقیم صلبه فی الرکوع والسجو دص ۱۳۲ نمبر ۸۶۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ رکوع میں نہ سر کو سرین کے برابر رکھے نہ جھکائے اور نہ زیادہ اٹھائے۔ لاینکہ : نہ زیادہ جھکائے۔ [۱۸] (۱۹) اور رکوع میں سبحان ربی العظیم تین مرتبہ کہے اور یہ اس کا ادنی درجہ ہے۔ کم سے کم تین مرتبہ سبحان ربی العظیم کہنا سنت ہے۔ اس سے زیادہ بھی کہہ سکتا ہے۔ لیکن طاق مرتبہ کہنا افضل ہے۔ صلى الله عن ابن مسعود ان النبي الله قال اذا ركع احدكم فقال ركوعه سبحان ربی العظيم ثلث مرات فقد تم ركوعه وذلك ادناه (ج) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی التسبیح فی الرکوع والسجود ص ۶۰ نمبر ۲۶ / ابوداؤد شریف ، باب ما یقول الرجل في ركوععدد سجوده ص ۱۳۴ نمبر ۸۷۰)
He should not lower it [19189?]. He says in his ruku' 'Subhana Rabbiya al-'Azim' three times, and that is its minimum [190]. Explanation: In ruku', he should place his head level with his buttocks. He should not lower his head too much nor raise it above the back. Rather, it should be level with the back. (1) This is a hadith: They mentioned the prayer of the Messenger of Allah, so Abu Humaid said: I am the most knowledgeable among you of the prayer of the Messenger of Allah. When the Messenger of Allah bowed, he placed his hands on his knees as if grasping them, and he [??] and kept them away from his sides. (al-Tirmidhi, chapter on placing hands away from sides in ruku', p. 60, no. 260) From this hadith it is understood that he should grasp the knees with his hands in a way that resembles a bowstring. (2) In a hadith from Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi, he said: The Prophet, when he bowed, was balanced; he did not raise his head nor lower it, and he placed his hands on his knees. (al-Nasa'i, chapter on balance in ruku', p. 18, no. 1040; Abu Dawud, chapter on the prayer of one who does not straighten his spine in ruku' and sujud, p. 132, no. 863) From this hadith it is understood that in ruku' he should not keep his head level with his buttocks, nor lower it, nor raise it too much. 'لا ينكسه': do not lower it too much. [18] (19) And in ruku' he says 'Subhana Rabbiya al-'Azim' three times, and that is its minimum. Saying 'Subhana Rabbiya al-'Azim' three times at least is sunnah. He may say more, but odd numbers are better. It is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet said: When one of you bows and says in his ruku' 'Subhana Rabbiya al-'Azim' three times, his ruku' is complete, and that is its minimum. (al-Tirmidhi, chapter on tasbih in ruku' and sujud, p. 60, no. 26; Abu Dawud, chapter on what a man says in his ruku' and sujud, p. 134, no. 870)
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on two aspects of ruku' (bowing) in prayer: the correct posture and the recommended tasbih. The author first states that the head should be level with the buttocks (i.e., the back straight and head not raised or lowered excessively). The two hadith from Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi confirm that the Prophet (peace be upon him) placed his hands on his knees and kept his back straight. A separate report emphasizes balance, not raising or lowering the head. The term 'لا ينكسه' is glossed as 'do not lower it too much'. Then the text turns to the tasbih: saying 'Subhana Rabbiya al-'Azim' three times is the minimum Sunnah. The hadith from Ibn Mas'ud states that three times completes the ruku' and that is the least. The commentary adds that reciting more is allowed, but an odd number is recommended. The passage reflects the Hanafi school: these are sunnah acts, not obligatory. The posture is part of the proper form (hay'ah) of ruku'; the tasbih is a sunnah recitation. The hadith proofs are all ahad (single-narrator) but accepted in practice.

Key Terms
رکوع (ruku'): Bowing in prayer with hands on knees and back straight.
سبحان ربی العظيم (Subhana Rabbiya al-'Azim): The tasbih recited in ruku', meaning 'Glory to my Lord, the Magnificent'.
سنت (sunnah): An established practice of the Prophet; its performance is rewarded and its omission is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum number of times to recite 'Subhana Rabbiya al-'Azim' in ruku' according to this passage?
A) One time
B) Three times
C) Seven times
D) It is not specified

Key Takeaway
In ruku', both the straight posture with hands on knees and the threefold tasbih are sunnah mu'akkadah, confirmed by the Prophet's practice.
